Eating Before Eid al-Adha Prayer
Hanafi ruling on the permissibility of eating before Eid al-Adha prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating before the Eid al-Adha prayer and explain why abandoning a mustahabb does not entail karahah.

Core Idea
Abandoning a recommended act does not make its opposite disliked; eating before Eid al-Adha prayer is permissible, not makruh.

In this lesson, we examine a common point of confusion: is it disliked to eat before the Eid al-Adha prayer? The sunnah is to delay eating until after the prayer, but this is only recommended. The passage clarifies that the chosen Hanafi position is that there is no dislike (karahah) in eating beforehand. Understanding this distinction between mustahabb and makruh is essential for proper fiqh application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its sunnah practice
The act in question is eating before the Eid al-Adha prayer. The sunnah is to delay eating until after the prayer, as reported from the Prophet (peace be upon him).
This sunnah applies to those offering the sacrifice, whether in the city or elsewhere.
2
Recognize the level of the sunnah
The sunnah of delaying is classified as mustahabb (recommended), not wajib. Abandoning a mustahabb is not sinful nor disliked in itself.
Mustahabb is a lower category than sunnah mu'akkadah; omitting it is not blameworthy.
3
Understand the legal effect of abandoning mustahabb
The author argues that leaving a mustahabb does not automatically make its opposite makruh. Karahah requires its own specific evidence, which is absent here.
Thus, even if delaying is recommended, eating before is not disliked. The chosen view is no karahah at all.
4
State the final ruling
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that it is permissible to eat before the Eid al-Adha prayer; there is no dislike, not even tanzihi (light dislike).
This is based on the expression in al-Bada'i: 'if he wishes he tastes, if he wishes he does not'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (لكن هنا يؤخر الأكل) للاتباع فيهما وهو مستحب، ولا يلزم من ترك المستحب ثبوت الكراهة إذ لا بد لها من دليل خاص فلذا كان المختار عدم كراهة الأكل قبل الصلاة. وأطلقه فشمل من كان التأخير في حقه، وشمل من في المصر ومن يضحي، وقيل إنه لا يستحب . والظاهر أنه غير صحيح لقول التبيين بعد ولكن يستحب أن يأكل وهو يعطي نفي التنزيه كما لا يخفي . قاله الشيخ إسماعيل فليتأمل والأحسن الاستدلال بما قاله في البدائع : وأما في عيد الأضحى فإن شاء ذاق وإن شاء لم يذق، والأدب أن لا يذوق شيئاً إلى وقت الفراغ من الصلاة حتى يكون تناوله من القرابين ا هـ . فإن هذا التعبير يفيد نفي الكراهة أصلاً، وانظر ما قدمناه في مكروهات الصلاة قبيل
His statement: (But here he delays eating) following the practice in both, and it is recommended. And the abandonment of a recommended action does not entail the establishment of dislikeability, because that requires specific evidence. Hence the chosen view is the absence of dislikeability of eating before the prayer. And he made it absolute, covering those for whom delay is applicable, and covering those who are in the city and those who are sacrificing. It is said that it is not recommended, and the apparent is that it is not correct because of the statement of al-Tabyin afterwards: 'But it is recommended to eat, and that gives negation of tanzih as is not hidden.' Said by Sheikh Ismail, so let it be pondered. The best is to use the proof from what is said in al-Bada'i: 'As for Eid al-Adha, if he wishes he tastes, and if he wishes he does not taste. And the proper conduct is not to taste anything until after finishing the prayer, so that his consumption be from the sacrifices.' End. For this expression indicates the negation of dislikeability entirely. And see what we presented in the chapter on makruhat of prayer earlier.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement on the ruling of eating before the Eid al-Adha prayer. The author clarifies that the sunnah is to delay eating until after the prayer, following the Prophet's practice. However, this is only recommended (mustahabb), not mandatory. Leaving a recommended action does not make the opposite makruh (disliked). Therefore, the chosen position is that eating before the Eid al-Adha prayer is not makruh. Some say it is not recommended, but the author dismisses that. The best evidence from al-Bada'i states that it is permissible to eat or not; the proper conduct is to wait until after the prayer so that the first food is from the sacrificed meat, but not doing so is not disliked.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; doing it is rewarded, not doing it is not sinful or disliked.
كراهة (karahah): Dislikeability; a ruling that abandoning an act is better than doing it, but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, what is the ruling on eating before the Eid al-Adha prayer?
A) It is haram.
B) It is makruh tanzihi.
C) It is not disliked; one may eat or not.
D) It is wajib to eat before the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Abandoning a mustahabb act does not make its opposite makruh; eating before the Eid al-Adha prayer is permissible with no dislike.

Qada of Eid Prayer: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qada for Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada of Eid prayer when missed or invalidated, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Eid prayer's obligation expires with its time; no qada required, but voluntary prayer is recommended.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: if Eid prayer is invalidated after starting or missed entirely, must one make it up? The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say no, drawing analogy with Friday prayer. Abu Yusuf disagrees, likening commencement to a vow. Understanding this difference sharpens your grasp of how obligation and time interact in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its original ruling
Eid prayer is wajib according to Hanafis. But the question here is whether its qada (make-up) is required if the prayer is missed or invalidated. Note the distinction between missing the prayer entirely (fawt) and invalidating it after starting.
2
State the majority Hanafi position
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, if Eid prayer is missed because its time expires (even if one sat for tashahhud), it drops and no qada is required. This is analogous to Friday prayer (al-Jumu'ah).
The Arabic says: 'وإن فسدت بخروج الوقت سقطت ولا يقضيها عندنا كالجمعة'
3
Introduce Abu Yusuf's dissent
Abu Yusuf argues that if one begins the Eid prayer and then invalidates it (e.g., by intentional impurify), qada becomes obligatory because commencement creates a binding obligation similar to a vow (nadhr).
Recorded in al-Muhit: 'إذا أفسدها بعد الشروع يقضي لأن الشروع في الإيجاب كالنذر'
4
Analyze the reasoning behind each view
The majority rely on the time-bound nature of Eid: when the time ends, the obligation lapses completely, like Friday prayer. Abu Yusuf emphasizes the act of starting the prayer, which he analogizes to a vow that must be fulfilled if broken.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah)
The dispute affects what a person does after invalidating a started Eid prayer. Abu Yusuf would require a fresh four-rak'ah prayer as qada; the majority allow (recommend) only a voluntary duha-like prayer, not as qada but for reward.
The text says: 'ولكنه يصلي أربعاً مثل صلاة الضحى إن شاء'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قضاء عليه أصلاً. وقال أبو يوسف : إذا أفسدها بعد الشروع يقضي لأن الشروع في الإيجاب كالنذر. كذا في المحيط . ولا يخفى أنه إذا لم يلزمه القضاء فالإثم عليه لترك الواجب من غير عذر كالسجدة الصلاتية إذا لم يسجد لها حتى فرغ من صلاته. وفي البدائع : وأما حكمها إذا فسدت أو فاتت فكل ما يفسد سائر الصلوات والجمعة يفسدها من خروج الوقت ولو بعد القعود وفوت الجماعة على التفصيل والاختلاف المذكور في الجمعة غير أنها إن فسدت بنحو حدث عمد يستقبلها، وإن فسدت بخروج الوقت سقطت ولا يقضيها عندنا كالجمعة ولكنه يصلي أربعاً مثل صلاة الضحى إن شاء لأنها إذا فاتته لا يمكن تداركها بالقضاء لفقد الشرائط ، فلو صلى مثل الضحي لنيل الثواب كان حسناً وهو مروي عن ابن مسعود.
Qada is not required originally. Abu Yusuf said: If he invalidates it after commencing, he must make it up because commencing obligates it like a vow. Thus in al-Muhit. It is not hidden that if he is not obligated to make it up, he incurs sin for leaving an obligation without excuse, like the prostration of recitation if he does not prostrate until after finishing his prayer. In al-Bada'i: As for its ruling if it becomes invalid or is missed—everything that invalidates other prayers and Friday prayer invalidates it, such as time exiting even after sitting, and missing congregation according to the detail and disagreement mentioned in Friday prayer, except that if it is invalidated by something like intentional impurity, he must redo it; if invalidated by time exiting, it drops and he does not make it up according to us, like Friday prayer, but he may pray four rak'ahs like duha prayer if he wishes, because when it is missed, he cannot make it up due to lack of conditions. So if he prays like duha to attain reward, it is good, and it is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on making up (qada) of Eid prayer if it is invalidated or missed. The author explains the Hanafi position: there is no original obligation of qada for Eid prayer. However, Abu Yusuf holds that if one begins the Eid prayer and then invalidates it, he must make it up because commencing the prayer creates a binding obligation similar to a vow (nadhr). The author notes that even if qada is not required, abandoning the prayer without excuse incurs sin, analogous to leaving the prostration of recitation. From al-Bada'i, it is clarified that the same invalidators that affect other prayers and Friday prayer also invalidate Eid prayer. If invalidation occurs through a deliberate act like breaking wudu, one must start the prayer over. If the time expires, the prayer is dropped without qada, like Friday prayer. Instead, one may pray four rak'ahs voluntarily (like duha) to gain reward, as reported from Ibn Mas'ud.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed or invalidated obligatory act later.
الفوت (al-fawt): Missing the prayer entirely due to time passing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the majority Hanafi position say about a person who invalidates a started Eid prayer due to intentional impurity after the time has expired?
A) He must make up the prayer as qada.
B) He does not make it up; he may pray four rak'ahs voluntarily.
C) He must repeat the prayer immediately if it is still daytime.
D) He is exempt from any prayer because he invalidated it intentionally.

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer, like Friday prayer, drops with time expiry; no qada, but voluntary prayer is recommended.

Delaying Eid al-Fitr Prayer Due to Excuse
Ruling on postponing Eid al-Fitr prayer to the next day due to excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying the Eid prayer and explain the evidence (dalil) and intra-madhhab difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is time-bound; delay is allowed only with excuse and only until noon of the next day.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a practical scenario: when the moon for Eid al-Fitr is not sighted until after noon, can the Eid prayer be delayed to the next day? The text clarifies the default rule (no qada) and the exception based on a hadith, while also noting an internal Hanafi difference. Understanding this ruling helps you apply the principles of time-bound worship and excuse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is the Eid al-Fitr prayer. The default rule is that it is not made up (qada) if missed, because it is a time-bound wajib that expires.
The text says: 'الأصل فيها أن لا تقضى' – the original rule is that it is not made up.
2
Locate the exception and its condition
The exception allows delaying the prayer to the next day, but only if there is a valid excuse (udhr). Furthermore, the delay is limited to noon of the next day. Without excuse, no delay; with excuse, no delay beyond next noon.
The good expression is: 'تؤخر بعذر إلى الزوال من الغد فقط'.
3
Examine the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Anas, where the Prophet delayed the prayer to the next day after a late moon sighting. This shows permissibility of delay with excuse.
The hadith is narrated by al-Tahawi and is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
4
Analyze the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa held that if missed on the first day, it is not made up at all. Abu Yusuf held that it can be delayed to the next day. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Yusuf's, as supported by al-Tahawi and al-Mujtaba.
Al-Tahawi's interpretation: the going out may have been for display, but the majority accept it as a prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وتؤخر بعذر إلى الغد فقط لأن الأصل فيها أن لا تقضى لكن ورد الحديث بتأخيرها إلى الغد للعذر فبقي ما عداه على الأصل فلا تؤخر إلى الغد بغير عذر ولا إلى ما بعده بعذر. ولما قدم أن انتهاء وقته زوال الشمس من اليوم الأول لم يحتج إلى التقييد هنا، فالعبارة الجيدة وتؤخر بعذر إلى الزوال من الغد فقط». ولم يذكر في الكتب المعتبرة اختلاف في هذا، وذكر في المجتبى عن الطحاوي في شرح الآثار أن هذا قول أبي يوسف. وقال أبو حنيفة : إن فاتت في اليوم الأول لم تقض. لأبي يوسف حديث أنس قال: أخبرني عمومتي من الأنصار أن الهلال خفي على الناس في آخر ليلة من شهر رمضان فأصبحوا صياماً فشهدوا عند النبي الله بعد الزوال أنهم رأوا الهلال في الليلة الماضية فأمرهم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بالفطر فأفطروا، وخرج بهم من الغد فصلى جواز النحر وحرمة الصوم وفيما عداه جرينا على الأصل. قال الطحاوي في حديث أنس وليخرجوا لعيدهم من الغد» وليس فيه أنه صلى صلاة العيد بهم فيحتمل أن يكون خروجهم لإظهار سواد المسلمين وإرهاباً لعدوهم اهـ.
His statement: (It is delayed due to excuse only until the next day) because the original rule is that it is not made up, but the hadith came to delay it until the next day for an excuse, so what remains beyond that stays on the original rule. Thus it is not delayed to the next day without excuse, nor beyond the next day with excuse. Since it was already mentioned that its end time is noon of the first day, there was no need for restriction here; so the good expression is: 'It is delayed due to excuse until noon of the next day only.' No difference is mentioned in the reliable books regarding this. In al-Mujtaba, from al-Tahawi in Sharh al-Athar, that this is the saying of Abu Yusuf. Abu Hanifa said: If it is missed on the first day, it is not made up. Abu Yusuf has the hadith of Anas: My uncles from the Ansar told me that the crescent was hidden from the people on the last night of Ramadan, so they began fasting, then they testified before the Prophet (peace be upon him) after noon that they had seen the crescent the previous night, so the Prophet ordered them to break their fast, and they broke it, and he went out with them the next day and prayed. (It indicates) permissibility of slaughtering and prohibition of fasting, but in what remains we follow the original rule. Al-Tahawi said about the hadith of Anas: 'And let them go out for their Eid the next day'; it does not mention that he prayed the Eid prayer with them, so it is possible that their going out was to show the strength of the Muslims and to terrify their enemy.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on delaying the Eid al-Fitr prayer. The default is that Eid prayer is not made up (qada). However, a hadith permits delaying it to the next day if there is a valid excuse (e.g., no news of sighting until after noon). Without excuse, it cannot be delayed, and with excuse, it cannot be delayed beyond the next day. The author notes that the precise formulation is 'delayed due to excuse until noon of the next day only.' There is a disagreement: Abu Yusuf holds that if missed on the first day, it can be prayed the next day (based on the hadith of Anas), while Abu Hanifa says it is not made up at all. The passage discusses the hadith: after a moon-sighting confusion, the Prophet went out with the people the next day to pray. However, al-Tahawi interprets this as possibly just a display of Muslim unity rather than an actual Eid prayer. The Hanafi position follows the majority view that delay is allowed only with excuse and only until the next day.

Key Terms
عذر (udhr): A valid excuse that justifies delaying the Eid prayer, such as lack of moon sighting until after noon.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed prayer after its time; Eid prayer is not subject to qada in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the latest time to which the Eid al-Fitr prayer can be delayed due to an excuse?
A) Midday of the second day
B) The following day until noon
C) Anytime within three days
D) It cannot be delayed at all

Key Takeaway
The Eid prayer can only be delayed to the next day until noon if there is a valid excuse; without excuse, it must be performed in its prime time.

Eating Before Eid al-Adha Prayer: The Hanafi Ruling
Explains that Eid al-Adha rulings mirror Eid al-Fitr except for eating before prayer, and clarifies the absence of karaha.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating before the Eid al-Adha prayer and explain why leaving a mustahabb act does not entail karaha.

Core Idea
Eating before Eid al-Adha prayer is permissible (mubah), but delaying is recommended (mustahabb).

Eid al-Adha shares nearly all rulings with Eid al-Fitr, except for one: when to eat. For Eid al-Fitr, it is mustahabb to eat before prayer; for Eid al-Adha, it is mustahabb to delay eating until after prayer. This might lead some to think eating before prayer is disliked. This lesson unpacks the precise Hanafi ruling and the legal reasoning behind the absence of dislike.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common rulings between the two Eids
The passage begins by stating that all rulings (description, conditions, time, recommended acts) for Eid al-Fitr apply equally to Eid al-Adha because the evidence is the same. Understand this foundational equality.
The exception is the eating before prayer.
2
Examine the exception: eating before prayer
The author then says 'but here he delays eating' – meaning for Eid al-Adha, it is recommended (mustahabb) to delay eating until after the prayer. This is based on the Prophet's practice (ittiba'). Note that the act itself (eating before) is not prohibited.
Mustahabb is a level of recommendation, not obligation.
3
Analyze the legal implication of leaving a mustahabb
The commentator emphasizes that leaving a mustahabb act does not automatically create a ruling of karaha (dislike). Karaha requires specific evidence (dalil khas). Since no such evidence exists for eating before Eid al-Adha prayer, it remains permissible.
This is a key Hanafi principle: the absence of proof for karaha means no karaha.
4
Review the chosen view and its support
The text concludes that the chosen view (al-mukhtar) is 'no karaha' in eating before the prayer – not even tanzihi (light dislike). It quotes al-Bada'i: 'If he wishes he tastes, and if he wishes he does not taste.' The better practice (adab) is to refrain until after prayer, but this is not a ruling of prohibition or dislike.
This is the mufta bihi (operative position) in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وهي أحكام الأضحى) أي الأحكام المذكورة لعيد الفطر ثابتة لعيد الأضحى صفة وشرطاً ووقتاً ومندوباً لاستوائهما دليلاً. واستثنى المصنف رحمه الله من ذلك فقال (لكن هنا يؤخر الأكل) للاتباع فيهما وهو مستحب، ولا يلزم من ترك المستحب ثبوت الكراهة إذ لا بد لها من دليل خاص فلذا كان المختار عدم كراهة الأكل قبل الصلاة. وأطلقه فشمل من كان التأخير في حقه، وشمل من في المصر ومن يضحي، وقيل إنه لا يستحب لهم. قوله: (فلذا كان المختار عدم كراهة الأكل قال في النهر : أي تحريماً ! صحيح لقول التبيين بعد ولكن يستحب أن يأكل وهو يعطي نفي التنزيه كما لا يخفي . قاله الشيخ إسماعيل فليتأمل والأحسن الاستدلال بما قاله في البدائع : وأما في عيد الأضحى فإن شاء ذاق وإن شاء لم يذق، والأدب أن لا يذوق شيئاً إلى وقت الفراغ من الصلاة حتى يكون تناوله من القرابين ا هـ . فإن هذا التعبير يفيد نفي الكراهة أصلاً
His statement: (It is the rulings of al-Adha) meaning the aforementioned rulings for Eid al-Fitr are established for Eid al-Adha in terms of description, condition, time, and recommended acts, due to equality in evidence. The author excepted from that and said (but here he delays eating) following the practice (ittiba') in both, and it is recommended (mustahabb). Leaving a recommended act does not necessitate the establishment of dislike (karaha), as that would require specific evidence, so the chosen view is no karaha for eating before the prayer. He gave it generally, so it includes those for whom delay is appropriate, and includes those in the city and those who sacrifice; it is said it is not recommended for them. His statement: (Therefore the chosen view is no karaha in eating) – al-Nahr said: That is, as a prohibition! Correct according to the statement of al-Tabyin after, but it is mustahabb to eat, and this gives negation of tanzih (dislike), as is not hidden. Sheikh Ismail said: Let it be considered, and better is the istidlal by what is said in al-Bada'i: As for Eid al-Adha, if he wishes he tastes, and if he wishes he does not taste, and the adab is not to taste anything until after finishing the prayer, so that his consumption is from the sacrifices. This expression indicates negation of karaha entirely.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage clarifies that the rulings of Eid al-Adha are identical to those of Eid al-Fitr in all respects (description, conditions, time, recommended acts) because the evidence is common. The exception is regarding eating before the prayer: for Eid al-Fitr, it is mustahabb to eat before the prayer; for Eid al-Adha, it is mustahabb to delay eating until after the prayer, following the practice of the Prophet (PBUH). However, the author points out that leaving a mustahabb act does not create a disliked (makruh) ruling; karaha requires specific evidence. Therefore, the chosen stance is that there is no karaha (neither tahrimi nor tanzihi) in eating before the Eid al-Adha prayer, though it is recommended not to. The text quotes al-Nahr and al-Bada'i to support that the better view is that eating before the prayer is permissible without any dislike, and the etiquette is to refrain until after to eat from the sacrifice.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): An action recommended but not obligatory; leaving it is not sinful.
كراهة (karaha): Dislike; an act that is makruh (either tanzihi or tahrimi).
مختار (mukhtar): The chosen view; the preferred opinion within the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on eating before the Eid al-Adha prayer according to the chosen view in this passage?
A) It is haram (forbidden)
B) It is makruh tanzihi (disliked)
C) It is mustahabb (recommended) to eat
D) It is permissible with no dislike, but delaying is recommended

Key Takeaway
For Eid al-Adha, eating before the prayer is permissible (mubah); delaying until after is recommended (mustahabb) but not obligatory, and there is no dislike (karaha) in eating before.

Sunnah of Reciting Takbir Loudly on the Way to Eid Prayer
Ruling on reciting takbir loudly while walking to Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting takbir loudly on Eid and explain the two narrations regarding when to stop reciting.

Core Idea
Takbir on Eid is sunnah in the road, not the musalla; stop upon arrival or continue until prayer?

When walking to the Eid prayer, it is a confirmed sunnah to recite takbir loudly. But where exactly is this sunnah observed? The classical texts clarify that it is restricted to the road, not the house or the prayer area. There is also a subtle difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars about when to stop reciting once you reach the musalla.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? Reciting takbir (Allahu Akbar) loudly while going to the Eid prayer. What is the hukm level? It is a sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
2
Locate the condition
Where is it sunnah? The text explicitly states it is in the road, not in the house or the musalla. This is a key condition.
The phrase 'ظاهره أنه ليس بمستحب في البيت وفي المصلى' confirms this.
3
Understand the two narrations
Two reports: one from al-Muhit says stop upon reaching the musalla; another says continue until the imam starts the prayer because the time for takbir continues.
The second narration is based on the time of takbir lasting until the prayer begins.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
Al-Bada'i prefers stopping at the musalla, but the common practice ('عمل الناس') is to continue until the prayer starts. The mufta bihi is the latter.
The tarjih authority is al-Bada'i for the first, but the operative fatwa follows practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ويكبر في الطريق جهراً للاتباع أيضاً وظاهره أنه ليس بمستحب في البيت وفي المصلى. وفي المحيط : ويكبر في حال خروجه إلى المصلى جهراً فإذا انتهى إلى المصلى يترك. وفي رواية لا يقطعها مالم يفتتح الإمام الصلاة لأنه وقت التكبير فإنه يكبر عقب الصلاة جهراً ويسن الجهر التكبير إظهاراً للشعائر .اهـ. وجزم في البدائع بالأولى وعمل الناس في المساجد على الرواية الثانية
His statement: (And he recites takbir loudly in the road) following the practice too, and apparently it is not mustahabb in the house or in the musalla. In al-Muhit: He recites takbir when leaving for the musalla loudly; when he reaches the musalla he stops. In another narration: He does not stop until the imam starts the prayer because it is the time of takbir, for he recites takbir after the prayer loudly, and it is sunnah to recite takbir loudly to manifest the rituals. The first is affirmed in al-Bada'i, and people in the mosques act on the second narration.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage discusses the sunnah of reciting takbir (Allahu Akbar) loudly while walking to the Eid prayer ground. The author points out that this is sunnah only in the road, not in the house or at the musalla itself. Two narrations are presented: one from al-Muhit says to stop upon reaching the musalla; another says to continue until the imam starts the prayer, because the time for takbir continues until the prayer. People generally follow the second narration, though al-Bada'i prefers the first.

Key Terms
التكبير (al-takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar'; in this context, the Eid takbir recited on the way to prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) In the house before leaving
B) In the musalla before the prayer
C) In the road on the way to the musalla
D) Both in the house and the road

Key Takeaway
Reciting takbir loudly on the road to Eid prayer is sunnah muakkadah; stop upon arrival or continue until prayer based on differing Hanafi narrations.

Teaching Udhiya and Takbir in the Friday Khutbah
Recommendation for the khatib to teach udhiya and takbir al-tashriq in the Friday khutbah before Eid al-Adha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the recommended content of the Friday khutbah before Eid al-Adha and explain the rationale based on the khutbah's purpose of teaching time-relevant rulings.

Core Idea
The Friday khutbah must teach temporal rulings, especially when ignorance prevails.

This passage from 'Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq' expands on the role of the khatib. It emphasizes that the khutbah is not just for spiritual exhortation but is a vital platform for teaching the community the practical rulings of the season — particularly udhiya and takbir al-tashriq before Eid al-Adha. The author connects this to the broader principle that knowledge is a trust, and the khatib must fulfill it by addressing the community's needs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended act
What does the author say the khatib should do in the Friday khutbah before Eid al-Adha? Locate the specific actions mentioned.
The text explicitly mentions teaching udhiya and takbir al-tashriq.
2
Understand the time-sensitive nature
Why should this teaching happen in the Friday khutbah before Eid? Notice the rationale given: the khutbah is for teaching rulings of the current time, and takbir al-tashriq begins on the day of Arafa.
The khatib must teach before the act begins so the community can act correctly.
3
Extract the general principle
The author extends to teaching prayer rulings in times of ignorance. What underlying principle does this reveal? The khutbah should address the community's need for legal knowledge.
Knowledge is a trust (أمانة) on scholars; they must disseminate it.
4
Apply to contemporary settings
How does this principle apply to your context? Think about rulings that modern communities are ignorant of, such as proper prayer, zakat calculation, or contemporary fiqh issues.
The khatib should prioritize teaching what is most needed and timely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ( ويعلم الأضحية وتكبير التشريق في الخطبة لأنها شرعت لتعليم أحكام الوقت، هكذا ذكروا مع أن تكبير التشريق يحتاج إلى تعليمه قبل يوم عرفة ليتعلموه يوم عرفة فإنه ابتداؤه فينبغي للخطيب أن يعلمهم أحكامه في الجمعة التي قبل عيد الأضحى كما أنه ينبغي له أن يعلمهم أحكام صدقة الفطر في الجمعة التي قبل عيد الفطر ليتعلموها ويخرجوها قبل الخروج إلى المصلى، ولم أره منقولا والعلم أمانة في عنق العلماء ويستفاد من كلامهم أن الخطيب إذا رأى حاجة إلى معرفة بعض الأحكام فإنه يعلمهم إياها في خطبة الجمعة بهم خصوصاً في زماننا من كثرة الجهل وقلة العلم فينبغي أن يعلمهم أحكام الصلاة كما لا يخفي
His statement: (And he teaches udhiya and takbir al-tashriq in the khutbah) because it is established to teach the rulings of the time. Thus they mentioned, although takbir al-tashriq needs to be taught before the day of Arafa so that they learn it on the day of Arafa, as it begins then. So it is proper for the khatib to teach its rulings in the Friday prayer before Eid al-Adha, just as he should teach the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr in the Friday prayer before Eid al-Fitr, so that they learn it and pay it before going out to the musalla. I have not seen this transmitted, but knowledge is a trust on the necks of scholars. It is understood from their words that if the khatib sees a need to know some rulings, he should teach them in the Friday khutbah, especially in our time due to much ignorance and little knowledge; so he should teach them the rulings of prayer, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage discusses the practice of teaching the rulings of udhiya (sacrifice) and takbir al-tashriq (the takbir recited after the fard prayers from the 10th to 13th of Dhul Hijjah) in the Friday khutbah before Eid al-Adha. The author notes that the khutbah is intended to educate the congregation about the rulings of the upcoming time. Since takbir al-tashriq begins on the day of Arafa, the khatib should teach about it in the Friday before that day, so people know it in advance. Similarly, the rulings of sadaqat al-fitr are taught before Eid al-Fitr. Although the author says he hasn't seen this explicitly transmitted, he emphasizes that knowledge is a trust and scholars should fulfill it. Especially in times of widespread ignorance, the khatib should teach essential rulings like those of prayer during the khutbah.

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (takbir al-tashriq): The takbir recited after each fard prayer from the 10th to the 13th of Dhul Hijjah, specifically after the noon prayer on the 10th to after the dawn prayer on the 13th (Hanafi view).
الأضحية (al-udhiya): The animal sacrifice performed on Eid al-Adha and the following three days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it is a fard requirement of the khutbah
B) So that people learn it before the day of Arafa when it begins
C) Because the Prophet specifically commanded it
D) Only if there are new Muslims present

Key Takeaway
The Friday khutbah before Eid al-Adha should include teaching udhiya and takbir al-tashriq to equip the community with necessary rulings, reflecting the khutbah's role as a source of timely religious knowledge.

Delaying Eid al-Adha Prayer and the Meaning of al-Ta'rif
Ruling on postponing Eid al-Adha prayer and clarifying al-Ta'rif

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying Eid al-Adha prayer, distinguish between delay with and without excuse, and explain why al-Ta'rif has no independent ruling.

Core Idea
Eid al-Adha prayer can be delayed up to three days; without excuse it is makruh but still valid.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a nuanced difference between the two Eid prayers. Unlike Eid al-Fitr, the time for Eid al-Adha extends through the days of tashriq, so delaying it without excuse is only disliked, not invalid. The author also dismisses a misconception about 'al-Ta'rif', affirming it is simply the name for standing at Arafat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
The text states that the Eid al-Adha prayer may be delayed for an excuse up to three days. Without excuse, delaying the first day is makruh, but the prayer remains valid within that window.
This is a ruling on the time window, not on the prayer's obligation.
2
Understand the temporal basis
The prayer is connected to the time of sacrifice (udhiyah), which spans three days after Eid. Thus, its time is flexible within that period.
This explains why the ruling differs from Eid al-Fitr.
3
Distinguish from Eid al-Fitr
For Eid al-Fitr, delay without excuse invalidates the prayer; it is not prayed later. Here, the text restricts by 'excuse' to negate karaha, not to define validity.
This is a critical difference: makruh vs. invalid.
4
Apply the restriction 'due to excuse'
When the text says 'delayed due to excuse,' the excuse removes the karaha. Without excuse, the prayer is still valid but disliked. The restriction serves to clarify the degree of karaha, not the act's validity.
In contrast, for Eid al-Fitr, the restriction affects validity itself.
5
Clarify 'al-Ta'rif'
The author asserts that 'al-Ta'rif' is 'not a thing' in the sense of a separate act or ruling. It simply means standing at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah, which is the essential pillar of Hajj (wuquf). No special prayer or additional practice is implied.
This refutes baseless innovations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وتؤخر بعذر إلى ثلاثة أيام لأنها موقتة بوقت الأضحية فتجوز ما دام وقتها باقياً ولا تجوز بعد خروجه لأنها لا تقضى. قيد بالعذر لأن تأخيرها لغير عذر عن اليوم الأول مكروه بخلاف تأخير عيد الفطر لغير عذر فإنه لا يجوز ولا يصلي بعده، فالتقييد بالعذر هنا لنفي الكراهة وفي عيد الفطر للصحة. كذا في أكثر الكتب المعتمدة. وفي المجتبى: وإنما قيده بالعذر لأنه لو تركها في اليوم الأول بغير عذر لم يصلها بعد. في صلاة الجلابي وهو من جملة غرائبه رحمه الله قوله ( والتعريف ليس بشيء) وهو في اللغة الوقوف بعرفات والمراد كذا
His statement: (It is delayed due to excuse for three days) because it is timed with the time of sacrifice, so it is permissible as long as its time remains, and it is not permissible after it exits because it is not made up. It is restricted with 'due to excuse' because delaying it without excuse on the first day is makruh, contrary to delaying Eid al-Fitr without excuse, for that is not permissible and he does not pray afterwards. So the restriction with excuse here is to negate karaha, and in Eid al-Fitr it is for validity. Thus in most reliable books. In al-Mujtaba: It is only restricted due to excuse because if he leaves it on the first day without excuse, he does not pray it afterwards. In Salat al-Jalabi, which is among his rarities. His statement: (And al-Ta'rif is not a thing) – it literally means standing at Arafat, and the intended meaning is such.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage covers two topics. First, the ruling on delaying the Eid al-Adha prayer: it can be delayed due to an excuse for up to three days because the time of Eid al-Adha extends through the days of tashriq (the days of sacrifice). Without excuse, delaying the first day is makruh (disliked), but not invalid; the prayer can still be performed later within the three days. For Eid al-Fitr, delaying without excuse invalidates the prayer altogether, and it is not prayed later. Second, the author clarifies the term 'al-Ta'rif', which literally means standing at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah. The expression 'not a thing' indicates that the ruling attributed to it (perhaps as a special prayer or practice) is baseless.

Key Terms
التعريف (al-ta'rif): The standing at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; the author clarifies it is simply the name of that action, not a separate ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on delaying Eid al-Adha prayer without excuse on the first day?
A) The prayer is invalid and cannot be performed later
B) It is makruh but the prayer can still be performed later within three days
C) It is haram and must be made up later
D) It is permissible and recommended

Key Takeaway
Eid al-Adha prayer can be delayed up to three days with or without excuse; without excuse it is makruh but valid, unlike Eid al-Fitr.

Ruling on Loud Takbir on the Way to 'Eid Prayer
Explains the ruling of saying takbir loudly on the way to 'Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on saying takbir loudly on the way to 'Eid prayer, identify the proof (dalil), and distinguish between the two narrations regarding when to stop.

Core Idea
Saying takbir loudly on the way to 'Eid prayer is sunnah based on following the Prophet and manifesting the rituals.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling of saying takbir loudly (jahr) on the way to the 'Eid prayer. It clarifies that it is sunnah based on following the Prophet (ittiba') and that it is not recommended at home or in the mosque. The text also presents a difference of narration within the Hanafi school regarding when to stop the takbir. We will unpack the ruling, the proof, and the practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is saying takbir aloud on the way to 'Eid prayer. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
The text says 'يكبر في الطريق جهراً' and the commentary classifies it as sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is 'للاتباع أيضاً' (following the Prophet) and 'إظهاراً للشعائر' (manifesting the rituals).
The dalil is from sunnah ahad, as it is based on ittiba'.
3
Distinguish the two narrations
First narration: stop takbir upon reaching the musalla. Second narration: continue until the imam starts the prayer.
The text cites both from al-Muhit and then mentions a preference.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is the second narration (continue until imam starts) based on the practice of people in mosques.
The author states 'وعمل الناس في المساجد على الرواية الثانية'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في الطريق جهراً. وقيده في غاية البيان بأن هذا في حق المصري، أما القروي فإنه يذوق من حين أصبح ولا يمسك كما في عيد الفطر لأن الأضاحي تذبح في القرى من الصباح. قوله (ويكبر في الطريق جهراً للاتباع أيضاً وظاهره أنه ليس بمستحب في البيت وفي المصلى. وفي المحيط : ويكبر في حال خروجه إلى المصلى جهراً فإذا انتهى إلى المصلى يترك. وفي رواية لا يقطعها مالم يفتتح الإمام الصلاة لأنه وقت التكبير فإنه يكبر عقب الصلاة جهراً ويسن الجهر التكبير إظهاراً للشعائر .اهـ. وجزم في البدائع بالأولى وعمل الناس في المساجد على الرواية الثانية.
In the road aloud. And he restricted it in Ghayat al-Bayan that this is for the city dweller; as for the villager, he breaks the fast from the time he rises and does not refrain (from eating) as in 'Eid al-Fitr because sacrifices are slaughtered in villages from the morning. He said (and he says takbir in the road loudly also following (the Prophet) and its apparent meaning is that it is not recommended at home nor in the musalla. In al-Muhit: He says takbir when going out to the musalla loudly, then when he reaches the musalla he stops. And in a narration: He does not stop until the imam begins the prayer because it is the time of takbir, then he says takbir after the prayer loudly, and it is sunnah to say takbir loudly as a manifestation of the rituals. End. And he decided in al-Bada'i' the first opinion, and the practice of people in mosques is upon the second narration.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the manner of saying takbir on the way to 'Eid prayer. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that one says takbir in the road aloud. The commentator first restricts this to the city dweller because the villager (one who lives in a village) breaks his fast at dawn and eats in the morning like 'Eid al-Fitr, as sacrifices are slaughtered early in villages, so they may not recite takbir as much. Then the commentary explains that saying takbir in the road is sunnah based on following the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam). It is not recommended at home or in the mosque. Two narrations are mentioned: one that one continues takbir until reaching the musalla and then stops, and another that one continues until the imam starts the prayer, and after the prayer one says takbir again loudly. The author of al-Hidaya al-Bada'i' preferred the first, but the practice of the people in mosques is on the second. The proof is following the Prophet (sunnah) and the principle of manifesting the rituals.

Key Terms
جهراً (jahran): Aloud, audibly, as opposed to silently.
اتِّبَاع (ittibāʿ): Following the example of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in this passage, when does a person in the city stop saying takbir aloud on the way to 'Eid prayer?
A) At the door of the house
B) When he reaches the musalla
C) When the imam starts the prayer
D) After the prayer in the musalla

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, saying takbir loudly on the way to 'Eid prayer is a sunnah muakkadah, with the mufta bihi being to continue until the imam starts the prayer, and it is not recommended at home or in the mosque.

Delaying 'Eid al-Adha Prayer Due to an Excuse
Ruling on delaying 'Eid al-Adha prayer with proof and contrast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying 'Eid al-Adha prayer and distinguish when it is makruh versus permissible.

Core Idea
Delaying 'Eid al-Adha prayer without excuse is makruh; with excuse, permissible up to three days.

The 'Eid al-Adha prayer is tied to the time of sacrifice. Unlike 'Eid al-Fitr, which cannot be delayed, the Hanafi school permits delaying the 'Eid al-Adha prayer up to three days if there is a valid excuse. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof, and the important contrast between the two 'Eid prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the exact act being ruled upon (delaying 'Eid al-Adha prayer) and the hukm level (makruh without excuse, permissible with excuse).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof that the prayer is timed with the sacrifice (udhiyah), making it valid during the days of tashriq.
The dalil is based on the connection between the prayer and the sacrifice time.
3
Contrast with 'Eid al-Fitr
Understand why the text restricts the ruling with 'excuse' for 'Eid al-Adha (to negate karahah) but for 'Eid al-Fitr it is a condition for validity.
This highlights the different legal natures of the two prayers.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi discussion
Examine the dispute about al-Mujtaba's wording and the author's defense; recognize that the relied-upon view is unambiguous.
The author confirms his quote is accurate and should not be dismissed as a mistake.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Conclude that the operative ruling is: delaying with excuse is permissible, without excuse is makruh, and if missed entirely it is not made up.
This is based on the majority of reliable books.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وتؤخر بعذر إلى ثلاثة أيام لأنها موقتة بوقت الأضحية فتجوز ما دام وقتها باقياً ولا تجوز بعد خروجه لأنها لا تقضى. قيد بالعذر لأن تأخيرها لغير عذر عن اليوم الأول مكروه بخلاف تأخير عيد الفطر لغير عذر فإنه لا يجوز ولا يصلي بعده، فالتقييد بالعذر هنا لنفي الكراهة وفي عيد الفطر للصحة. كذا في أكثر الكتب المعتمدة. وفي المجتبى: وإنما قيده بالعذر لأنه لو تركها في اليوم الأول بغير عذر لم يصلها بعد. في صلاة الجلابي وهو من جملة غرائبه رحمه الله. قوله : فينبغي للخطيب أن يعلمهم الخ) قال في النهر : قدمنا ما يستغنى به عن فارجع إليه، وما قدمه هو قوله في خطبة صلاة الفطر يمكن أن تظهر في حق من أتى بها في العام القابل أو في حق من لم يؤدها قبل الصلاة ا.هـ. ولا يخفى ما فيه فإن من العام إلى العام ينسى العالم فضلاً عن العوام، وظهور الثمرة في حق من لم يؤدها فقط يعيد إذ المقصود تذكير الأحكام للعام على أنه لا يظهر في حق تكبير التشريق خصوصاً مع ما ذكره المؤلف من الذي يستفاد من كلامهم فإنه يؤيد ما قاله، وقد ذكر في الدر المختار في أول باب صدقة الفطر عن الشمني أنه كان عليه الصلاة والسلام يخطب قبل الفطر بيومين يأمر بإخراجها. قوله : (وفي المجتبى وإنما قيده بالعذر الخ) قال في النهر أقول : الذي في المعراج عن المجتبى ما قدمناه يعني من قوله في صلاة الفطر لو أخرها بلا عذر لم يصلها بخلاف عيد الأضحى قال : وهو الموافق لكلامهم، والظاهر أن ما في البحر سهوا قلت : الذي رأيته في المجتبى عين ما ذكره المؤلف فلا ينبغي الحكم عليه بالسهو بدون مراجعة له كما اهـ.
He said (and it is delayed with an excuse up to three days because it is timed with the time of sacrifice, so it is permissible as long as its time remains, and it is not permissible after its exit because it is not made up. It is restricted by the excuse because delaying it without an excuse from the first day is makruh, unlike delaying 'Eid al-Fitr without an excuse, for it is not permissible and one does not pray it after. Thus the restriction with an excuse here is to negate the karahah, and in 'Eid al-Fitr it is for validity. Thus in most reliable books. And in al-Mujtaba: He only restricted it with the excuse because if he left it on the first day without an excuse, he would not pray it after. In the prayer of al-Jilabi, and it is among his rarities, may Allah have mercy on him. He said: 'So it is befitting for the khateeb to teach them...' He said in al-Nahr: We have already presented what suffices, so refer to it. And what he presented is his statement in the sermon of 'Eid al-Fitr: It can appear in regard to one who performs it in the coming year or in regard to one who did not perform it before the prayer. End. And it is not hidden what is in it, for from one year to another the scholar forgets, let alone the common people. And the benefit appears only in regard to the one who did not perform it; the purpose is to remind the rulings to the general public. And it does not appear in regard to takbir al-tashriq particularly with what the author mentioned from their statements, for it supports what he said. And it was mentioned in al-Durr al-Mukhtar at the beginning of the chapter on sadaqat al-fitr from al-Shumnni that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to deliver a sermon two days before al-Fitr commanding its payment. He said: (And in al-Mujtaba: He only restricted it with the excuse...) He said in al-Nahr: I say: What is in al-Mi'raj from al-Mujtaba is what we have presented, meaning his statement concerning the prayer of al-Fitr that if he delayed it without an excuse, he would not pray it, contrary to 'Eid al-Adha. He said: And it is in agreement with their statements, and it is apparent that what is in al-Bahr is a mistake. I said: What I have seen in al-Mujtaba is exactly what the author mentioned, so one should not judge it as a mistake without consulting it. End.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with proof on delaying 'Eid al-Adha prayer due to an excuse. The matn states it can be delayed up to three days with an excuse. The commentary explains that the prayer is tied to the time of sacrifice (udhiyah), so it remains valid as long as that time lasts; after the three days it is not made up. The restriction to excuse is because delaying without excuse from the first day is makruh (disliked). This contrasts with 'Eid al-Fitr prayer, which cannot be delayed at all without excuse; if one misses it, it is not prayed later. Thus, for 'Eid al-Adha, excuse negates karahah, while for 'Eid al-Firt, excuse is for validity (i.e., it is not valid at all after the first day). The author then engages in a scholarly discussion about the khateeb's sermon, quoting from al-Nahr and al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and clarifies a potential misunderstanding regarding al-Mujtaba: the author's quote from al-Mujtaba is correct, and the claim of a mistake in al-Bahr is not valid without verification.

Key Terms
مكروه (makrūh): Disliked but not sinful; here it refers to delaying 'Eid al-Adha prayer without excuse on the first day.
قضاء (qaḍāʾ): Making up a missed act of worship after its time; here 'Eid prayer is not made up (la tuqda).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if someone delays 'Eid al-Adha prayer without an excuse from the first day?
A) It is permissible, but makruh
B) It is invalid and must be made up
C) It is not permissible and cannot be prayed later
D) It is valid but sinful

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits delaying the 'Eid al-Adha prayer up to three days with a valid excuse; without excuse, it is makruh but valid.

Definition and Ruling of Ta'rif (Standing at 'Arafat)
Defines ta'rif and explains that it has no legal effect outside 'Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ta'rif outside 'Arafat and explain why it is not considered valid standing using the analogy of fish blood.

Core Idea
Ta'rif outside 'Arafat is 'not something' in the law—it carries no weight, like the blood of a fish.

The term 'ta'rif' appears in the matn as 'laysa bi shay'' (is not something). This lesson unpacks what that means: it is an act that resembles the valid wuquf but lacks legal significance because it occurs outside the designated place. Through the commentators' explanations and a striking analogy from Imam Muhammad, we will see why the Hanafi school considers it prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi).

Guided Path
1
Define ta'rif linguistically and technically
Start from the literal meaning 'standing at 'Arafat' and note that in this passage it refers to standing outside 'Arafat to resemble the pilgrims.
The shift in meaning is crucial: the act is not the real wuquf.
2
Identify the three interpretations of 'laysa bi shay''
The text mentions three views: (1) it must be avoided (makruh), (2) it has no reward (mubah), (3) it has no legal effect like standing. Compare them.
The third view from Ghayat al-Bayan is the preferred explanation.
3
Analyze the fish blood analogy
Imam Muhammad said fish blood is 'not something' in rulings of blood – it is real blood but legally irrelevant. Similarly, ta'rif is a real action but legally null as standing.
The analogy illustrates that external similarity does not confer validity.
4
Determine the ruling and its basis
The commentator concludes 'wa zahiruhu anna al-karahah tahrimiyyah' – it is prohibitively disliked. The reason: acts of worship specific to a place cannot be performed elsewhere (like tawaf only around Kaaba).
This links to the usul principle of location-specific worship (ibadah mukhtassah bi makan).
5
Apply the same reasoning to the analogous case of sacrificing chicken
The text from al-Dhakhira says sacrificing a rooster in imitation of udhiyah is makruh, as it resembles Magian customs. This confirms that mimicking a ritual in the wrong context is prohibited.
This shows the principle extends beyond hajj to other acts of worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (والتعريف ليس بشيء) وهو في اللغة الوقوف بعرفات والمراد به هنا وقوف الناس يوم عرفة في غير عرفات تشبهاً بالواقفين بها. واختلف في معنى اللفظ؛ ففي فتح القدير أن ظاهره أنه مطلوب الاجتناب فيكون مكروهاً، وفي النهاية ليس بشيء يتعلق به الثواب وهو يصدق على الإباحة، وفي غاية البيان أي ليس بشيء في حكم الوقوف لقول محمد في الأصل دم السمك ليس بشيء في حكم الدماء، وهذا لأنه شيء حقيقة لكونه موجوداً إلا أنه لما لم يكن معتبراً نفى عنه اسم الشيء . وإنما لم يعتبر تعريفهم لأن الوقوف لما كان عبادة مخصوصة بمكان لم يجز فعله إلا في ذلك المكان كالطواف وغيره، تری أنه لا يجوز الطواف حول سائر البيوت تشبهاً بالطواف حول الكعبة اهـ. وظاهره أن الكراهة تحريمية. وفي الذخيرة من كتاب الحظر والإباحة التضحية بالديك أو بالدجاج في أيام الأضحية ممن لا أضحية عليه لعسرته بطريق التشبيه بالمضحين مكروه لأن هذا من رسوم المجوس اهـ.
He said (and al-ta'rif is not something). In language it is standing at 'Arafat. What is meant here is the standing of people on the day of 'Arafah in other than 'Arafat, resembling those who stand there. And they differed on the meaning of the phrase. In Fath al-Qadir, its apparent meaning is that it is required to avoid, so it is makruh. In al-Nihaya, it is not something to which reward is attached, and it is true regarding permissibility. In Ghayat al-Bayan, it is not something in the ruling of standing, based on Muhammad's statement in al-Asl: 'The blood of a fish is not something in the ruling of bloods.' This is because it is something in reality as it exists, but since it is not considered, the name of thing is negated from it. And their ta'rif is not considered because standing, being an act of worship specific to a place, is not permitted except in that place, like tawaf and others. Do you not see that tawaf around other houses resembling tawaf around the Kaaba is not permissible. End. And its apparent meaning is that the karahah is tahrimi. And in al-Dhakhira, from the book of prohibition and permission: sacrificing a rooster or a chicken during the days of sacrifice by one who has no sacrifice due to hardship, by way of resembling those who sacrifice, is makruh because this is from the customs of the Magians. End.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage defines the term ta'rif and rules that it is 'not something' (laysa bi shay'). Ta'rif linguistically means standing at 'Arafat, but here it refers to people standing on the day of 'Arafah outside 'Arafat imitating the pilgrims. The commentary discusses the meaning of 'not something'. Some scholars (Fath al-Qadir) interpret it as requiring avoidance, thus makruh. Others (al-Nihaya) say it has no reward but is permissible. The preferred explanation from Ghayat al-Bayan uses an analogy from Imam Muhammad: the blood of a fish is not considered blood in the rulings of blood (e.g., impurities). Similarly, ta'rif outside 'Arafat is not considered a valid act of worship. The reason is that standing at 'Arafat is a specific location-based worship; performing it elsewhere is like performing tawaf around ordinary houses imitating the Kaaba. This is not permissible. The apparent ruling is that it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). The passage then adds a related ruling from al-Dhakhira: sacrificing a rooster or chicken during the days of sacrifice by someone who cannot afford an udhiyah, if done to resemble those who sacrifice, is makruh because it imitates the practices of the Magians. This is another example of the prohibition of imitating others in acts of worship.

Key Terms
التعريف (al-ta'rīf): Linguistically standing at 'Arafat; here, the act of standing on the day of 'Arafah outside 'Arafat imitating the pilgrims.
مكروه تحريماً (makrūh taḥrīman): Prohibitively disliked; an action that should be avoided as it is close to haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred interpretation in the text, what is the ruling for a person who stands outside 'Arafat on the day of 'Arafah imitating the pilgrims?
A) Permissible and rewarded
B) Makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked)
C) Makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked)
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
Standing outside 'Arafat on 'Arafah day imitating pilgrims is not a valid act of worship; it is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) because it mimics a location-specific ritual in the wrong place.

Takbir al-Tashriq: Timing, Conditions, and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains the ruling of takbir al-tashriq, its timing, and the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of takbir al-tashriq, identify its conditions, and explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding its timing.

Core Idea
Takbir al-tashriq is sunnah after fard prayers in congregation from Fajr of 'Arafah to 'Asr of the 13th, per the Sahibayn.

This lesson examines the ruling on takbir al-tashriq, a sunnah act performed during the days of 'Eid al-Adha. The passage explains its timing, the required conditions, and an intra-Hanafi dispute over whether it extends to the days of tashriq (11th–13th). Understanding this dispute clarifies the operative fatwa position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Takbir al-tashriq is a specific takbir recited after obligatory prayers. According to the Sahibayn, it is sunnah mu'akkadah from Fajr of the 9th of Dhul Hijjah ('Arafah) until 'Asr of the 13th.
The text states 'sunna after Fajr of 'Arafah until the eighth time', which the sharh explains covers up to 'Asr of the 13th.
2
List the conditions for its recitation
The text mentions four conditions: being in a city (misr), performing an obligatory prayer (maktuba), in congregation (jama'a), and the congregation being numerically desirable (mustahabb). These conditions imply that it is not recited by travelers or those praying alone.
These conditions are specific to the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa holds that takbir is not recited on the days of tashriq (11th–13th), only on 'Arafah and Nahr (10th). The Sahibayn maintain it is sunnah throughout, which is the relied-upon position.
The dispute hinges on the interpretation of the term 'takbir al-tashriq' – whether it is a technical name or literal description.
4
Examine the linguistic argument
The author argues that 'takbir al-tashriq' is a proper noun, so it applies to the entire period even if the literal meaning (drying meat) is absent on 'Arafah. The majority of its performance occurs on the days of tashriq, giving them the ruling of the majority.
This reasoning supports the Sahibayn's view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The fatwa relies on the Sahibayn's position: takbir al-tashriq is sunnah after every fard prayer from Fajr of 'Arafah to 'Asr of the 13th for those fulfilling the conditions.
This is the operative ruling in the Hanafi school today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وسن بعد فجر عرفة إلى ثماني مرة الله أكبر إلى آخره بشرط إقامة ومصر ومكتوبة وجماعة مستحبة) بيان لتكبير التشريق والإضافة فيه بيانية أي التكبير الذي هو التشريق فإن التكبير لا يسمى تشريقاً إلا إذا كان بتلك الألفاظ في شيء من الأيام المخصوصة فهو حينئذ متفرع على قول الكل، وبهذا اندفع ما في غاية البيان من أن هذه الإضافة وقعت على قولهما لأنه لا تكبير في أيام التشريق عند أبي حنيفة .اهـ. فإن التكبير في هذا الوقت الخاص يسمى تشريقاً فإذا صار علماً عليه خرج من إفادته معناه الأصلي من تشريق اللحم مع أنه إن روعي هذا المعنى لم يكن متفرعاً على قول أحد لأنهم اتفقوا على تكبير التشريق في يوم عرفة وليس المعنى موجوداً فيه، وما في الحقائق من أنه إنما أضيف إلى التشريق مع أنه يؤتى به في غيرها لما أن أكثره في أيام التشريق وللأكثر حكم الكل يؤول إلى أنه على قولهما كما لا يخفى. وعلى هذا فما في الخلاصة والبدائع من أن أيام النحر ثلاثة وأيام التشريق ثلاثة ويمضي ذلك كله في أربعة أيام العاشر من ذي الحجة للنحر خاصة والثالث عشر للتشريق خاصة واليومان فيما بينهما للنحر والتشريق جميعاً .اهـ. فبيان للواقع من أفعال الناس من أنهم يشرقون اللحم في أيام مخصوصة لا بيان لتكبير التشريق لا تفاقهم على أن اليوم الأول من أيام النحر يكبر فيه . ثم صرح في البدائع بأن التشريق في اللغة كما يطلق على إلقاء لحوم الأضاحي بالمشرقة يطلق
He said (and it is sunnah after Fajr of 'Arafah until the eighth time Allahu Akbar etc., with the condition of residence, city, obligatory prayer, and desirable congregation). Explanation of takbir al-tashriq, and the idafah is explanatory, i.e., the takbir that is tashriq. For takbir is only called tashriq if it is with those words on some of the specific days. So then it is based on the saying of all. And by this is repelled what is in Ghayat al-Bayan that this idafah occurred according to the two (Sahibayn) because there is no takbir on the days of tashriq according to Abu Hanifah. End. For the takbir in this specific time is called tashriq, and when it becomes a technical term, it departs from its original meaning of drying meat. Even if this meaning were considered, it would not be based on anyone's saying, because they agreed on takbir al-tashriq on the day of 'Arafah and the meaning is not present there. And what is in al-Haqa'iq that it is added to tashriq even though it is performed at other times because most of it is on the days of tashriq, and the majority takes the ruling of the whole, leads to it being according to the two (Sahibayn), as is not hidden. Upon this, what is in al-Khulasa and al-Bada'i' that the days of Nahr are three and the days of Tashriq are three, and that passes in four days: the 10th of Dhul Hijjah is for Nahr specifically, the 13th for Tashriq specifically, and the two days between are for both Nahr and Tashriq. End. So it is an explanation of the reality of people's actions that they dry meat on specific days, not an explanation of takbir al-tashriq, because they agreed that the first day of Nahr one says takbir on it. Then he stated clearly in al-Bada'i' that tashriq in language is applied to throwing the meat of sacrifices in the sun to dry.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding takbir al-tashriq. It begins by stating it is sunnah from Fajr of 'Arafah until a certain time (the eighth time, meaning after prayer), with conditions of being in a city (misr), performing obligatory prayer in congregation. The commentary then explains the term 'takbir al-tashriq' and addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that there is no takbir on the days of tashriq (the 11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) consider it sunnah on those days. The author argues that the term 'takbir al-tashriq' is a proper name, so it applies to the takbir recited in this specific period regardless of its literal meaning. This refutes the claim that the addition 'tashriq' supports the Sahibayn's view alone. The author then discusses the classification of days: days of Nahr (sacrifice) are three (10th, 11th, 12th), days of Tashriq are three (11th, 12th, 13th), overlapping in the middle two days. This is descriptive of people's practice of drying meat, not of takbir. The takbir is agreed upon for the first day of Nahr. Finally, he clarifies the linguistic meaning of tashriq as drying meat in the sun.

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (takbīr al-tashrīq): The takbir recited after every fard prayer from Fajr of 'Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah) to 'Asr of the 13th Dhul Hijjah.
أيام التشريق (ayyām al-tashrīq): The 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah, called so because meat is dried (tashriq) in the sun during these days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) After Maghrib on the day of 'Arafah
C) After Fajr on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah
D) After 'Asr on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah

Key Takeaway
Takbir al-tashriq is a sunnah mu'akkadah recited by those in congregation in a city from Fajr of 'Arafah to 'Asr of the 13th, following the Sahibayn's view.

Ruling and Conditions of Takbir al-Tashriq
States ruling, conditions, and evidence for Takbir al-Tashriq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of Takbir al-Tashriq, identify its conditions, and explain the Quranic evidence for its obligation.

Core Idea
Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib, not sunnah — the matn's term is metaphorical.

This lesson examines the ruling of Takbir al-Tashriq, the special takbir recited after fard prayers during the days of Tashriq. Although the matn calls it sunnah, the commentator clarifies that the relied-upon Hanafi position is that it is wajib. We will explore the Quranic evidence, conditions, and the effect of following the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is Takbir al-Tashriq? Note that the matn calls it sunnah, but the commentator states the correct view is wajib.
The term 'sunnah' here is a conventional metaphor for 'wajib'.
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verses cited: Surah al-Baqarah 2:203 and Surah al-Hajj 22:28. Understand that the imperative indicates obligation per Hanafi usul.
The 'numbered days' and 'known days' are interpreted as the days of Tashriq.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'udhkuru' and 'yadhkuru' – in Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-wujub unless there is a qarinah to reduce it. Here, no such qarinah exists, so the command indicates obligation.
The contextual indicator (qarinah) in the author's own words confirms obligation via iqtida'.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa held a shorter time (until Asr of the 10th); the Sahibayn held until end of Tashriq (13th). The matn follows the Sahibayn. Cross-madhhab: Shafi'i considers it sunnah.
The thamarah al-khilaf: sin vs no sin for omission.
5
Evaluate the conditions (shurut)
The conditions for wajib are: residence (muqim), city (misr), fard prayer, congregation (jama'ah). Women and travelers become obligated only if they follow a resident congregation (iqtida').
The athar of Ali (RA) is used to prove the condition of 'misr jami'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسن بعد فجر عرفة إلى آخر أيام التشريق مرة: الله أكبر الله أكبر لا إله إلا الله والله أكبر الله أكبر ولله الحمد، بشرط إقامة ومصر ومكتوبة وجماعة مستحبة. وبالاقتداء يجب على المرأة والمسافر. قوله (وسن بعد فجر عرفة إلى ثماني مرة الله أكبر إلى آخره بشرط إقامة ومصر ومكتوبة وجماعة مستحبة) بيان لتكبير التشريق. ثم سماه في الكتاب سنة تبعاً للكرخي مع أنه واجب على الأصح كما في غاية البيان للأمر في قوله تعالى: (واذكروا الله في أيام معدودات) [البقرة:203] ولقوله تعالى: (ويذكروا اسم الله في أيام معلومات) [الحج:28] على القول بأن كلاً منهما أيام التشريق. ومطلق الأمر للوجوب وإطلاق اسم السنة على الواجب جائز. ولا يخفى أنه مجاز عرفاً فيحتاج إلى قرينة وهي في كلام المصنف قوله بعده: وبالاقتداء يجب على المرأة والمسافر. فصرح بالوجوب بالاقتداء ولولا أنه واجب وجب بالاقتداء. واستدل أبو حنيفة على اشتراط المصر لوجوب التكبير بقول علي: لا جمعة ولا تشريق ولا فطر ولا أضحى إلا في مصر جامع.
And it is sunnah after Fajr of Arafah until the end of the days of Tashriq, once: 'Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illallah, Wallahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar wa lillahil hamd,' with the condition of residence, being in a city, obligatory prayer, and recommended congregation. And by following, it becomes obligatory upon women and travelers. His statement (and it is sunnah after Fajr of Arafah until eight times... so on with the condition of residence and city and obligatory prayer and recommended congregation) is an explanation of the Takbir of Tashriq. Then he called it in the book sunnah following al-Karkhi, while it is obligatory according to the correct view as in Ghayat al-Bayan, due to the command in His statement (And remember Allah during [specific] numbered days) [2:203] and His statement (And mention the name of Allah on known days) [22:28] on the view that both refer to the days of Tashriq. And the absolute command indicates obligation, and applying the term 'sunnah' to what is obligatory is permissible. And it is not hidden that this is a conventional metaphor, so it requires a contextual indicator, which is in the author's statement afterwards: 'And by following, it becomes obligatory upon women and travelers.' So he explicitly states obligation by following, and were it not obligatory, it would not become obligatory by following. And Abu Hanifa argued for the condition of the city for the obligation of takbir by the statement of Ali: 'There is no Friday prayer, no Tashriq, no Fitr, and no Adha except in a comprehensive city.'
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling of Takbir al-Tashriq, the special takbir recited after obligatory prayers during the days of Tashriq (11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul-Hijjah) starting from Fajr of the Day of Arafah (9th Dhul-Hijjah). The author states the text from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: 'It is sunnah after Fajr of Arafah until the end of the days of Tashriq.' The commentator clarifies that despite the author calling it sunnah, the correct position in the Hanafi school is that it is wajib (obligatory). This is based on the Quranic commands in Surah al-Baqarah (2:203) and Surah al-Hajj (22:28), where the absolute imperative indicates obligation. The term 'sunnah' is used metaphorically, but the context of the text—namely that by following (i.e., women and travelers become obligated if they pray with a resident congregation)—shows it is truly wajib. Additionally, Imam Abu Hanifa cites the athar of Sayyiduna Ali that the Takbir of Tashriq is only prescribed in a 'misr jami'' (a major city with a congregational mosque and inhabitants). The conditions for the obligation are: being a resident (muqim), being in a city, praying an obligatory prayer in congregation, and the congregation being recommended (i.e., a congregation that is not obligatory but still holds the ruling). Women and travelers are not originally obligated, but if they pray with such a congregation, they must follow the imam and recite the takbir.

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (Takbir al-Tashriq): The specific takbir recited after fard prayers from Fajr of the Day of Arafah until the end of the days of Tashriq
مصر جامع (Misr Jami'): A major city where Friday prayers are established with a congregational mosque and sufficient inhabitants
اقتداء (Iqtida'): Following the imam in congregational prayer; here means if a woman or traveler prays behind a resident imam in a congregation, they become obligated to recite the takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mutamad (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of Takbir al-Tashriq?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Wajib
C) Mustahab
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib for residents in a city praying obligatory prayers in congregation; women and travelers become obligated by following.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Ruling of Takbir al-Tashreeq: Wajib, Not Sunnah
Explains the ruling of Takbir Tashreeq and its proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position that Takbir al-Tashreeq is wajib, explain the Quranic evidence, and identify the contextual indicator that resolves the author's use of 'sunnah'.

Core Idea
Takbir al-Tashreeq is wajib; the author called it sunnah metaphorically.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the commentator clarifies the ruling of Takbir al-Tashreeq. Although the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq labels it as 'sunnah', the soundest view in the Hanafi school is that it is wajib (obligatory). We'll explore the Quranic evidence and the reasoning behind this classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the recitation of Takbir al-Tashreeq after the obligatory prayers. The matn calls it sunnah, but the sharh clarifies it is wajib on the soundest view.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator cites Quran 2:203 and 22:28, where the imperative 'udhkuru' is taken as a command indicating obligation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, the imperative form amr indicates wujub. The context of 'ayyam ma'dudat' and 'ayyam ma'lumat' is interpreted as the days of Tashreeq.
4
Understand the metaphorical usage
The term 'sunnah' is used metaphorically because every wajib is a good practice. The contextual indicator (qarinah) is found in the text's own statement that following the imam makes it obligatory for women and travelers.

على رفع الصوت بالتكبير . قاله النضير بن شميل. ولذا استدل أبو حنيفة على اشتراط المصر لوجوب التكبير بقول علي : لا جمعة ولا تشريق ولا فطر ولا أضحى إلا في مصر جامع. فحينئذ ظهر أن الإضافة فيه على وقل الكل. ثم سماه في الكتاب سنة تبعاً أنه واجب على الأصح كما في غاية البيان للأمر في قوله تعالى واذكروا الله

في أيام معدودات [البقرة: ۲۰۳] ولقوله تعالى ويذكروا اسم الله في أيام معلومات [ الحج : : ۲۸] على القول بأن كلاً منهما أيام التشريق وقيل المعدودات أيام التشريق والمعلومات أيام العشر . وقيل : المعلومات يوم النحر ويومان بعده والمعدودات أيام التشريق لأنه أمر في المعدودات بالذكر مطلقاً وفي المعلومات الذكر على ما رزقهم من بهيمة الأنعام وهي الذبائح ومطلق الأمر للوجوب وإطلاق اسم السنة على الواجب جائز لأن السنة عبارة عن الطريقة المرضية أو السيرة الحسنة وكل واجب هذا صفته. كذا في البدائع. ولا يخفى أنه مجاز عرفاً فيحتاج إلى قرينة وإلا انصرف إلى المعنى الحقيقي وهي في كلام المصنف قوله بعده وبالاقتداء يجب على المرأة والمسافر . فصرح بالوجوب بالاقتداء ولولا أنه واجب وجب بالاقتداء. وقد يقال: إن الأمر في الآية يفيد الافتراض لأنه قطعي فلا بد له من صارف منه إلى الوجوب، والحق كما قدمنا مراراً أن السنة المؤكدة والواجب متساويان في الرتبة فلذا تارة يصرحون في الشيء بأنه سنة ويصرحون فيه بعينه بأنه واجب لعدم التفاوت في استحقاق الإثم بتركه وبين وقته فأفاد أن أوله عقب فجر يوم عرفة، فالمراد ببعد عقب في
من المسألتين فإن التشبه هنا وإن كان بالمسلمين فهو مكروه كما يفيده كلام المحقق في الفتح وغيره في النهر والحاصل أن ناطقة عباراتهم بترجيح الكراهة وشذوذ غيره قوله : (وقد يقال الخ) يؤخذ جوابه مما قاله في الفتح: اختلف في أن تكبيرات التشريق واجبة في المذهب أو سنة والأكثر على أنها واجبة، ودليل السنة أنهض وهو مواظبته صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم وأما الاستدلال بقوله تعالى الله ويذكروا اسم في أيام معلومات [الحج: ۲۸] فالظاهر منها ذكر اسمه على الذبيحة نسخاً لذكرهم عليها غيره في الجاهلية بدليل على ما رزقهم من بهيمة الأنعام بل قد قيل : إن الذكر كناية نفس الذبح ا هـ . إلا أن يقال مراده أن من استدل بالآية يلزمه القول بالفرضية تأمل قوله : (والحق كما قدمناه مراراً الخ أي الحق في الجواب عن المصنف حيث سماه سنة لا في الجواب عن قوله فقد يقال فكان ينبغي تأخير القيل إلى ما بعد الجواب. هذا وفيما قاله نظر لأن الذي قدمه مراراً أنهما متساويان في أصل الإثم بتركهما لا أنهما في رتبة واحدة بل الإثم فيهما متفاوت، وظاهر كلامه أنهما متحدان فيما صدقا عليه كالإنسان والبشر وليس كذلك يدل عليه ما شاع بينهم وحرروه في كتبهم من ذكر الخلاف في الوتر هل هو سنة أو واجب وترجيحهم قول الإمام بوجوبه فلو كانا متساويين لما ساغ ذلك .
