وهذا عند أبي حنيفة فالتكبير عنده عقب ثماني صلوات فينتهي بالتكبير عقب العصر يوم النحر، وعندهما ينتهي بالتكبير عقب العصر من آخر أيام التشريق وهي ثلاث وعشرون صلاة وهو قول عمر وعلي ورجحاه لأنه الأكثر وهو الأحوط في العبادات. ورجح أبو حنيفة قول ابن مسعود لأن الجهر بالتكبير بدعة فكان الأخذ بالأقل أولى احتياطاً، وقد ذكروا في مسائل السجدات أن ما تردد بين بدعة وواجب فإنه يؤتى به احتياطاً، وما تردد بين بدعة وسنة يترك احتیاطاً كما في المحيط وغيره، وهو يقتضي ترجيح قولهما ولهذا ذكر الأسبيجابي وغيره أن الفتوى على قولهما. وفي الخلاصة : وعليه عمل الناس اليوم. وفي المجتبى : والعمل والفتوى في عامة الأمصار وكافة الأعصار على قولهما. وهذا بناء على أنه إذا اختلف أبو حنيفة وصاحباه فالأصح أن العبرة بقوة الدليل كما في آخر الحاوي القدسي وهو مبني على أن قولهما في كل مسألة مروي عنه أيضاً كما ذكره في الحاوي أيضاً، وإلا فكيف يفتى بغير قول صاحب المذهب! و به اندفع ما ذكره في فتح القدير من ترجيح قوله هنا ورد فتوى المشايخ بقولهما إلا أن يريدوا بالواجب المذكور في باب السجدات الفرض ويلتزم أن ما تردد بين بدعة وواجب اصطلاحي فإنه يترك كالسنة فيترجح قوله، وفي قوله مرة إشارة إلى رد ما نقل عن الشافعي أنه يكرر التكبير ثلاثاً. وقول الله أكبر إلى آخره بيان لألفاظه وهو : الله أكبر الله أكبر لا إله إلا الله، والله أكبر الله أكبر ولله الحمد. وقد ذكر الفقهاء أنه مأثور عن الخليل عليه السلام وأصله أن جبريل عليه السلام لما جاء بالفداء خاف العجلة على إبراهيم فقال : الله أكبر الله أكبر . فلما رآه إبراهيم عليه السلام قال : لا إله إلا الله والله أكبر. فلما علم إسماعيل الفداء قال إسماعيل : الله أكبر ولله الحمد. كذا في غاية البيان. وكثير من الكتب ولم يثبت عند المحدثين كما في فتح القدير، وقد صرحوا بأن الذبيح إسماعيل وفيه اختلاف بين السلف والخلف ؛ فطائفة قالوا به وطائفة قالوا بأنه إسحق والحنفية مائلون إلى الأول، ورجحه الإمام أبو الليث السمرقندي في البستان بأنه أشبه بالكتاب والسنة ، فأما الكتاب فقوله تعالى وفديناه بذبح عظيم ﴾ [الصادفات : ١٠٧] ثم قال بعد قصة الذبح وبشرناه باسحق ) [الصافات : ۱۱۲] الآية . وأما الخبر فما روي عنه عليه السلام «أنا ابن الذبيحين يعني أباه عبد الله وإسماعيل . واتفقت الأمة أنه كان من ولد إسماعيل. وقال أهل التوراة : مكتوب في التوراة أنه كان إسحق فإن صح ذلك فيها آمنا به اهـ. وأما محل أدائه فدبر الصلاة وفورها من غير أن يتخلل ما يقطع حرمة الصلاة حتى لو ضحك قهقهة أو أحدث متعمداً قوله : (ولا خلاف فيه كذا نقله في النهر عن السراج قال : وفيه نظر قوله : (إلا أن يريد بالواجب المذكور الخ) يبعده أنهم ذكروا فيمن شك في الوتر أنها الثانية أو المثالثة أنه يقنت فيهما
Book of Prayer, Chapter of the Two Eid Prayers. And it (the Eid prayer) is written (obligatory) and congregation is recommended, and by following (the imam) it becomes obligatory upon the woman and the traveler. Raising the voice with the takbir. Al-Nadr ibn Shumayl said it. Hence Abu Hanifa inferred the condition of a city (misr) for the obligation of takbir from the saying of Ali: 'There is no Jumu'ah, no Tashreeq, no Fitr, no Adha except in a congregational city.' Then it became apparent that the addition (of the word) therein is upon... Then in the book, he called it Sunnah following that it is obligatory according to the soundest view, as in Ghayat al-Bayan, due to the command in His statement: 'And remember Allah during [specific] numbered days' [2:203] and His statement: 'And they may mention the name of Allah on known days' [22:28] on the view that each refers to the days of Tashreeq, and it is said the numbered days are the days of Tashreeq and the known days are the ten days (of Dhul Hijjah). And it is said: the known days are the Day of Sacrifice and the two days after it, and the numbered days are the days of Tashreeq, because in the numbered days the command is for absolute remembrance, and in the known days the remembrance is upon what He provided them of grazing livestock, i.e., the sacrifices, and an absolute command indicates obligation, and calling the obligatory 'Sunnah' is permissible because Sunnah means the approved way or the good practice, and every obligatory act has this description. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And it is not hidden that it is a metaphorical usage conventionally, so it needs a contextual indicator; otherwise it would be taken in its real meaning, and that indicator is in the author's statement after it: 'and by following it becomes obligatory upon the woman and the traveler.' So he explicitly stated obligation by following, and were it not obligatory, it would not become obligatory by following. And it may be said: The command in the verse indicates obligation because it is definitive, so it must have a diverting factor from that to obligation. The truth, as we have repeatedly stated, is that the emphatic Sunnah and the obligatory are equal in rank, hence sometimes they explicitly call a thing 'Sunnah' and at the same time explicitly call it 'wajib' due to no difference in deserving sin for leaving it... And it indicated that its beginning is after the dawn of the day of Arafah, so what is meant by 'after' is 'immediately after'... From the two issues, for imitation here even if it is of Muslims, it is disliked as indicated by the words of the investigator in al-Fath and others in al-Nahr. The summary is that their statements confirm preference for dislike and the oddity of other than it. His statement: 'It may be said etc.' The answer to it is taken from what he said in al-Fath: 'There is disagreement about whether the takbirs of Tashreeq are obligatory in the madhhab or Sunnah, and the majority hold that they are obligatory, and the proof of Sunnah is stronger, which is his (the Prophet's) constancy upon it.' As for the inference from His statement 'and they may mention the name of Allah on known days', the apparent meaning is the mention of His name upon the sacrifice, abrogating their mention of other than Him upon it in the Jahiliyyah, as evidence by 'upon what He provided them of grazing livestock'. Rather, it has been said that 'remembrance' is a metaphor for the slaughter itself. End. Except that it may be said that his intent is that whoever infers from the verse is compelled to say it is obligatory. Reflect on his statement: 'And the truth as we have repeatedly stated etc.', i.e., the truth in answering the author where he called it Sunnah, not in answering his statement 'it may be said', so it would have been better to delay the 'qil' until after the answer. This, and what he said has some consideration because what he repeatedly stated is that they are equal in the origin of sin for leaving them, not that they are one rank; rather, the sin in them is different. The apparent meaning of his statement is that they are identical in what they apply to, like 'human' and 'mankind', but that is not the case, as indicated by what is well-known among them and recorded in their books of mentioning the disagreement about witr, whether it is Sunnah or wajib, and their preferring the imam's view that it is wajib; if they were equal, that would not be permissible... from his statement: 'and there is no disagreement in it', and the end of his statement indicated by his saying 'to eight', i.e., along with eight prayers, hence he did not say 'eight' (feminine), and it is among the limits that are included in the limit. Thus in al-Musaffa. And this is according to Abu Hanifa: the takbir according to him is after eight prayers, ending with the takbir after Asr on the Day of Sacrifice. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it ends with the takbir after Asr of the last day of Tashreeq, which is twenty-three prayers. This is the view of Umar and Ali, and they preferred it because it is more and is the more cautious in acts of worship. Abu Hanifa preferred the view of Ibn Mas'ud because raising the voice with takbir is an innovation (bid'ah), so taking the lesser (number) is more precautionary. It is mentioned in the issues of prostrations that what is ambiguous between an innovation and an obligatory act is performed precautionarily, and what is ambiguous between an innovation and a Sunnah is left precautionarily, as in al-Muhit and others. And this requires preferring their view, and hence al-Asbijabi and others stated that the fatwa is on their view. In al-Khulasa: 'And upon it is the practice of the people today.' In al-Mujtaba: 'And practice and fatwa in most cities and all ages are upon their view.' This is based on the principle that when Abu Hanifa and his two companions disagree, the correct view is that consideration is given to the strength of the evidence, as in the end of al-Hawi al-Qudsi. And it is based on the fact that their statement in every issue is also narrated from him (Abu Hanifa), as mentioned in al-Hawi as well; otherwise, how could one give a fatwa contrary to the statement of the school's founder? And with this is repelled what is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir of preferring his (Abu Hanifa's) view here and rejecting the fatwa of the mashayikh with their view, unless they mean by 'wajib' mentioned in the chapter of prostrations the 'fard' (obligatory) and adhere that what is ambiguous between an innovation and a terminological wajib is left like a Sunnah, thus his view is preferred. In his statement 'once' there is an indication of rejecting what is transmitted from al-Shafi'i that he repeats the takbir three times. And his saying 'Allahu Akbar' to the end is an explanation of its wording, which is: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, la ilaha illa Allah, wa Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, wa lillahi al-hamd. The jurists have mentioned that it is reported from al-Khalil (Ibrahim), peace be upon him, and its origin is that when Jibril came with the ransom, he feared haste upon Ibrahim, so he said: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar. When Ibrahim saw him, he said: La ilaha illa Allah wa Allahu Akbar. When Isma'il learned of the ransom, he said: Allahu Akbar wa lillahi al-hamd. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan and many books. But it is not confirmed by the muhaddithin, as in Fath al-Qadir. And they explicitly stated that the sacrificed one is Isma'il, but there is disagreement among the predecessors and successors: a group said it is Isma'il and a group said it is Ishaq. The Hanafis incline to the first, and Imam Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi preferred it in al-Bustan because it is more in line with the Book and Sunnah. As for the Book, His statement: 'And We ransomed him with a great sacrifice' [37:107], then after the story of the sacrifice: 'And We gave him glad tidings of Ishaq' [37:112]. As for the hadith, what is narrated from him: 'I am the son of the two sacrificed ones', meaning his father Abdullah and Isma'il. The ummah agrees that he (the Prophet) was from the offspring of Isma'il. The people of the Torah say: It is written in the Torah that it was Ishaq; if that is confirmed in it, we believe in it. End. As for the place of its performance: after the prayer and immediately, without anything intervening that breaks the sanctity of the prayer, to the extent that if someone laughs loudly or intentionally breaks wudu... His statement: 'There is no disagreement in it' is transmitted in al-Nahr from al-Siraj, who said: 'There is consideration in it.' His statement: 'Unless they intend by the wajib mentioned' etc. is far from it because they mentioned concerning one who doubts in witr whether it is the second or third that he performs qunut in both of them.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the rulings of Takbir al-Tashreeq (the additional takbirs recited after the obligatory prayers during the days of Tashreeq — the 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah). The commentator begins by establishing that although the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq called it 'sunnah', the soundest view (al-ashah) is that it is wajib (obligatory). He cites the Quranic commands from Surah al-Baqarah (2:203) and al-Hajj (22:28) as evidence, arguing that a command (amr) indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul. The commentator then explains the metaphorical use of 'sunnah' here, noting that 'sunnah' can mean 'good practice' and that every wajib is a good practice, so the term can be applied. However, he stresses the need for a contextual indicator (qarinah) to shift from the literal meaning of 'sunnah' (which is not obligatory) to the intended meaning of 'wajib'. He finds that indicator in the author's statement that following the imam makes the takbir obligatory upon women and travelers — something that would only be said of an act that is itself obligatory. The passage then delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of prayers after which the takbir is recited. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is recited after 8 prayers: from the Fajr of the Day of Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah) to the Asr of the Day of Sacrifice (10th). According to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is recited after 23 prayers: from the Fajr of the Day of Arafah to the Asr of the last day of Tashreeq (13th). This view is attributed to Umar and Ali, and is considered more cautious (ahwat). The commentator notes that the later fatwa and practice are on the view of the Sahibayn, despite the principle that when Imam Abu Hanifa differs, strength of evidence should prevail. The explanation given is that the disciples' view is also transmitted from Abu Hanifa himself in other narrations, and that the majority of scholars have followed it. Finally, the passage presents the specific wording of the takbir and a story about its origin from Prophet Ibrahim and his son Isma'il, though it notes that this story is not confirmed by hadith scholars. The digression about which son was the intended sacrifice (Isma'il vs. Ishaq) shows the Hanafi leaning towards Isma'il, supported by Quranic evidence and a hadith.

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (takbīr al-tashrīq): The extra takbirs (saying 'Allahu Akbar') recited after the obligatory prayers during the days of Tashreeq (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah), starting after Fajr of the Day of Arafah.
مصر جامع (miṣr jāmiʿ): A large city or town where congregational Friday prayers are held; a condition for the obligation of takbir according to Abu Hanifa, as derived from the saying of Ali.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi position regarding the ruling of Takbir al-Tashreeq?
A) It is sunnah.
B) It is wajib.
C) It is fard.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
Takbir al-Tashreeq is wajib, not sunnah; the term 'sunnah' in the matn is a metaphorical usage with a clear contextual indicator.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Dispute on the Number of Prayers for Takbir al-Tashreeq: 8 vs 23
Explains the intra-Hanafi dispute on the number of prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples regarding the number of prayers after which Takbir al-Tashreeq is recited, state the proof for each, and identify the relied-upon fatwa.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa said 8 prayers; Sahibayn said 23; the fatwa follows Sahibayn.

The same passage now addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute about the duration of Takbir al-Tashreeq. Imam Abu Hanifa, based on a statement of Ibn Mas'ud, held it is recited after 8 prayers. His two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, based on statements of Umar and Ali, held it is recited after 23 prayers. The later fatwa and practice have adopted the view of the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa: 8 prayers, ending with Asr of the Day of Sacrifice. Sahibayn: 23 prayers, ending with Asr of the last day of Tashreeq.
2
Identify the proof for each
Abu Hanifa relied on Ibn Mas'ud's statement that takbir is an innovation, so the lesser number is precautionary. Sahibayn relied on statements of Umar and Ali, and considered the greater number more cautious.
3
Analyze the principle of precaution
The principle in 'masa'il al-sajadat' is that if something is ambiguous between a bid'ah and a wajib, it is performed; if between a bid'ah and a sunnah, it is left. Sahibayn's view is to perform more, which is precautionary.
4
Determine the tarjih
The fatwa is on Sahibayn's view because their evidence is stronger and also transmitted from Abu Hanifa himself. This is the practice of the people in most cities and ages.

كتاب الصلاة باب صلاة العيدين
ومكتوبة وجماعة مستحبة وبالاقتداء يجب على المرأة والمسافر .
على رفع الصوت بالتكبير . قاله النضير بن شميل. ولذا استدل أبو حنيفة على اشتراط المصر لوجوب التكبير بقول علي : لا جمعة ولا تشريق ولا فطر ولا أضحى إلا في مصر جامع. فحينئذ ظهر أن الإضافة فيه على وقل الكل. ثم سماه في الكتاب سنة تبعاً أنه واجب على الأصح كما في غاية البيان للأمر في قوله تعالى واذكروا الله
للكرخي مع
في أيام معدودات [البقرة: ۲۰۳] ولقوله تعالى ويذكروا اسم الله في أيام معلومات [ الحج : : ۲۸] على القول بأن كلاً منهما أيام التشريق وقيل المعدودات أيام التشريق والمعلومات أيام العشر . وقيل : المعلومات يوم النحر ويومان بعده والمعدودات أيام التشريق لأنه أمر في المعدودات بالذكر مطلقاً وفي المعلومات الذكر على ما رزقهم من بهيمة الأنعام وهي الذبائح ومطلق الأمر للوجوب وإطلاق اسم السنة على الواجب جائز لأن السنة عبارة عن الطريقة المرضية أو السيرة الحسنة وكل واجب هذا صفته. كذا في البدائع. ولا يخفى أنه مجاز عرفاً فيحتاج إلى قرينة وإلا انصرف إلى المعنى الحقيقي وهي في كلام المصنف قوله بعده وبالاقتداء يجب على المرأة والمسافر . فصرح بالوجوب بالاقتداء ولولا أنه واجب وجب بالاقتداء. وقد يقال: إن الأمر في الآية يفيد الافتراض لأنه قطعي فلا بد له من صارف منه إلى الوجوب، والحق كما قدمنا مراراً أن السنة المؤكدة والواجب متساويان في الرتبة فلذا تارة يصرحون في الشيء بأنه سنة ويصرحون فيه بعينه بأنه واجب لعدم التفاوت في استحقاق الإثم بتركه وبين وقته فأفاد أن أوله عقب فجر يوم عرفة، فالمراد ببعد عقب في
من المسألتين فإن التشبه هنا وإن كان بالمسلمين فهو مكروه كما يفيده كلام المحقق في الفتح وغيره في النهر والحاصل أن ناطقة عباراتهم بترجيح الكراهة وشذوذ غيره قوله : (وقد يقال الخ) يؤخذ جوابه مما قاله في الفتح: اختلف في أن تكبيرات التشريق واجبة في المذهب أو سنة والأكثر على أنها واجبة، ودليل السنة أنهض وهو مواظبته صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم وأما الاستدلال بقوله تعالى الله ويذكروا اسم في أيام معلومات [الحج: ۲۸] فالظاهر منها ذكر اسمه على الذبيحة نسخاً لذكرهم عليها غيره في الجاهلية بدليل على ما رزقهم من بهيمة الأنعام بل قد قيل : إن الذكر كناية نفس الذبح ا هـ . إلا أن يقال مراده أن من استدل بالآية يلزمه القول بالفرضية تأمل قوله : (والحق كما قدمناه مراراً الخ أي الحق في الجواب عن المصنف حيث سماه سنة لا في الجواب عن قوله فقد يقال فكان ينبغي تأخير القيل إلى ما بعد الجواب. هذا وفيما قاله نظر لأن الذي قدمه مراراً أنهما متساويان في أصل الإثم بتركهما لا أنهما في رتبة واحدة بل الإثم فيهما متفاوت، وظاهر كلامه أنهما متحدان فيما صدقا عليه كالإنسان والبشر وليس كذلك يدل عليه ما شاع بينهم وحرروه في كتبهم من ذكر الخلاف في الوتر هل هو سنة أو واجب وترجيحهم قول الإمام بوجوبه فلو كانا متساويين لما ساغ ذلك .
عن
عبارته ولا خلاف فيه وأفاد آخره بقوله إلى ثمان» أي مع ثماني صلوات فلذا لم يقل ثمانية وهي من الغايات التي تدخل في المغيا. كذا في المصفي .
•
وهذا عند أبي حنيفة فالتكبير عنده عقب ثماني صلوات فينتهي بالتكبير عقب العصر يوم النحر، وعندهما ينتهي بالتكبير عقب العصر من آخر أيام التشريق وهي ثلاث وعشرون صلاة وهو قول عمر وعلي ورجحاه لأنه الأكثر وهو الأحوط في العبادات. ورجح أبو حنيفة قول ابن مسعود لأن الجهر بالتكبير بدعة فكان الأخذ بالأقل أولى احتياطاً، وقد ذكروا في مسائل السجدات أن ما تردد بين بدعة وواجب فإنه يؤتى به احتياطاً، وما تردد بين بدعة وسنة يترك احتیاطاً كما في المحيط وغيره، وهو يقتضي ترجيح قولهما ولهذا ذكر الأسبيجابي وغيره أن الفتوى على قولهما. وفي الخلاصة : وعليه عمل الناس اليوم. وفي المجتبى : والعمل والفتوى في عامة الأمصار وكافة الأعصار على قولهما. وهذا بناء على أنه إذا اختلف أبو حنيفة وصاحباه فالأصح أن العبرة بقوة الدليل كما في آخر الحاوي القدسي وهو مبني على أن قولهما في كل مسألة مروي عنه أيضاً كما ذكره في الحاوي أيضاً، وإلا فكيف يفتى بغير قول صاحب المذهب! و به اندفع ما ذكره في فتح القدير من ترجيح قوله هنا ورد فتوى المشايخ بقولهما إلا أن يريدوا بالواجب المذكور في باب السجدات الفرض ويلتزم أن ما تردد بين بدعة وواجب اصطلاحي فإنه يترك كالسنة فيترجح قوله، وفي قوله مرة إشارة إلى رد ما نقل عن الشافعي أنه يكرر التكبير ثلاثاً. وقول الله أكبر إلى آخره بيان لألفاظه وهو : الله أكبر الله أكبر لا إله إلا الله، والله أكبر الله أكبر ولله الحمد. وقد ذكر الفقهاء أنه مأثور عن الخليل عليه السلام وأصله أن جبريل عليه السلام لما جاء بالفداء خاف العجلة على إبراهيم فقال : الله أكبر الله أكبر . فلما رآه إبراهيم عليه السلام قال : لا إله إلا الله والله أكبر. فلما علم إسماعيل الفداء قال إسماعيل : الله أكبر ولله الحمد. كذا في غاية البيان. وكثير من الكتب ولم يثبت عند المحدثين كما في فتح القدير، وقد صرحوا بأن الذبيح إسماعيل وفيه اختلاف بين السلف والخلف ؛ فطائفة قالوا به وطائفة قالوا بأنه إسحق والحنفية مائلون إلى الأول، ورجحه الإمام أبو الليث السمرقندي في البستان بأنه أشبه بالكتاب والسنة ، فأما الكتاب فقوله تعالى وفديناه بذبح عظيم ﴾ [الصادفات : ١٠٧] ثم قال بعد قصة الذبح وبشرناه باسحق ) [الصافات : ۱۱۲] الآية . وأما الخبر فما روي عنه عليه السلام «أنا ابن الذبيحين يعني أباه عبد الله وإسماعيل . واتفقت الأمة أنه كان من ولد إسماعيل. وقال أهل التوراة : مكتوب في التوراة أنه كان إسحق فإن صح ذلك فيها آمنا به اهـ. وأما محل أدائه فدبر الصلاة وفورها من غير أن يتخلل ما يقطع حرمة الصلاة حتى لو ضحك قهقهة أو أحدث متعمداً قوله : (ولا خلاف فيه كذا نقله في النهر عن السراج قال : وفيه نظر قوله : (إلا أن يريد بالواجب المذكور الخ) يبعده أنهم ذكروا فيمن شك في الوتر أنها الثانية أو المثالثة أنه يقنت فيهما
Book of Prayer, Chapter of the Two Eid Prayers. And it (the Eid prayer) is written (obligatory) and congregation is recommended, and by following (the imam) it becomes obligatory upon the woman and the traveler. Raising the voice with the takbir. Al-Nadr ibn Shumayl said it. Hence Abu Hanifa inferred the condition of a city (misr) for the obligation of takbir from the saying of Ali: 'There is no Jumu'ah, no Tashreeq, no Fitr, no Adha except in a congregational city.' Then it became apparent that the addition (of the word) therein is upon... Then in the book, he called it Sunnah following that it is obligatory according to the soundest view, as in Ghayat al-Bayan, due to the command in His statement: 'And remember Allah during [specific] numbered days' [2:203] and His statement: 'And they may mention the name of Allah on known days' [22:28] on the view that each refers to the days of Tashreeq, and it is said the numbered days are the days of Tashreeq and the known days are the ten days (of Dhul Hijjah). And it is said: the known days are the Day of Sacrifice and the two days after it, and the numbered days are the days of Tashreeq, because in the numbered days the command is for absolute remembrance, and in the known days the remembrance is upon what He provided them of grazing livestock, i.e., the sacrifices, and an absolute command indicates obligation, and calling the obligatory 'Sunnah' is permissible because Sunnah means the approved way or the good practice, and every obligatory act has this description. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And it is not hidden that it is a metaphorical usage conventionally, so it needs a contextual indicator; otherwise it would be taken in its real meaning, and that indicator is in the author's statement after it: 'and by following it becomes obligatory upon the woman and the traveler.' So he explicitly stated obligation by following, and were it not obligatory, it would not become obligatory by following. And it may be said: The command in the verse indicates obligation because it is definitive, so it must have a diverting factor from that to obligation. The truth, as we have repeatedly stated, is that the emphatic Sunnah and the obligatory are equal in rank, hence sometimes they explicitly call a thing 'Sunnah' and at the same time explicitly call it 'wajib' due to no difference in deserving sin for leaving it... And it indicated that its beginning is after the dawn of the day of Arafah, so what is meant by 'after' is 'immediately after'... From the two issues, for imitation here even if it is of Muslims, it is disliked as indicated by the words of the investigator in al-Fath and others in al-Nahr. The summary is that their statements confirm preference for dislike and the oddity of other than it. His statement: 'It may be said etc.' The answer to it is taken from what he said in al-Fath: 'There is disagreement about whether the takbirs of Tashreeq are obligatory in the madhhab or Sunnah, and the majority hold that they are obligatory, and the proof of Sunnah is stronger, which is his (the Prophet's) constancy upon it.' As for the inference from His statement 'and they may mention the name of Allah on known days', the apparent meaning is the mention of His name upon the sacrifice, abrogating their mention of other than Him upon it in the Jahiliyyah, as evidence by 'upon what He provided them of grazing livestock'. Rather, it has been said that 'remembrance' is a metaphor for the slaughter itself. End. Except that it may be said that his intent is that whoever infers from the verse is compelled to say it is obligatory. Reflect on his statement: 'And the truth as we have repeatedly stated etc.', i.e., the truth in answering the author where he called it Sunnah, not in answering his statement 'it may be said', so it would have been better to delay the 'qil' until after the answer. This, and what he said has some consideration because what he repeatedly stated is that they are equal in the origin of sin for leaving them, not that they are one rank; rather, the sin in them is different. The apparent meaning of his statement is that they are identical in what they apply to, like 'human' and 'mankind', but that is not the case, as indicated by what is well-known among them and recorded in their books of mentioning the disagreement about witr, whether it is Sunnah or wajib, and their preferring the imam's view that it is wajib; if they were equal, that would not be permissible... from his statement: 'and there is no disagreement in it', and the end of his statement indicated by his saying 'to eight', i.e., along with eight prayers, hence he did not say 'eight' (feminine), and it is among the limits that are included in the limit. Thus in al-Musaffa. And this is according to Abu Hanifa: the takbir according to him is after eight prayers, ending with the takbir after Asr on the Day of Sacrifice. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it ends with the takbir after Asr of the last day of Tashreeq, which is twenty-three prayers. This is the view of Umar and Ali, and they preferred it because it is more and is the more cautious in acts of worship. Abu Hanifa preferred the view of Ibn Mas'ud because raising the voice with takbir is an innovation (bid'ah), so taking the lesser (number) is more precautionary. It is mentioned in the issues of prostrations that what is ambiguous between an innovation and an obligatory act is performed precautionarily, and what is ambiguous between an innovation and a Sunnah is left precautionarily, as in al-Muhit and others. And this requires preferring their view, and hence al-Asbijabi and others stated that the fatwa is on their view. In al-Khulasa: 'And upon it is the practice of the people today.' In al-Mujtaba: 'And practice and fatwa in most cities and all ages are upon their view.' This is based on the principle that when Abu Hanifa and his two companions disagree, the correct view is that consideration is given to the strength of the evidence, as in the end of al-Hawi al-Qudsi. And it is based on the fact that their statement in every issue is also narrated from him (Abu Hanifa), as mentioned in al-Hawi as well; otherwise, how could one give a fatwa contrary to the statement of the school's founder? And with this is repelled what is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir of preferring his (Abu Hanifa's) view here and rejecting the fatwa of the mashayikh with their view, unless they mean by 'wajib' mentioned in the chapter of prostrations the 'fard' (obligatory) and adhere that what is ambiguous between an innovation and a terminological wajib is left like a Sunnah, thus his view is preferred. In his statement 'once' there is an indication of rejecting what is transmitted from al-Shafi'i that he repeats the takbir three times. And his saying 'Allahu Akbar' to the end is an explanation of its wording, which is: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, la ilaha illa Allah, wa Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, wa lillahi al-hamd. The jurists have mentioned that it is reported from al-Khalil (Ibrahim), peace be upon him, and its origin is that when Jibril came with the ransom, he feared haste upon Ibrahim, so he said: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar. When Ibrahim saw him, he said: La ilaha illa Allah wa Allahu Akbar. When Isma'il learned of the ransom, he said: Allahu Akbar wa lillahi al-hamd. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan and many books. But it is not confirmed by the muhaddithin, as in Fath al-Qadir. And they explicitly stated that the sacrificed one is Isma'il, but there is disagreement among the predecessors and successors: a group said it is Isma'il and a group said it is Ishaq. The Hanafis incline to the first, and Imam Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi preferred it in al-Bustan because it is more in line with the Book and Sunnah. As for the Book, His statement: 'And We ransomed him with a great sacrifice' [37:107], then after the story of the sacrifice: 'And We gave him glad tidings of Ishaq' [37:112]. As for the hadith, what is narrated from him: 'I am the son of the two sacrificed ones', meaning his father Abdullah and Isma'il. The ummah agrees that he (the Prophet) was from the offspring of Isma'il. The people of the Torah say: It is written in the Torah that it was Ishaq; if that is confirmed in it, we believe in it. End. As for the place of its performance: after the prayer and immediately, without anything intervening that breaks the sanctity of the prayer, to the extent that if someone laughs loudly or intentionally breaks wudu... His statement: 'There is no disagreement in it' is transmitted in al-Nahr from al-Siraj, who said: 'There is consideration in it.' His statement: 'Unless they intend by the wajib mentioned' etc. is far from it because they mentioned concerning one who doubts in witr whether it is the second or third that he performs qunut in both of them.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the rulings of Takbir al-Tashreeq (the additional takbirs recited after the obligatory prayers during the days of Tashreeq — the 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah). The commentator begins by establishing that although the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq called it 'sunnah', the soundest view (al-ashah) is that it is wajib (obligatory). He cites the Quranic commands from Surah al-Baqarah (2:203) and al-Hajj (22:28) as evidence, arguing that a command (amr) indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul. The commentator then explains the metaphorical use of 'sunnah' here, noting that 'sunnah' can mean 'good practice' and that every wajib is a good practice, so the term can be applied. However, he stresses the need for a contextual indicator (qarinah) to shift from the literal meaning of 'sunnah' (which is not obligatory) to the intended meaning of 'wajib'. He finds that indicator in the author's statement that following the imam makes the takbir obligatory upon women and travelers — something that would only be said of an act that is itself obligatory. The passage then delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of prayers after which the takbir is recited. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is recited after 8 prayers: from the Fajr of the Day of Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah) to the Asr of the Day of Sacrifice (10th). According to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is recited after 23 prayers: from the Fajr of the Day of Arafah to the Asr of the last day of Tashreeq (13th). This view is attributed to Umar and Ali, and is considered more cautious (ahwat). The commentator notes that the later fatwa and practice are on the view of the Sahibayn, despite the principle that when Imam Abu Hanifa differs, strength of evidence should prevail. The explanation given is that the disciples' view is also transmitted from Abu Hanifa himself in other narrations, and that the majority of scholars have followed it. Finally, the passage presents the specific wording of the takbir and a story about its origin from Prophet Ibrahim and his son Isma'il, though it notes that this story is not confirmed by hadith scholars. The digression about which son was the intended sacrifice (Isma'il vs. Ishaq) shows the Hanafi leaning towards Isma'il, supported by Quranic evidence and a hadith.

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (takbīr al-tashrīq): The extra takbirs recited after obligatory prayers during the days of Tashreeq.
مسائل السجدات (masāʾil al-sajadāt): A set of rules in Hanafi fiqh regarding cases where an act is ambiguous between a bid'ah and a wajib or sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, how many prayers after which Takbir al-Tashreeq is recited?
A) 8 prayers
B) 23 prayers
C) 15 prayers
D) 20 prayers

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi is 23 prayers, following the Sahibayn, despite Abu Hanifa's view of 8.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Dispute on Number of Prayers for Takbir al-Tashriq
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the count of prayers for takbir al-tashriq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the number of prayers for takbir al-tashriq, and explain the basis for the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa held 8 prayers; Sahibayn held 23; fatwa follows Sahibayn as a precaution.

Takbir al-tashriq is a sunnah mu'akkadah recited after obligatory prayers during the days of Tashriq. However, within the Hanafi school, there is an important intra-madhhab dispute on exactly how many prayers after which it is recited. This lesson unpacks the arguments of Abu Hanifa and his two companions, and explains why later authorities ruled in favor of the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
From the passage, extract the exact numbers: Abu Hanifa says after 8 prayers (ending Asr of Nahr), Sahibayn say after 23 prayers (ending Asr of last Tashriq day).
The 8 prayers are from Fajr of Arafah to Asr of the 10th; the 23 include all five daily prayers from Fajr of the 9th to Asr of the 13th.
2
Understand the proofs (dalil) for each
Abu Hanifa relies on Ibn Mas'ud's practice and the principle of avoiding innovation by limiting the number. Sahibayn rely on Umar and Ali's practice and the principle of caution in worship by extending it.
Both sides use precaution but with different orientations.
3
Apply the precautionary principle from the prostration chapter
The passage cites a rule: when uncertain between innovation and wajib, perform it; when between innovation and sunnah, leave it. Sahibayn's view is considered closer to wajib (since takbir is sunnah mu'akkadah, almost wajib), so their 23 prayer count is preferred.
This rule tips the scale toward Sahibayn.
4
Analyze the tarjih (preference) mechanism
Later authorities like al-Asbijabi, al-Khulasa, and al-Mujtaba state that fatwa is on Sahibayn's view because the strength of evidence supports it, and because their opinions are also narrated from Abu Hanifa himself.
The passage refutes Fath al-Qadir's objection by clarifying terminology.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon position is the Sahibayn's: 23 prayers. This is the practice of the people in all regions and ages.
A Hanafi mufti today will advise takbir after every fard prayer from Fajr of Arafah to Asr of the 13th.

كتاب الصلاة باب صلاة العيدين عبارته ولا خلاف فيه وأفاد آخره بقوله إلى ثمان» أي مع ثماني صلوات فلذا لم يقل ثمانية وهي من الغايات التي تدخل في المغيا. كذا في المصفي. وهذا عند أبي حنيفة فالتكبير عنده عقب ثماني صلوات فينتهي بالتكبير عقب العصر يوم النحر، وعندهما ينتهي بالتكبير عقب العصر من آخر أيام التشريق وهي ثلاث وعشرون صلاة وهو قول عمر وعلي ورجحاه لأنه الأكثر وهو الأحوط في العبادات. ورجح أبو حنيفة قول ابن مسعود لأن الجهر بالتكبير بدعة فكان الأخذ بالأقل أولى احتياطاً، وقد ذكروا في مسائل السجدات أن ما تردد بين بدعة وواجب فإنه يؤتى به احتياطاً، وما تردد بين بدعة وسنة يترك احتياطاً كما في المحيط وغيره، وهو يقتضي ترجيح قولهما ولهذا ذكر الأسبيجابي وغيره أن الفتوى على قولهما. وفي الخلاصة: وعليه عمل الناس اليوم. وفي المجتبى: والعمل والفتوى في عامة الأمصار وكافة الأعصار على قولهما. وهذا بناء على أنه إذا اختلف أبو حنيفة وصاحباه فالأصح أن العبرة بقوة الدليل كما في آخر الحاوي القدسي وهو مبني على أن قولهما في كل مسألة مروي عنه أيضاً كما ذكره في الحاوي أيضاً، وإلا فكيف يفتى بغير قول صاحب المذهب! وبه اندفع ما ذكره في فتح القدير من ترجيح قوله هنا ورد فتوى المشايخ بقولهما إلا أن يريدوا بالواجب المذكور في باب السجدات الفرض ويلتزم أن ما تردد بين بدعة وواجب اصطلاحي فإنه يترك كالسنة فيترجح قوله
The book of prayer, chapter on the two Eid prayers. His statement: 'And there is no disagreement in it, and its end benefited by his saying 'up to eight,' meaning with eight prayers, so he did not say eight (masculine) because they are among the goals that are included in the goal.' So in al-Masfi. And this is according to Abu Hanifa: the takbir according to him is after eight prayers, so it ends with the takbir after Asr on the day of Nahr. According to them (the two companions), it ends with the takbir after Asr on the last day of Tashriq, which is twenty-three prayers. This is the saying of Umar and Ali, and they preferred it because it is more and it is the more precautionary in acts of worship. Abu Hanifa preferred the saying of Ibn Mas'ud because raising the voice in takbir is an innovation, so taking the lesser number is more appropriate as a precaution. They mentioned in the matters of prostrations that what is uncertain between innovation and obligatory is performed as a precaution, and what is uncertain between innovation and sunnah is left as a precaution, as in al-Muhit and others. This implies the preference of their saying, and therefore al-Asbijabi and others said that the fatwa is on their saying. In al-Khulasa: 'And the practice of people today is upon it.' In al-Mujtaba: 'And practice and fatwa in all regions and all ages are upon their saying.' This is based on the principle that if Abu Hanifa and his two companions differ, the soundest view is that consideration is given to the strength of the evidence, as in the end of al-Hawi al-Qudsi. This is based on the fact that their saying in every issue is also narrated from him, as mentioned in al-Hawi; otherwise, how can one give fatwa contrary to the saying of the founder of the school! And with this is refuted what was mentioned in Fath al-Qadir of preferring his saying here and rejecting the fatwa of the scholars by their saying, unless they intend by 'obligatory' mentioned in the chapter on prostrations the fard, and it is held that what is uncertain between innovation and terminological obligation is left like a sunnah, so his saying is preferred.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of prayers after which the takbir of tashriq is recited. The matn states that there is no disagreement that the takbir is said after eight prayers (i.e., from Fajr of the Day of Arafah to Asr of the Day of Nahr). The commentator clarifies that Abu Hanifa holds this view: takbir ends after Asr on the Day of Nahr, totaling eight prayers. His two distinguished disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (Sahibayn), hold that the takbir continues until after Asr on the last day of Tashriq, which amounts to twenty-three prayers. They support their position with the practice of Umar and Ali, arguing that the larger number is more precautionary in worship. Abu Hanifa, on the other hand, follows Ibn Mas'ud, reasoning that since the audible recitation of takbir was an innovation introduced later, it is safer to limit it to the fewer number to avoid unnecessary addition in worship. The text then notes a principle: when there is doubt between an innovation and an obligatory act, one performs it as a precaution; but when between innovation and sunnah, one leaves it. This principle actually favors Sahibayn, as the takbir is closer to obligatory. Consequently, later scholars like al-Asbijabi, al-Khulasa, and al-Mujtaba declare that the fatwa is on the view of Sahibayn, and this is the established practice. The passage defends this by stating that when Abu Hanifa and his two companions differ, the weight is given to the stronger evidence, and moreover, the companions' opinions are also transmitted from Abu Hanifa himself. This refutes the objection from Fath al-Qadir that preferred Abu Hanifa's view, explaining that the term 'wajib' in the prostration chapter might mean 'fard,' thus making the precaution principle apply differently.

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (takbir al-tashriq): The phrase 'Allahu akbar' recited after obligatory prayers during the days of Tashriq.
صاحباه (sahibahu): His two companions, i.e., Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, after how many prayers does takbir al-tashriq end?
A) 8
B) 23
C) 5
D) 12

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is that takbir al-tashriq is recited after 23 prayers, following the Sahibayn's view.

Conditions of Takbir al-Tashriq and the Dispute on Eid Prayer
Rulings on conditions and a dispute regarding Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for performing Takbir al-Tashriq according to the Hanafi school and identify which conditions are disputed between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Takbir al-Tashriq is only after fard prayers in congregation for residents in a misr, but the Sahibayn allow it after Eid prayer due to inherited custom.

In this lesson, we examine the detailed conditions for Takbir al-Tashriq as outlined in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The passage lists requirements such as residence, congregational prayer, and location in a metropolis. It also addresses a notable disagreement: whether the takbir should be recited after Eid prayer. Understanding these conditions ensures correct practice during the days of Tashriq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Takbir al-Tashriq is a sunnah muakkadah performed after specific prayers. Recognize that it is not obligatory but strongly recommended.
This sets the overall context for the conditions.
2
List the conditions from the text
The passage lists conditions: residence (not traveling), being in a misr (city), after a fard prayer (maktubah) performed in congregation that is mustahabb (not women/naked), and immediate performance without delay.
Pay attention to exceptions like travelers and villages.
3
Analyze the internal Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa restricts the takbir to the five daily fard prayers, excluding Eid prayer. The Sahibayn allow it after Eid prayer due to the practice of Muslims (tawaruth). Understand the evidence for each view and the mufta bihi position.
This dispute affects practical application in many Hanafi communities.

As for the place of its performance: after the prayer and immediately without anything that cuts the sanctity of the prayer intervening, even if he laughs loudly or intentionally breaks wudu... [the text continues at length describing conditions]. And he conditioned residence (iqama) to exclude the traveler, so there is no takbir upon him. And if travelers pray in the metropolis (misr) in congregation, on the soundest view he does, as in al-Bada'i. And he restricted it to the metropolis to exclude the people of villages. And he restricted it to the prescribed prayer (maktuba) to exclude obligatory prayers like witr and Eid, and the supererogatory, so no takbir after them. In al-Mujtaba: The Balkhians recite takbir after the Eid prayer because it is performed in congregation like Friday. In the Mabsut of Abu al-Layth: If one recites takbir after the Eid prayer, there is no harm because the Muslims have inherited it so it is necessary to follow their inheritance. In al-Zahiriyya from al-Faqih Abu Ja'far: I heard that our teachers used to allow takbir in the markets during the ten days. In al-Mujtaba: Do not prevent the common people from it, and we adopt that. And Friday enters under 'prescribed prayer' as in al-Muhit. He intended by 'prescribed prayer' the obligatory prayers of the five daily prayers, so no takbir after the funeral prayer even though it is obligatory. And he conditioned it being in congregation, so no takbir for the one praying alone. And he conditioned it being mustahabb to exclude the congregation of women and naked people. And freedom is not a condition on the soundest view, so even if a slave leads a congregation, he and they must recite takbir. The commentator mentioned that the summary is that its conditions are the conditions of Friday except the sermon, the ruler, and freedom in one narration, and that is the soundest. But it is not correct, as time and general permission are not among its conditions. This all is according to Abu Hanifa, taking from the saying of Ali: 'No Friday, no Tashriq, no Fitr, no Adha except in a congregational metropolis.' For the meaning of Tashriq here is takbir as we have mentioned, because the drying of meat is not specific to any place. And they derived it from that as mentioned in its chapter. And qunut is not fard. His saying: 'And the soundest according to me is that he recites takbir.' Similarly, al-Fath mentioned it as the soundest. He said in al-Shurnublaliyya: It contradicts what al-Zayla'i said: If he is overtaken by an event before he recites takbir, he performs wudu and recites takbir on the correct view. His saying: 'And the commentator mentioned that the summary...' and similar in Sharh al-Jami' li Qadikhan. His saying: 'And it is not correct...' He said in al-Nahr: Rather it is correct, because among its conditions is time, meaning the days of Tashriq, so if he misses a prayer during its days and makes it up outside its days, he does not recite takbir. And if the ruler or his deputy is not a condition, then there is no meaning to requiring general permission. It is as if they dispensed with mentioning the ruler from it, and we have already stated that general permission was not mentioned in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage details the conditions and rules for performing the takbir of tashriq. It begins by stating the immediate performance right after the prayer, provided nothing cuts the sanctity of the prayer (like loud laughter, intentional breaking of wudu, deliberate speech, leaving the mosque, etc.). If such an act occurs, one does not say the takbir because the prayer's sanctity is lost. However, turning away from the qibla without leaving the mosque or without passing the rows does not cut the sanctity; similarly, being overtaken by an event (like breaking wudu unintentionally) does not prevent the takbir. In the case of a sudden event, one may go for wudu and return to say takbir, or may say it without purification, as the takbir does not require purity. Imam al-Sarakhsi says the soundest is not to leave for wudu because leaving without need would cut the immediacy of the prayer, so he says the takbir immediately. The text then lists conditions: residence (not a traveler), being in a city (miser), and being after obligatory prayers (maktuba), not after witr or Eid prayers or nafl. However, there are narrations from Balkh and Abu al-Layth allowing takbir after Eid prayer due to custom. The takbir is also recommended in the markets during the ten days. Congregation is a condition, so the person praying alone does not recite. The prayer must be one recommended (mustahabb) for congregation, excluding women's congregation and naked people. Freedom is not a condition. The passage then discusses a comparison to Friday prayer conditions, but corrects that time (the days of Tashriq) and general permission are not conditions. The final part refutes a commentator's claim that the condition al-amm are not required, citing that the ruler is not a condition, so general permission is irrelevant. It also notes that if a missed prayer is made up outside the days of Tashriq, no takbir is said.

Key Terms
مصر (misr): A city where congregational Friday prayer is held; here, the takbir is limited to such places.
مكتوبة (maktubah): The prescribed obligatory daily prayers (five times), excluding funeral prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Takbir al-Tashriq is a sunnah muakkadah with specific conditions and an internal Hanafi dispute about Eid prayer, with the mufta bihi allowing takbir after Eid.

Takbir al-Tashriq: Continuity Despite Hadath
Ruling on when takbir is still recited despite interruption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between actions that break the sanctity (hurmat) of the prayer time and those that do not, and apply the Hanafi ruling on reciting Takbir al-Tashriq when overtaken by hadath.

Core Idea
Takbir al-tashriq follows the sanctity of prayer; hadath does not break it, but speech and leaving do.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the effect of various post-prayer interruptions on the obligation to recite takbir al-tashriq. Understanding which actions preserve the sanctity of the prayer time and which break it is essential for correctly performing this sunnah muakkadah. We will examine the key principle that takbir is a characteristic of prayer and thus its performance depends on the continuity of that sanctity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Takbir al-tashriq is a sunnah muakkadah recited after fard prayers on the days of tashriq. The passage discusses whether it should still be recited after certain interruptions.
This is a post-prayer dhikr, not a prayer itself.
2
Categorize interruptions
Distinguish between actions that break the sanctity (speech, leaving mosque) and those that do not (turning face, hadath). The sanctity is the hurmat of the prayer time that remains after the prayer.
The passage lists specific examples.
3
Apply the qiyas principle
The origin is that whatever cuts the building (of prayer) cuts the takbir, and what does not cut it does not cut takbir. This analogy connects takbir to prayer continuity.
This is the key talil.
4
Handle the case of hadath
Two options: go purify and return, or recite immediately. Understand the reasoning: takbir does not require taharah, so immediate recitation is valid.
Imam al-Sarakhsi's preferred view is to recite immediately.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The strongest view is to recite immediately without leaving, to preserve the continuity of the prayer time.
This is based on the principle that leaving without need would cut the building.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو تكلم عامداً أو ساهياً أو خرج من المسجد أو جاوز الصفوف في الصحراء لا يكبر لأن التكبير من خصائص الصلاة حيث لا يؤتى به إلا عقب الصلاة فيراعي لإتيانه حرمتها وهذه العوارض تقطع حرمتها، ولو صرف وجهه عن القبلة ولم يخرج من المسجد ولم يجاوز الصفوف أو سبقه الحدث يكبر لأن حرمة الصلاة باقية والأصل أن كل ما يقطع البناء يقطع التكبير وما لا فلا . وإذا . سبقه الحدث فإن شاء ذهب وتوضأ ورجع فكبر، وإن شاء كبر من غير تطهير لأنه لا يؤدي في تحريمة الصلاة فلا يشترط له الطهارة . قال الإمام السرخسي والأصح عندي أنه يكبر ولا يخرج من المسجد للطهارة لأن التكبير لما لم يفتقر إلى الطهارة كان خروجه مع عدم الحاجة قاطعاً لفور الصلاة فلا يمكنه التكبير بعد ذلك فيكبر للحال جزماً. كذا في البدائع .
Or if he speaks intentionally or unintentionally, or leaves the mosque, or passes beyond the rows in the desert, he does not recite takbir because takbir is from the characteristics of prayer, as it is only performed after prayer, so for its performance one considers its sanctity, and these occurrences cut its sanctity. But if he turns his face away from the qibla without leaving the mosque or passing beyond the rows, or if hadath overtakes him, he recites takbir because the sanctity of prayer remains, and the origin is that everything that cuts the building (of prayer) cuts the takbir, and what does not, does not. And if hadath overtakes him, then if he wishes he goes, performs wudu, returns, and recites takbir; and if he wishes he recites takbir without purification because it is not performed within the opening of prayer, so purification is not a condition for it. Imam al-Sarakhsi said: the most correct view according to me is that he recites takbir and does not leave the mosque for purification, because since takbir does not require purification, his leaving without need would be cutting the continuity of prayer, so he cannot recite takbir after that, so he recites takbir immediately definitively. Thus in al-Bada'i'.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement combined with proof. It discusses the effect of various actions on the permissibility of reciting takbir al-tashriq after an obligatory prayer. The author first lists actions that cut the sanctity of the prayer time, thereby preventing takbir: deliberate or forgetful speech, leaving the mosque (or passing beyond the rows in an open desert). The reasoning is that takbir is a characteristic of prayer—it is performed only after prayer—so its performance respects the sanctity of the prayer time. These actions break that sanctity. Conversely, turning the face away from the qibla while remaining inside the mosque or congregation, or being overtaken by a ritual impurity (hadath), does not break the sanctity, so takbir is still recited. The author then details the case of hadath: the person may either go, perform wudu, return, and recite takbir, or recite immediately without purification because takbir does not require taharah for its commencement. Imam al-Sarakhsi prefers that he recite immediately without leaving the mosque, since leaving would break the continuity of the prayer time, making subsequent takbir impossible. This ruling is from the Bada'i' al-Sana'i'.

Key Terms
حرمة الصلاة (hurmat al-salat): The inviolability or sanctity of the prayer time, which continues after the prayer for performing follow-up acts like takbir.
الحدث (al-hadath): A state of ritual impurity (minor or major) that nullifies wudu or requires ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person is overtaken by hadath after praying Fajr on the day of Arafah, what is the ruling regarding takbir al-tashriq according to the preferred Hanafi view?
A) He must not recite because he is impure.
B) He may recite immediately without purification.
C) He must first do wudu and then recite.
D) He must leave the mosque to purify.

Key Takeaway
Takbir al-tashriq is recited after prayer as long as the sanctity of the prayer time remains intact; hadath does not break it, but speech and leaving do.

Conditions for Takbir al-Tashriq According to Abu Hanifa
Lists conditions for takbir and discusses dispute about equivalence to Jumu'ah conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for Takbir al-Tashriq and identify which conditions are disputed within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Takbir al-Tashriq is only for residents praying in congregation in a city after the five daily prayers.

Takbir al-Tashriq is a sunnah muakkadah recited during the days of Tashriq. However, it is not obligatory on everyone. The Hanafi school sets specific conditions that must be met for its recitation. This lesson will parse those conditions and examine a key intra-Hanafi dispute about whether they match the conditions of Jumu'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal status
Takbir al-Tashriq is a sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah) according to the Hanafi school. Understand that it is not fard or wajib.
2
Enumerate the conditions
List the conditions: residence (not traveler), city (not village), congregation (not alone), after an obligatory five-time prayer (not witr, Eid, or funeral), and the congregation must be of men (not women or naked people).
Freedom is not a condition; slaves may recite.
3
Examine the exceptions and special cases
Note that travelers can recite if they pray in a city congregation. The people of Balkh recite after Eid prayer based on custom. Funeral prayer is excluded despite being obligatory.
Custom plays a role in the Balkh practice.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
A commentator equated the conditions to those of Jumu'ah, adding time and general permission. The author rejects this, citing the statement of Ali (ra) that these prayers are only in a major city. Also, there is a dispute about wudu if hadath occurs before takbir.
The author's view is the mufta bihi.
5
Trace the dalil
The primary evidence is the saying of Ali ibn Abi Talib (ra): 'There is no Jumu'ah, no tashriq, no Fitr, no Adha except in a major city.' This proves restriction to a city.
Tashriq here is interpreted as takbir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشرط الإقامة احترازاً عن المسافر فلا تكبير عليه، ولو صلى المسافرون في المصر جماعة على الأصح كما في البدائع . وقيد بالمصر احترازاً : عن ن أهل القرى، وقيد بالمكتوبة احترازاً عن الواجب كصلاة الوتر والعيدين وعن النافلة فلا تكبير عقبها. وفي المجتبى : والبلخيون يكبرون عقب صلاة العيد لأنها تؤدى بجماعة فأشبه الجمعة .اهـ. وفي مبسوط أبي الليث : ولو كبر على أثر صلاة العيد لا بأس به لأن المسلمين توارثوا هكذا فوجب أن يتبع توارث المسلمين أهـ. وفي الظهيرية عن الفقيه أبي جعفر قال : سمعت أن مشايخنا كانوا يرون التكبير في الأسواق في الأيام العشر اهـ. وفي المجتبى : لا تمنع العامة عنه وبه نأخذ وتدخل الجمعة في المكتوبة كما في المحيط. وأراد بالمكتوبة الصلاة المفروضة من الصلوات الخمس فلا تكبير عقب صلاة الجنازة وإن كانت مكتوبة . وقيد بالجماعة فلا تكبير على المنفرد ، وقيد بكونها مستحبة احترازاً عن جماعة النساء والعراة، ولم يشترط الحرية لأنها ليست بشرط على الأصح حتى لو أم العبد قوماً وجب عليه وعليهم التكبير . وذكر الشارح أن الحاصل أن شروطه شروط الجمعة غير الخطبة والسلطان والحرية في رواية وهو الأصح .اهـ. وليس بصحيح إذ ليس الوقت والإذن العام من شروطه، وهذا كله عند أبي حنيفة أخذاً من قول علي لا جمعة ولا تشريق ولا فطر ولا أضحى إلا في مصر جامع فإن المراد بالتشريق التكبير كما قدمناه لأن تشريق اللحم لا يختص بمكان دون مكان . وعللوه بذلك كما مر في بابه مع أن القنوت غير فرض قوله : (والأصح عندي أنه يكبر) وكذا ذكر في الفتح أنه الأصح . قال في الشرنبلالية ويخالفه ما قاله الزيلعي وإن سبقه الحدث قبل أن يكبر توضأ وكبر على الصحيح.
And the condition of residence is to exclude the traveler, so there is no takbir upon him, even if travelers pray in the city with congregation according to the most correct view, as in al-Bada'i'. And it is restricted to the city to exclude the people of villages. And restricted to the obligatory prayer (maktubah) to exclude the obligatory like witr and the two Eids and supererogatory, so no takbir after them. In al-Mujtaba: The people of Balkh recite takbir after the Eid prayer because it is performed with congregation, so it resembles Jumu'ah. End. In Mabsut of Abu al-Layth: If he recites takbir after the Eid prayer, it is fine because Muslims have inherited it this way, so it is necessary to follow the inheritance of Muslims. End. In al-Zahiriyyah from al-Faqih Abu Ja'far: I heard that our teachers used to see takbir in the markets in the ten days. End. In al-Mujtaba: Do not prevent the public from it, and we adopt it, and Jumu'ah is included in the obligatory prayers, as in al-Muhit. And by 'obligatory prayer' he means the five daily prayers, so no takbir after funeral prayer even though it is obligatory. And restricted by congregation, so no takbir for the one praying alone. And restricted by it being recommended (mustahabbah) to exclude the congregation of women and naked people. And freedom is not a condition because it is not a condition according to the most correct view, so even if a slave leads a congregation, takbir is obligatory upon him and them. And the commentator said: the summary is that its conditions are the conditions of Jumu'ah except for the khutbah, the ruler, and freedom in one narration, and it is the most correct. End. But it is not correct because time and general permission are not among its conditions. And all this according to Abu Hanifa, taken from the saying of Ali: 'There is no Jumu'ah, no tashriq, no Fitr, no Adha except in a major city.' For by 'tashriq' is meant takbir, as we have mentioned, because the drying of meat is not specific to any place. And they explained it with that as has passed in its chapter, even though qunut is not obligatory. His saying: (And the most correct according to me is that he recites takbir) and similarly mentioned in al-Fath that it is the most correct. He said in al-Sharnuballaliyyah: And what al-Zayla'i said contradicts it: if he is overtaken by hadath before reciting takbir, he performs wudu and recites takbir, which is the correct view.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage enumerates the conditions for the obligation or recommendation of takbir al-tashriq according to Abu Hanifa. Key conditions are: (1) residency (excluding travelers), though if travelers pray congregationally in a city, they do recite takbir; (2) congregation performed in a major city (misr), excluding villagers; (3) the prayer must be an obligatory five-time prayer (maktubah), excluding obligatory prayers like witr, Eid, and supererogatory prayers. The author notes that the people of Balkh and others recite takbir after Eid prayer based on custom. The congregation must be a recommended congregation of men, not solely women or naked people. Slaves can lead and takbir is obligatory on them and their followers. The commentator (the author of the sharh?) states that the conditions resemble those of Jumu'ah except for khutbah, sultan, and freedom. The author rejects this, saying time (i.e., the days of Tashriq) and general permission are not conditions. The basis is the statement of Ali that these prayers are only in a major city. The passage also mentions a dispute within the Hanafi school about whether one should leave for wudu after hadath before takbir; al-Zayla'i holds that wudu is required.

Key Terms
المصر (al-misr): A major city with a congregational mosque where Jumu'ah is held.
المكتوبة (al-maktubah): The five daily obligatory prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, who must recite Takbir al-Tashriq?
A) Every Muslim, regardless of location.
B) Residents praying in congregation in a city after the five daily prayers.
C) Only men, excluding women and travelers.
D) Both residents and travelers, provided they pray in congregation.

Key Takeaway
Takbir al-Tashriq is a sunnah muakkadah for resident men praying in congregation in a city after the five obligatory prayers.

Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn: Who Must Recite Takbir al-Tashriq?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on obligation of takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding who must recite takbir al-tashriq and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school adopted the Sahibayn's view that takbir is obligatory on all who pray the fard prayer.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute where the two chief disciples differ from the Imam on the obligation of takbir al-tashriq. While Abu Hanifa restricted it to residents praying in congregation, the Sahibayn extended it to everyone who performs the obligatory prayers. The later school followed the more comprehensive view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two positions
Determine what act is under discussion (takbir al-tashriq) and who is obligated according to each view.
Abu Hanifa: only residents in congregation; Sahibayn: all who pray the fard prayer.
2
Examine the basis of each position
Locate the dalil for each view. Abu Hanifa's basis was a hadith from Ali; the Sahibayn reasoned that takbir follows the prayer.
For Sahibayn, 'it is a follower of it, so it is obligatory upon the traveler, the woman, and the villager.'
3
Notice the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Understand how the difference affects actual practice. Under Abu Hanifa, a traveler alone does not recite; under Sahibayn, he must.
The thamarah is a difference in obligation for travelers, women, and villagers.
4
Identify the mufta bihi position
The passage states that the fatwa is upon the view of the Sahibayn. Recognise that the school adopts their view for practical application.
Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Jawhara confirm this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما عندهما فهو واجب على كل من يصلي المكتوبة لأنه تبع لها فيجب على المسافر والمرأة والقروي. قال في السراج الوهاج والجوهرة والفتوى على قولهما في هذا أيضاً. فالحاصل أن الفتوى على قولهما في آخر وقته وفيمن يجب عليه.
And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is obligatory upon everyone who prays the obligatory prayer because it is a follower of it, so it is obligatory upon the traveler, the woman, and the villager. He said in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Jawhara: The fatwa is upon their view in this as well. So the conclusion is that the fatwa is upon their view regarding its end time and regarding who it is obligatory upon.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). According to Abu Hanifa (as detailed earlier), takbir al-tashriq is only for residents praying in congregation. But the Sahibayn consider it obligatory (or sunnah muakkadah) on every person who prays any of the five daily prayers, regardless of travel, gender, or village residence. Their reasoning is that takbir is a follower (tabi') of the prayer, so it shares its obligation. The text then states that the fatwa (authoritative legal opinion) is upon the view of the Sahibayn, both regarding the time (i.e., that it lasts until the end of the days of Tashriq) and regarding who must recite it. This is a clear example of how the later Hanafi school adopted the more expansive view of the two companions for practice.

Key Terms
عندهما (indahuma): According to the two: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
الفتوى على قولهما (al-fatwa 'ala qawlihima): The authoritative legal opinion is based on their view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only residents in cities.
B) Only men over puberty.
C) Everyone who prays the obligatory prayer, including travelers and women.
D) Only those who attend the Eid prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's mufta bihi is that takbir al-tashriq is wajib on every person who prays the obligatory prayer, regardless of travel, gender, or location.

Takbir al-Tashriq for Qada Prayers: The Four Scenarios
Explains four scenarios for takbir in qada prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four scenarios for takbir al-tashriq in make-up prayers and state the ruling for each, including the disagreement of Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Takbir al-tashriq applies to a make-up prayer only if the prayer was missed during the Days of Tashriq and is made up in the same year.

When a person misses a prayer during the Days of Tashriq (11th-13th of Dhul Hijjah) and later makes it up, is takbir al-tashriq required? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies four distinct cases, only one of which mandates takbir. Mastering these scenarios prevents errors in post-prayer practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The author states that takbir after these prayers applies to both performance (ada) and make-up (qada).
2
List the three exceptions
There are three cases where no takbir is recited: (1) missing outside Tashriq and making up inside, (2) missing inside and making up outside, (3) missing inside and making up in the next year inside.
The first two are agreed upon; the third is disputed.
3
Note the disagreement on the third case
Abu Yusuf disagreed on the third case, but the correct position (zahir al-riwaya) is no takbir.
4
Apply the fourth case
Takbir is only recited in the fourth case: missing during the days and making up in the same year during the days, because the time is still present, like the udhiyah sacrifice.
This is the only scenario where takbir is required for qada.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأطلق المصنف في التكبير عقب هذه الصلوات فشمل الأداء والقضاء وهي رباعية لا تكبير في ثلاثة منها : الأولى فاتته في غير أيام التشريق فقضاها فيها. ثانيها فاتته في هذه الأيام فقضاها في غير هذه الأيام . ثالثها فاتته في هذه الأيام فقضاها فيها من السنة القابلة ولا تكبير في الأوليين اتفاقاً. وفي الثالثة خلاف أبي يوسف والصحيح ظاهر الرواية والتكبير إنما هو في الرابعة وهي ما إذا فاتته في هذه الأيام فقضاها فيها من هذه السنة فإنه يكبر لقيام وقته كالأضحية، ثم الذي يؤدي عقب الصلاة ثلاثة أشياء : سجود السهو وتكبير التشريق والتلبية إلا أن السهو يؤدي في تحريمة الاقتداء بالساهي بعد سلامه والتكبير يؤدي في حرمتها لا في تحريمتها حتى الصلاة حتى صح بهم الأستاذ في لم يصح الاقتداء بالإمام بعد السلام قبل التكبير والتلبية لا تؤدى في شيء منها، ولذا قال في الخلاصة : ويبدأ الإمام بسجود السهو ثم بالتكبير ثم بالتلبية إن كان محرماً. وفي فتاوى الولوالجي : لو بدأ بالتلبية سقط السجود والتكبير ولما لم يكن مؤدى في تحريمتها لو تركه الإمام فعلى القوم أن يأتوا به كسامع السجدة مع تاليها بخلاف ما إذا لم يسجد لإمام للسهو فإنهم لا يسجدون . قال يعقوب : صليت . المغرب يوم عرفة فسهوت أن أكبر بهم فكبر بهم أبو حنيفة رحمه الله . وقد استنبط من هذه الواقعة أشياء منها هذه المسألة، ومنها أن تعظيم إطاعته لا فيما يظنه طاعة لأن أبا يوسف تقدم بأمر أبي حنيفة ، ومنها أنه ينبغي للأستاذ إذا تفرس في بعض أصحابه الخير أن يقدمه ويعظمه عند الناس حتى يعظموه، ومنها أن التلميذ لا ينبغي أن ينسى حرمة أستاذه وإن قدمه أستاذه وعظمه ألا ترى أن أبا يوسف شغله ذلك عن التكبير حتى سها قوله (وبالاقتداء يجب على المرأة والمسافر أي باقتدائهما بمن يجب عليه يجب عليهما بطريق التبعية. والمرأة تخافت بالتكبير لأن صوتها ،عورة، وكذا يجب على المسبوق لأنه مقتد تحريمة لكن لا يكبر مع الإمام ويكبر بعدما قضى ما فاته وفي الأصل: ولو تابعه لا تفسد صلاته وفي التلبية تفسد. كذا في الخلاصة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم بالصواب.
And the author (al-Musannif) spoke absolutely about takbir after these prayers, so it includes performance and make-up, and it is tetra: no takbir in three of them: first: one missed it in non-days of Tashriq and made it up in them; second: one missed it in these days and made it up in other than these days; third: one missed it in these days and made it up in them in the next year; and there is no takbir in the first two by agreement. In the third there is disagreement of Abu Yusuf, and the correct is the apparent narration, and takbir is only in the fourth: that is when one missed it in these days and made it up in them in this same year, because its time stands, like the udhiyah. Then three things are performed after prayer: sajdat al-sahw, takbir al-tashriq, and talbiyah, except that sajdat al-sahw is performed within the opening of following the forgetful one after his salam, and takbir is performed within its sanctity, not in its opening, until prayer until correct with them the teacher in it is not correct for following the imam after salam before takbir, and talbiyah is not performed in any of them. And for that reason it is said in al-Khulasah: The imam begins with sajdat al-sahw, then takbir, then talbiyah if he is in ihram. And in Fatawa al-Walwaliji: If he begins with talbiyah, the prostration and takbir drop. And since it is not performed in its opening, if the imam leaves it, then the congregation should perform it like the hearer of the prostration verse with the reciter, unlike when the imam does not prostrate for forgetfulness, they do not prostrate. Ya'qub said: I prayed Maghrib on the day of Arafah and I forgot to recite takbir with them, so Abu Hanifa recited takbir with them. And from this incident things have been derived, including this issue, and that the reverence for his obedience is not in what he thinks is obedience because Abu Yusuf advanced by the order of Abu Hanifa, and that it is proper for a teacher when he perceives good in some of his students to advance him and honor him before people so that they honor him, and that a student should not forget the respect of his teacher even if his teacher advances and honors him. Do you not see that that occupied Abu Yusuf such that he forgot the takbir? His saying: (And by following, it becomes obligatory upon the woman and the traveler) i.e., by their following someone upon whom it is obligatory, it becomes obligatory upon them by way of subordination. And the woman should lower her voice in takbir because her voice is ‘awrah. Similarly, it is obligatory upon the masbuq because he is a follower in the opening, but he does not recite takbir with the imam; he recites after completing what he missed. And in al-Asl: If he follows him (in takbir), his prayer would not be invalidated, but in talbiyah it would be invalidated. Thus in al-Khulasah. And Allah, Most High, knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage covers several separate rulings. First, it discusses four scenarios for make-up prayers (qada) regarding takbir: no takbir when a prayer missed outside the days of Tashriq is made up within them; no takbir when a prayer missed during the days is made up outside them; no takbir when it is made up in the same days but in the next year (disputed by Abu Yusuf, but the correct view is no takbir). Takbir is only recited in the fourth scenario: when a prayer missed during the days of Tashriq is made up within the same year in these days. Second, it clarifies the order of three post-prayer acts: sajdat al-sahw, then takbir al-tashriq, then talbiyah for someone in ihram. This order is from the Khulasah. Third, an anecdote: Ya'qub (Abu Yusuf) forgot the takbir, so Abu Hanifa led it himself. Lessons are derived about respect for teachers and not letting such respect cause negligence. Fourth, it discusses that women and travelers must recite takbir if they follow someone upon whom it is obligatory; women should say it quietly. A masbuq (latecomer) recites takbir after completing his missed parts. Following an imam in talbiyah invalidates prayer, but following in takbir does not, per al-Asl.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Prostration for forgetfulness performed after the prayer to compensate for omissions or additions.
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The phrase 'Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk' recited by one in ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which scenario requires takbir al-tashriq for a make-up prayer?
A) Missed outside Tashriq, made up in Tashriq
B) Missed in Tashriq, made up outside Tashriq
C) Missed in Tashriq, made up in next year's Tashriq
D) Missed in Tashriq, made up in same year's Tashriq

Key Takeaway
Takbir al-tashriq for make-up prayers is only required when the prayer was missed during the Days of Tashriq and is made up within the same year's Days of Tashriq.
