Order of Post-Prayer Acts: Sajda, Takbir, Talbiya
Explains order of sajda, takbir, talbiya after prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the order of sajdat al-sahw, takbir al-tashriq, and talbiya after prayer, and explain the ruling if the order is changed.

Core Idea
The prescribed order is sajdat al-sahw first, then takbir, then talbiya; beginning with talbiya drops the other two.

After the fard prayer, three acts may be performed: sajdat al-sahw, takbir al-tashriq, and talbiya (if in ihram). This passage establishes their correct order and explains what happens if the order is violated, particularly if one begins with talbiya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three post-prayer acts
The passage lists three: sajdat al-sahw, takbir al-tashriq, and talbiya.
Talbiya only applies if one is in ihram.
2
Determine the correct order
From al-Khulasah: the imam begins with sajdat al-sahw, then takbir, then talbiya.
This order is the recommended sequence.
3
Analyze the consequence of changing the order
If one begins with talbiya, both sajdat al-sahw and takbir are dropped (Fatawa al-Walwaliji).
The reason is that talbiya is not performed within the prayer's sanctity, so it breaks the sequence.
4
Apply the rule for the congregation if imam omits an act
If the imam omits sajdat al-sahw, the followers must perform it themselves, unlike the case where the imam does not prostrate for forgetfulness at all (then followers do not prostrate).
The passage draws an analogy to the hearer of a prostration verse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأطلق المصنف في التكبير عقب هذه الصلوات فشمل الأداء والقضاء وهي رباعية لا تكبير في ثلاثة منها : الأولى فاتته في غير أيام التشريق فقضاها فيها. ثانيها فاتته في هذه الأيام فقضاها في غير هذه الأيام . ثالثها فاتته في هذه الأيام فقضاها فيها من السنة القابلة ولا تكبير في الأوليين اتفاقاً. وفي الثالثة خلاف أبي يوسف والصحيح ظاهر الرواية والتكبير إنما هو في الرابعة وهي ما إذا فاتته في هذه الأيام فقضاها فيها من هذه السنة فإنه يكبر لقيام وقته كالأضحية، ثم الذي يؤدي عقب الصلاة ثلاثة أشياء : سجود السهو وتكبير التشريق والتلبية إلا أن السهو يؤدي في تحريمة الاقتداء بالساهي بعد سلامه والتكبير يؤدي في حرمتها لا في تحريمتها حتى الصلاة حتى صح بهم الأستاذ في لم يصح الاقتداء بالإمام بعد السلام قبل التكبير والتلبية لا تؤدى في شيء منها، ولذا قال في الخلاصة : ويبدأ الإمام بسجود السهو ثم بالتكبير ثم بالتلبية إن كان محرماً. وفي فتاوى الولوالجي : لو بدأ بالتلبية سقط السجود والتكبير ولما لم يكن مؤدى في تحريمتها لو تركه الإمام فعلى القوم أن يأتوا به كسامع السجدة مع تاليها بخلاف ما إذا لم يسجد لإمام للسهو فإنهم لا يسجدون . قال يعقوب : صليت . المغرب يوم عرفة فسهوت أن أكبر بهم فكبر بهم أبو حنيفة رحمه الله . وقد استنبط من هذه الواقعة أشياء منها هذه المسألة، ومنها أن تعظيم إطاعته لا فيما يظنه طاعة لأن أبا يوسف تقدم بأمر أبي حنيفة ، ومنها أنه ينبغي للأستاذ إذا تفرس في بعض أصحابه الخير أن يقدمه ويعظمه عند الناس حتى يعظموه، ومنها أن التلميذ لا ينبغي أن ينسى حرمة أستاذه وإن قدمه أستاذه وعظمه ألا ترى أن أبا يوسف شغله ذلك عن التكبير حتى سها قوله (وبالاقتداء يجب على المرأة والمسافر أي باقتدائهما بمن يجب عليه يجب عليهما بطريق التبعية. والمرأة تخافت بالتكبير لأن صوتها ،عورة، وكذا يجب على المسبوق لأنه مقتد تحريمة لكن لا يكبر مع الإمام ويكبر بعدما قضى ما فاته وفي الأصل: ولو تابعه لا تفسد صلاته وفي التلبية تفسد. كذا في الخلاصة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم بالصواب.
And the author (al-Musannif) spoke absolutely about takbir after these prayers, so it includes performance and make-up, and it is tetra: no takbir in three of them: first: one missed it in non-days of Tashriq and made it up in them; second: one missed it in these days and made it up in other than these days; third: one missed it in these days and made it up in them in the next year; and there is no takbir in the first two by agreement. In the third there is disagreement of Abu Yusuf, and the correct is the apparent narration, and takbir is only in the fourth: that is when one missed it in these days and made it up in them in this same year, because its time stands, like the udhiyah. Then three things are performed after prayer: sajdat al-sahw, takbir al-tashriq, and talbiyah, except that sajdat al-sahw is performed within the opening of following the forgetful one after his salam, and takbir is performed within its sanctity, not in its opening, until prayer until correct with them the teacher in it is not correct for following the imam after salam before takbir, and talbiyah is not performed in any of them. And for that reason it is said in al-Khulasah: The imam begins with sajdat al-sahw, then takbir, then talbiyah if he is in ihram. And in Fatawa al-Walwaliji: If he begins with talbiyah, the prostration and takbir drop. And since it is not performed in its opening, if the imam leaves it, then the congregation should perform it like the hearer of the prostration verse with the reciter, unlike when the imam does not prostrate for forgetfulness, they do not prostrate. Ya'qub said: I prayed Maghrib on the day of Arafah and I forgot to recite takbir with them, so Abu Hanifa recited takbir with them. And from this incident things have been derived, including this issue, and that the reverence for his obedience is not in what he thinks is obedience because Abu Yusuf advanced by the order of Abu Hanifa, and that it is proper for a teacher when he perceives good in some of his students to advance him and honor him before people so that they honor him, and that a student should not forget the respect of his teacher even if his teacher advances and honors him. Do you not see that that occupied Abu Yusuf such that he forgot the takbir? His saying: (And by following, it becomes obligatory upon the woman and the traveler) i.e., by their following someone upon whom it is obligatory, it becomes obligatory upon them by way of subordination. And the woman should lower her voice in takbir because her voice is ‘awrah. Similarly, it is obligatory upon the masbuq because he is a follower in the opening, but he does not recite takbir with the imam; he recites after completing what he missed. And in al-Asl: If he follows him (in takbir), his prayer would not be invalidated, but in talbiyah it would be invalidated. Thus in al-Khulasah. And Allah, Most High, knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage covers several separate rulings. First, it discusses four scenarios for make-up prayers (qada) regarding takbir: no takbir when a prayer missed outside the days of Tashriq is made up within them; no takbir when a prayer missed during the days is made up outside them; no takbir when it is made up in the same days but in the next year (disputed by Abu Yusuf, but the correct view is no takbir). Takbir is only recited in the fourth scenario: when a prayer missed during the days of Tashriq is made up within the same year in these days. Second, it clarifies the order of three post-prayer acts: sajdat al-sahw, then takbir al-tashriq, then talbiyah for someone in ihram. This order is from the Khulasah. Third, an anecdote: Ya'qub (Abu Yusuf) forgot the takbir, so Abu Hanifa led it himself. Lessons are derived about respect for teachers and not letting such respect cause negligence. Fourth, it discusses that women and travelers must recite takbir if they follow someone upon whom it is obligatory; women should say it quietly. A masbuq (latecomer) recites takbir after completing his missed parts. Following an imam in talbiyah invalidates prayer, but following in takbir does not, per al-Asl.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Prostration for forgetfulness performed after the prayer to compensate for omissions or additions.
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The phrase 'Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk' recited by one in ihram.
تكبير التشريق (takbir al-tashriq): The phrase 'Allahu akbar, Allahu akbar, la ilaha illa Allah, wallahu akbar, Allahu akbar, wa lillahi al-hamd' recited after fard prayers from the Fajr of Arafa to the Asr of the 13th of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Fatawa al-Walwaliji, what happens if one begins with talbiya after prayer?
A) Sajdat al-sahw and takbir are still valid if done afterwards.
B) Only sajdat al-sahw is dropped.
C) Both sajdat al-sahw and takbir are dropped.
D) The prayer becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
The correct order after prayer is sajdat al-sahw first, then takbir al-tashriq, then talbiya; beginning with talbiya drops the other two.

Rulings for Women, Travelers, and the Masbuq on Takbir
Rulings for women, travelers, masbuq on takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for women, travelers, and the masbuq regarding takbir al-tashriq, including the proper timing and consequences of following the imam.

Core Idea
Women and travelers follow the obligation of takbir when they pray behind someone upon whom it is obligatory; a masbuq recites takbir after completing his missed rak'ats, not with the imam.

Takbir al-tashriq is obligatory upon residents in congregation. But what about women, travelers, and those who join late (masbuq)? This passage explains that they become obligated by following someone who is obligated. It also specifies the proper time for the masbuq to recite takbir and warns that following the imam in talbiya invalidates the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Understand the general rule of obligation via following
The passage states that women and travelers are obligated to recite takbir by way of subordination when they follow an imam upon whom it is obligatory.
This is a secondary obligation (follow-up).
2
Note the special ruling for women regarding voice
Women must lower their voice (ikhfat) when reciting takbir because their voice is awrah (i.e., they should not attract attention).
This applies to all recitations in prayer for women.
3
Apply the ruling for the masbuq (latecomer)
The masbuq is obligated similarly because he is a follower in the opening, but he does not recite takbir with the imam; he recites after completing what he missed.
This ensures his takbir is performed within the sanctity of his own prayer completion.
4
Distinguish between following in takbir vs. talbiya
If the masbuq follows the imam in takbir (i.e., recites with him), his prayer is not invalidated. But if he follows in talbiya, his prayer is invalidated.
Takbir is part of the prayer's sanctity, while talbiya is not a part of prayer.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage covers several separate rulings. First, it discusses four scenarios for make-up prayers (qada) regarding takbir: no takbir when a prayer missed outside the days of Tashriq is made up within them; no takbir when a prayer missed during the days is made up outside them; no takbir when it is made up in the same days but in the next year (disputed by Abu Yusuf, but the correct view is no takbir). Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): One who joins the congregation late and misses part of the prayer.
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The phrase 'Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk' recited by one in ihram.
عورة (awrah): Intimate parts that must be covered. For a woman's voice, it is considered awrah in the context of recitation leading to attracting non-mahram men.

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a masbuq regarding takbir al-tashriq?
A) He recites it with the imam immediately after the imam's salam.
B) He recites it after completing his make-up rak'ats.
C) He does not recite it because he is a follower.
D) He recites it before the salam of the imam.

Key Takeaway
Women, travelers, and masbuq are obligated to recite takbir when following an obligated imam; women lower their voice, masbuq recites after finishing make-up, and following in talbiya invalidates prayer.

Takbir al-Tashriq: Obligation and Qada Scenarios
Expansion of qada rules for Takbir al-Tashriq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on Takbir al-Tashriq, identify the four qada scenarios, and determine when the takbir is required after make-up prayers.

Core Idea
Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib on all who pray fard, but qada takbir only if missed and made up within the same Tashriq year.

This lesson examines the ruling of Takbir al-Tashriq—the takbirs recited after fard prayers from the day of Arafah through the days of Tashriq. We explore an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding its obligation and the specific scenarios in which it applies to make-up prayers. The passage also clarifies the order of post-prayer actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State what Takbir al-Tashriq is and its legal status per the Hanafi school.
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is wajib upon everyone who prays the prescribed prayer.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Contrast the Sahibayn's view with Imam Abu Hanifa's (the latter considers it sunnah). Identify that the fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view.
The text explicitly says 'al-fatwa 'ala qawlihima'.
3
Examine the four qada scenarios
List the four possibilities for making up a missed prayer relative to the days of Tashriq. Determine in which scenario the takbir is required.
Takbir is only required in the fourth scenario: missed during Tashriq and made up in the same year's Tashriq days.
4
Apply the post-prayer order
Understand the sequence: sajdah al-sahw, then takbir al-tashriq, then talbiya. Note that if talbiya is started first, the previous two are dropped.
This is relevant for the imam leading the prayer.
5
Consider special cases
Apply the ruling to women (lower voice) and the masbuq (performs takbir after completing missed rakats).
The masbuq does not follow the imam in takbir but does it later.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة باب صلاة العيدين وأما عندهما فهو واجب على كل من يصلي المكتوبة لأنه تبع لها فيجب على المسافر والمرأة والقروي. قال في السراج الوهاج والجوهرة والفتوى على قولهما في هذا أيضاً. فالحاصل أن الفتوى على قولهما في آخر وقته وفيمن يجب عليه. وأطلق المصنف في التكبير عقب هذه الصلوات فشمل الأداء والقضاء وهي رباعية لا تكبير في ثلاثة منها : الأولى فاتته في غير أيام التشريق فقضاها فيها. ثانيها فاتته في هذه الأيام فقضاها في غير هذه الأيام . ثالثها فاتته في هذه الأيام فقضاها فيها من السنة القابلة ولا تكبير في الأوليين اتفاقاً. وفي الثالثة خلاف أبي يوسف والصحيح ظاهر الرواية والتكبير إنما هو في الرابعة وهي ما إذا فاتته في هذه الأيام فقضاها فيها من هذه السنة فإنه يكبر لقيام وقته كالأضحية، ثم الذي يؤدي عقب الصلاة ثلاثة أشياء : سجود السهو وتكبير التشريق والتلبية إلا أن السهو يؤدي في تحريمة الاقتداء بالساهي بعد سلامه والتكبير يؤدي في حرمتها لا في تحريمتها حتى الصلاة حتى صح بهم الأستاذ في لم يصح الاقتداء بالإمام بعد السلام قبل التكبير والتلبية لا تؤدى في شيء منها، ولذا قال في الخلاصة : ويبدأ الإمام بسجود السهو ثم بالتكبير ثم بالتلبية إن كان محرماً. وفي فتاوى الولوالجي : لو بدأ بالتلبية سقط السجود والتكبير ولما لم يكن مؤدى في تحريمتها لو تركه الإمام فعلى القوم أن يأتوا به كسامع السجدة مع تاليها بخلاف ما إذا لم يسجد لإمام للسهو فإنهم لا يسجدون . قال يعقوب : صليت . المغرب يوم عرفة فسهوت أن أكبر بهم فكبر بهم أبو حنيفة رحمه الله . وقد استنبط من هذه الواقعة أشياء منها هذه المسألة، ومنها أن تعظيم إطاعته لا فيما يظنه طاعة لأن أبا يوسف تقدم بأمر أبي حنيفة ، ومنها أنه ينبغي للأستاذ إذا تفرس في بعض أصحابه الخير أن يقدمه ويعظمه عند الناس حتى يعظموه، ومنها أن التلميذ لا ينبغي أن ينسى حرمة أستاذه وإن قدمه أستاذه وعظمه ألا ترى أن أبا يوسف شغله ذلك عن التكبير حتى سها قوله (وبالاقتداء يجب على المرأة والمسافر أي باقتدائهما بمن يجب عليه يجب عليهما بطريق التبعية. والمرأة تخافت بالتكبير لأن صوتها ،عورة، وكذا يجب على المسبوق لأنه مقتد تحريمة لكن لا يكبر مع الإمام ويكبر بعدما قضى ما فاته وفي الأصل: ولو تابعه لا تفسد صلاته وفي التلبية تفسد. كذا في الخلاصة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم بالصواب.
الظاهر، نعم بقي أن يقال من شرائطها الجماعة التي هي جمع والواحد هنا مع الإمام جماعة فكيف يصح أن يقال إن شروطه شروط الجمعة اهـ ؟ والجواب أن المراد الاشتراك في اشتراط الجماعة فيهما لا من كل وجه وإلا انتفض ما أجاب به وإلا فإن الشرط في الجمعة وقت الظهر فالاشتراك في اشتراط الوقت فيهما مطلقاً فكذا الجماعة تدبر قوله : (فقضاها فيها) أي في العام القابل في هذه الأيام قوله : (حتى لو سها) أي حيث نسي ما لا عادة حين علمه خلفه وذلك أن العادة إنما هو نسيان التكبير الأول وهو الكائن عقيب ينسي ا بعد توالي ثلاثة أوقات فلم تجر العادة بنسيانه لعدم بعد العهد به . كذا في الفتح .
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Eid Prayer. As for according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is obligatory upon everyone who prays the prescribed prayer because it is a follow-up to it, so it is obligatory upon the traveler, the woman, and the villager. It is said in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Jawhara: the fatwa is on their statement in this also. So the outcome is that the fatwa is on their statement regarding its last time and regarding who it is obligatory upon. And the author (Musannif) made absolute [the mention of] takbir after these prayers, so it includes performance and make-up (qada). It is four [cases], no takbir in three of them: the first: one missed it in other than the days of tashriq and made it up during them. The second: one missed it during these days and made it up in other than these days. The third: one missed it during these days and made it up during them in the following year. There is no takbir in the first two by agreement. In the third there is a difference of Abu Yusuf, and the correct [view] is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya). Takbir is only in the fourth: which is when one misses it during these days and makes it up during them in this same year, for he makes takbir because its time has arrived, like the udhiya. Then that which is performed after the prayer are three things: prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw), takbir al-tashriq, and talbiya. However, sajdah al-sahw is performed in the opening takbir (tahrimah) of following the forgetful one after his salam; and takbir is performed in its sanctity (hurmah) not in its opening takbir (tahrimah), even... [unclear]... it is not valid to follow the imam after salam before takbir. And talbiya is not performed in any of them. Hence it is said in al-Khulasa: The imam begins with sajdah al-sahw, then takbir, then talbiya if he is in ihram. In Fatawa al-Walwalji: If he begins with talbiya, the sajdah and takbir are dropped. And since it is not performed in its tahrimah, if the imam leaves it, the people must do it, like the listener to a verse of prostration with its reciter, unlike when the imam does not perform sajdah for forgetfulness, then they do not perform it. Ya'qub said: I prayed Maghrib on the day of Arafah and I forgot to make takbir with them, so Abu Hanifa made takbir with them. From this incident several things are derived: among them this issue; among them that glorification of his obedience is not in what he thinks is obedience, because Abu Yusuf proceeded by the command of Abu Hanifa; among them that it is fitting for a teacher, if he perceives goodness in some of his students, to advance him and honor him before people so that they honor him; among them that a student should not forget the respect of his teacher, even if his teacher advances and honors him. Do you not see that Abu Yusuf was occupied by that and so forgot the takbir? His statement: (And by following, it is obligatory upon the woman and the traveler) i.e., by their following one upon whom it is obligatory, it becomes obligatory upon them by way of followership. And the woman lowers her voice in takbir because her voice is 'awrah. Similarly, it is obligatory upon the masbuq because he is a follower in the tahrimah, but he does not make takbir with the imam; he makes takbir after he completes what he missed. In al-Asl: If he follows him in it, his prayer is not invalidated, but in talbiya it is invalidated. Thus in al-Khulasa. And Allah Most High knows best what is correct.
Apparently, yes, it remains to be said: among its conditions is the congregation (jama'ah), which is a group, and the one [person] here with the imam is a congregation. So how can it be said that its conditions are the conditions of Friday prayer? The answer: what is meant is the sharing in the condition of congregation in both, not from every aspect; otherwise the response would be invalid. Otherwise, the condition for Friday prayer is the time of Zuhr, so the sharing in the condition of time in both is absolute; likewise congregation. Reflect. His statement: (and makes it up during them) i.e., in the following year during these days. His statement: (even if he forgets) i.e., when he forgets what is not customary at the time of its knowledge behind him. That is because the custom is only forgetting the first takbir which occurs after... after the passing of three times, so forgetting it is not customary due to the recency of the time. Thus in al-Fath.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion of the ruling on Takbir al-Tashriq (the takbirs recited after the fard prayers from the dawn of the day of Arafah until the Asr of the last day of Tashriq). It addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to the disciples, this takbir is wajib (obligatory) upon every person who is obligated to pray the five daily prayers, including the traveler, woman, and villager. The fatwa is on their view. The author then explains four scenarios regarding qada (make-up) of the Eid prayer and the accompanying takbir: if a person misses the Eid prayer, the takbir is not required in three situations, but is required in the fourth (when missed during the days of Tashriq and made up in the same year). This is analogous to the udhiya sacrifice. The passage then discusses the order of actions performed after the prayer: sajdah al-sahw, takbir al-tashriq, and talbiya (during Hajj). The imam should do sajdah first, then takbir, then talbiya. If he starts with talbiya, the others are dropped. A historical anecdote about Abu Yusuf forgetting the takbir while leading prayer on the day of Arafah, and Abu Hanifa correcting him, yields several lessons: respecting the teacher, and the importance of following the prescribed order. Finally, it clarifies that women lower their voice in takbir, and a masbuq (latecomer) performs takbir after completing his missed rakats. The marginal note at the end addresses an objection about the conditions of Eid prayer being similar to those of Jumu'ah.

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (Takbir al-Tashriq): The takbirs recited after every fard prayer from Fajr of the day of Arafah until Asr of the last day of Tashriq.
قضاء (Qada): The make-up prayer for a missed fard prayer.
مسبوق (Masbuq): A latecomer who joins the congregation after the imam has already begun the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following qada scenarios is Takbir al-Tashriq required?
A) Missed prayer during Tashriq, made up outside Tashriq.
B) Missed prayer outside Tashriq, made up during Tashriq.
C) Missed prayer during Tashriq, made up in the following year's Tashriq.
D) Missed prayer during Tashriq, made up in the same year's Tashriq.

Key Takeaway
Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib on all obligated for fard prayer, but in qada it is only required when the missed prayer is made up within the same year's days of Tashriq.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

The Eclipse Prayer: Ruling, Description, and Proof
Expounds the ruling and manner of eclipse prayer with proof and intra-school difference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the eclipse prayer, describe its performance, and explain the evidence from the hadith as well as the intra-Hanafi difference with Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
The eclipse prayer is a sunnah muakkadah like nafl, two rakats with one ruku each, led by the Jumu'ah imam.

The eclipse of the sun or moon is a sign of Allah's power, and the Prophet ﷺ prescribed a specific prayer for such occasions. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on Salat al-Kusuf, its manner, the primary evidence, and a notable difference of opinion within the school. The key is understanding why it is classified as nafl and how its performance differs from other congregational prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text opens by stating the prayer is two rakats 'like nafl.' Determine the hukm level: is it fard, wajib, or sunnah? The Hanafi position is that it is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized supererogatory).
The hadith command 'sallu' is interpreted as recommendation, not obligation.
2
Understand the description
Note the specific features: no adhan, no iqama, no khutbah; it is announced 'al-salatu jamiah'; each rakat has one ruku and two sajdahs; it is not performed in disliked times; the imam of Jumu'ah leads; supplication continues until the eclipse clears.
The phrase 'like nafl' governs the entire description.
3
Examine the primary evidence
The hadith from Bukhari provides the basis: the sun and moon are signs of Allah, and when you see them, pray. Locate the command and note how Hanafi usul classifies it as zanni al-dalala, leading to sunnah rather than obligation.
The hadith itself is sahih, but its legal force is considered zanni in transmission (ahad) and in indication (command can be for obligation or recommendation).
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf held that the eclipse prayer should be like the Eid prayer, not like nafl. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad) maintain it is like nafl. Identify the key difference: Abu Yusuf's view likely involved extra takbirs or different structure.
The mufta bihi position is the majority view: like nafl.
5
Apply the recommended conditions
Qadi al-Usbijabi mentions three mustahabbat: the imam (sultan or judge), the time (when nafl is permissible), and the place (eidgah or congregational mosque). Consider the ruling if these are not met: prayer is still valid, but less preferred.
Individual prayer at home is permissible but disliked in groups per locality.

باب صلاة الكسوف
قوله : (وبه اندفع ما في السراج الخ قال في النهر : معنى قوله لا بد من شرائط الجمعة» أي

Chapter of Eclipse Prayer. He prays two rakats like supererogatory prayer (nafl), [led by] the imam of Jumu'ah, without raising voice and without sermon, then he supplicates until the sun clears. Chapter of Eclipse Prayer. Its suitability after Eid is that both are performed in congregation during the day without adhan or iqama. He delayed it after Eid because the Eid prayer is obligatory according to the correct view. It is said: 'kasafat al-shams' (the sun eclipsed) and 'kasafaha Allah' (God eclipsed it), transitive and intransitive. Jarir said in elegy for Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz: 'The sun is rising, not eclipsing; the stars of the night and the moon weep for you.' i.e., it does not eclipse the light of the stars with its rising due to the paucity of its light and its weeping for you, and because of that light appears from it. On this, his word 'stars' is in the accusative as object, and 'the moon' is conjoined. Its completion is in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. Some consider 'kusuf' for the sun and moon, and some consider 'kusuf' for the sun and 'khusuf' for the moon. The basis for the eclipse prayer is the hadith of Bukhari: 'The sun and the moon are not eclipsed for the death of anyone among people, but they are two signs from the signs of Allah. So when you see them, pray.' In another narration: 'So supplicate.' His statement: (prays two rakats like nafl, imam of Jumu'ah) is an explanation of its quantity and its manner of performance. As for its quantity, it is mentioned that it is two rakats; that is an explanation of the minimum. Hence it is said in al-Mujtaba: If they wish, they may pray it as two rakats, or four, or more, each two rakats with one taslim, or each four. As for its manner of performance, it is like the performance of nafl: each rakat with one ruku and two sajdahs; that there is no adhan for it, no iqama, and no sermon; rather it is announced 'al-salatu jamiah' (prayer is gathering) to gather if they have not gathered; that it is not prayed during the disliked times; and that it is not disliked to lengthen standing, ruku, sujud, supplications, and remembrances — which is from the characteristics of nawafil. He distinguished by his saying 'like nafl' from the statement of Abu Yusuf, for he said: like the form of the Eid prayer. And his restriction to 'imam of Jumu'ah' is an explanation of what is recommended. Qadi al-Usbijabi said: It is recommended in the solar eclipse three things: the imam, the time, and the place. As for the imam, it is the sultan or the judge and whoever has the authority to establish Jumu'ah and the two Eids. As for the time, it is that in which supererogatory prayer is permissible. And the place is where the Eid prayer is performed or the congregational mosque. If they pray in another place, it suffices them, but the first is better. If they pray individually in their homes, it is permissible, but it is disliked to gather in every district. End. And by this is refuted what is in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that mentioning the imam indicates... Chapter of Eclipse Prayer. His statement: (And by this is refuted what is in al-Siraj...) He said in al-Nahr: The meaning of his statement 'the conditions of Jumu'ah are necessary' i.e.... not completed.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on the Eclipse Prayer (Salat al-Kusuf). It opens with the ruling: the prayer is two rakats, performed like a voluntary (nafl) prayer, but led by the imam of Jumu'ah, without raising the voice (tajhir) and without a sermon (khutbah). After the prayer, one supplicates until the eclipse clears. The commentator then explains the connection to the previous chapter (Eid), noting that both are performed in congregation during the day without adhan or iqama. The hadith from Bukhari is cited as the primary evidence: the sun and moon are signs of Allah, not eclipsed for anyone's death; when you see an eclipse, pray. The description of the prayer is detailed: it is at minimum two rakats, but can be more (four, six, etc.) each pair with a taslim. Each rakat has one ruku and two sajdahs, like nafl. There is no adhan, iqama, or khutbah; instead the call 'al-salatu jamiah' is made. It is not prayed during disliked times. There is a disagreement with Abu Yusuf who said it should be like the Eid prayer (with takbirs?). The preferred view is that it is like nafl. The Qadi al-Usbijabi mentions three recommended things: the imam (the sultan or judge), the time (when nafl is permissible), and the place (the musalla of Eid or the congregational mosque). Individual prayer at home is permissible but disliked in groups in every locality. The passage ends with a refutation of a point in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, but the text is cut off.

Key Terms
الكسوف (al-Kusuf): The eclipse of the sun or the moon; lexically both are called kusuf, but some distinguish kusuf for sun and khusuf for moon.
النفل (al-Nafl): Supererogatory prayer; voluntary worship beyond the obligatory.
إمام الجمعة (Imam al-Jumu'ah): The imam who leads the Friday prayer; in the context of eclipse prayer, it is recommended that he leads, but not required.
الصلاة جامعة (al-Salatu Jamiah): The announcement made to gather people for the eclipse prayer; equivalent to 'prayer is gathering'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Four rakats with one taslim, like the Eid prayer
D) Two rakats with audible recitation and a sermon after the prayer

Key Takeaway
The eclipse prayer is a sunnah muakkadah performed as two rakats like nafl, led by an imam, without adhan/iqama/khutbah, and with supplication until the eclipse clears.

Eclipse Prayer: Sunnah Status and Form
Detailed legal analysis of solar eclipse prayer including form, conditions, and internal disagreements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eclipse prayer, explain its form (like nafl), and distinguish between the majority view (sunnah mu'akkadah) and the minority view (wajib).

Core Idea
Eclipse prayer is sunnah mu'akkadah, performed silently like nafl, without sermon, led by the jumu'ah imam.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks the rulings for the solar eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf). It confirms the prayer's form is like supererogatory prayer (nafl), but its legal status is debated: the majority hold it is an emphasized sunnah, while some Hanafis consider it wajib. The commentary also clarifies that recitation is silent, there is no sermon, and the imam of jumu'ah leads if possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The matn states the prayer is two rak'ahs 'like nafl.' The hadith from Bukhari provides the proof. Determine whether the imperative 'pray' indicates obligation or recommendation.
The Hanafi usul principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub unless diverted.
2
Analyze the internal Hanafi dispute on wujub vs sunnah
Muhammad al-Shaybani's placement in al-Asl among nafl suggests non-obligation. The majority view is sunnah mu'akkadah because it is not a constant ritual. A minority (author of al-Asrar) held wajib.
The majority tarjih is based on the accidental nature of eclipses.
3
Examine the form: silent recitation vs loud
The matn says 'without loud recitation' because it is daytime nafl. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and al-Shafi'i argued for loudness based on Ibn 'Abbas' hadith. The Hanafi response: the hadith does not explicitly state loudness; estimation of length would be unnecessary if loud.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf): Hanafi prays silently, Shafi'i loudly.
4
Understand the conditions: imam, time, place
The imam of jumu'ah is recommended. Time must be permissible for voluntary prayer (not disliked times). Place is the musalla or large mosque. If imam absent, individuals pray separately.
The refutation of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: all conditions of jumu'ah are not required.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical application
The relied-upon position is sunnah mu'akkadah, silent recitation, no sermon, supplication after prayer until the eclipse ends. If the imam of jumu'ah is not present, pray individually.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa in the Hanafi school.

أنه لا بد من شرائط الجمعة وهو كذلك إلا الخطبة اهـ . لكن جعله الوقت من المستحبات لا يصح لأنه لا تجوز الصلاة في الأوقات المكروهة ولم يبين المصنف رحمه الله صفتها من الوجوب والسنية. وقد ذكر في البدائع قولين وذكر محمد في الأصل ما يدل على عدم الوجوب فإنه قال : ولا تصلى نافلة في جماعة إلا قيام رمضان وصلاة الكسوف استثناها من النافلة، والمستثنى من جنس المستثنى منه فدل على كونها نافلة، لكن مطلق الأمر في قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «فصلوا» يدل على الوجوب إلا لصارف وما قد يتوهم من أنه ذكره مع قوله «وادعوا» فإن الدعاء ليس بواجب إجماعاً فكذا الصلاة غير صحيح لأن القرآن في النظم لا يوجب القرآن في
الحكم.
قوله : (بلا جهر تصريح بما علم من قوله كالنفل لأن النفل النهاري لا يكون جهراً لدفع قولهما من الجهر لحديث ابن عباس : صلى بنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الكسوف فقام بنا قياماً طويلاً نحواً من سورة البقرة ولوجهر لما احتيج إلى الحزر، وقد تركنا الدلائل الكثيرة في هذا الباب والكلام مع الشافعي والصاحبين روماً للاختصار قال في المجتبى: وأما قدر القراءة فيها فروي أنه عليه السلام قام في الركعة الأولى بقدر سورة البقرة، وفي الثانية بقدر سورة آل عمران، فإن طول القراءة خفف الدعاء أو على العكس .اهـ. قوله : (وخطبة) أي بلا خطبة لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أمر بها ولم يبين الخطبة، وما ورد من خطبته يوم مات إبراهيم وكسفت الشمس فإنما كان للرد على من قال إنها كسفت لموته لا لأنها مشروعة له، ولذا خطب بعد الانجلاء ولو كانت سنة له الخطب قبله كالصلاة والدعاء قوله : (ثم يدعو حتى تنجليي الشمس) أي يدعو الإمام والناس معه حتى تنجلي الشمس للحديث المتقدم. أطلقه فأفاد أن الداعي مخير إن شاء دعا جالساً مستقبل القبلة وإن شاء دعا قائماً يستقبل الناس بوجهه. قال الحلواني وهذا أحسن ولو قام ودعا معتمداً على عصا أو قوس كان أيضاً حسناً . وأفاد بكلمة «ثم» أن السنة تأخير الدعاء الصلاة لأنه عن هو السنة في الأدعية. وفي المحيط : ولا يصعد الإمام على المنبر للدعاء ولا يخرج قوله : (وإلا صلوها فرادى) أي إن لم يحضر إمام الجمعة صلى الناس فرادى تحرزاً عن الفتنة إذ هي تقام بجمع عظيم. وروي عن أبي حنيفة أن لكل إمام مسجد أن يصلي بجماعة والصحيح ظاهر الرواية لأن أداء هذه
في تحصيل كمال السنة ، نعم ظاهر ما قاله الأسبيجابي يفيد أنه لو صلاها عند الاستواء صحت فتدبره قوله : ( فدل على كونها نافلة) ذكر في البدائع الجواب عنه وهو أن تسمية محمد إياها نافلة لا ينفي الوجوب لأن النافلة عبارة عن الزيادة وكل واجب زيادة على الفرائض الموظفة اهـ . قلت : لي فيه نظر فإنه إذا كان المراد من النافلة الزائد على الفرائض يلزم عليه خروج العيد مع أنها لا تصلى بدون جماعة. وفي العناية : ذهب إلى وجوبها بعض أصحابنا واختاره صاحب الأسرار والعامة ذهبت إلى كونها سنة لأنها ليست من شعائر الإسلام فإنها توجد
بعارض لكن صلاها النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم فكانت سنة والأمر للندب .
Book of Prayer, Chapter on Eclipse Prayer
Chapter on Eclipse Prayer
291
He prays two rak'ahs like nafl, the imam of jumu'ah, without loud recitation and without sermon, then he makes supplication until the sun clears.
Chapter on Eclipse Prayer
Its appropriateness to 'Eid is that each is performed in congregation during the day without adhan or iqamah. He placed it after 'Eid because 'Eid prayer is obligatory according to the correct view. It is said: kasafat al-shams (the sun eclipsed) - it eclipses, eclipse; and kasafaha Allah (God caused it to eclipse) - transitive and intransitive. Jarir said in his elegy for 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz:

The sun is rising, not eclipsed, weeping for you, the stars of night and the moon.
Meaning it does not eclipse the light of the stars with its rising due to the weakness of their light and its weeping for you, and because of that its light appears. So according to this, his word (stars) is in the accusative as the object, and (the moon) is conjoined to it. The complete explanation is in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. Some make kusuf for the sun and moon, and some make kusuf for the sun and khusuf for the moon. The basis for eclipse prayer is the hadith of al-Bukhari: 'The sun and moon are not eclipsed for the death of anyone among people, but they are two signs among the signs of Allah; so when you see them, pray.' And in another narration: 'So supplicate.' His statement: (He prays two rak'ahs like nafl, the imam of jumu'ah) is an explanation of its amount and its manner of performance. As for its amount, he mentioned that it is two rak'ahs, which is an explanation of the minimum. Hence it is said in al-Mujtaba: If they wish, they may pray it as two rak'ahs or four or more, each two rak'ahs with one taslim, or each four. As for its manner of performance, it is the manner of performing nafl: each rak'ah with one bowing and two prostrations; and that there is no adhan for it, no iqamah, no sermon; and the call 'al-salat jami'ah' is made so that they gather if they have not already gathered; and that it is not prayed in disliked times; and that lengthening the standing, bowing, prostrations, supplications, and remembrances is not disliked, which is among the characteristics of supererogatory prayers. He restricted by his saying 'like nafl' (to exclude) the statement of Abu Yusuf, for he said: in the manner of 'Eid prayer. And his restriction to the imam of jumu'ah is an explanation of what is recommended. Al-Qadi al-Isbijabi said: For the solar eclipse prayer, three things are recommended: the imam, the time, and the place. As for the imam, it is the sultan or the judge or whoever has authority to establish jumu'ah and the two 'Eids. As for the time, it is the time in which voluntary prayer is permissible. And the place is where 'Eid prayer is performed or the congregational mosque. If they pray in another place, it suffices them, but the first is better. And if they pray individually in their homes, it is permissible, and it is disliked to gather in every locality. End. And by this is refuted what is in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that the mention of imam indicates the necessity of the conditions of jumu'ah. (His statement: (And by this is refuted what is in al-Siraj...) He said in al-Nahr: The meaning of his statement 'the conditions of jumu'ah are necessary' - i.e., except the sermon. But making the time among the recommended is not correct because prayer is not permitted in disliked times. And the author, may Allah have mercy on him, did not clarify its status of obligation or sunnah. It has been mentioned in al-Bada'i' that there are two opinions. Muhammad mentioned in al-Asl what indicates non-obligation, for he said: No supererogatory prayer is performed in congregation except qiyam Ramadan and the eclipse prayer, he excluded it from supererogatory prayers, and what is excluded is of the same kind as that from which it is excluded, so that indicates it is supererogatory. But the absolute command in his saying, peace be upon him, 'Pray' indicates obligation unless there is a diverting factor. And what might be imagined - that he mentioned it together with his saying 'and supplicate' - supplication is not obligatory by consensus, so likewise prayer - is not valid because parallelism in wording does not require parallelism in ruling.
His statement: (without loud recitation) is clarification of what is known from his saying 'like nafl' because daytime nafl is not loud, to refute the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding loudness due to the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, led us in the eclipse prayer and stood with us for a long recitation, about the length of Surah al-Baqarah. And if it were loud, there would be no need to estimate. And we have left out many proofs in this chapter and the discussion with al-Shafi'i and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) for the sake of brevity. He said in al-Mujtaba: As for the amount of recitation in it, it is narrated that he, peace be upon him, stood in the first rak'ah for the length of Surah al-Baqarah, and in the second for the length of Surah Al 'Imran. If he lengthens the recitation, he shortens the supplication, or vice versa. End. His statement: (and sermon) i.e., without sermon because he, peace be upon him, commanded it but did not explain a sermon. And what is narrated of his sermon on the day when Ibrahim died and the sun eclipsed was only to refute those who said it eclipsed for his death, not because it is prescribed for it. Hence he delivered the sermon after the clearing. If it were a sunnah for it, he would have delivered the sermon before it, like the prayer and supplication. His statement: (Then he makes supplication until the sun clears) i.e., the imam and the people with him make supplication until the sun clears, due to the hadith mentioned earlier. He left it unrestricted, so it indicates that the supplicant has a choice: if he wishes, he may supplicate sitting, facing the qiblah; and if he wishes, he may supplicate standing, facing the people. Al-Halwani said: This is better. And if he stands and supplicates leaning on a staff or a bow, that is also good. And by the word 'then' it indicates that it is sunnah to delay the supplication after the prayer, because that is the sunnah in supplications. In al-Muhit: The imam does not ascend the pulpit for the supplication, nor does he go out. His statement: (Otherwise they pray individually) i.e., if the imam of jumu'ah is not present, the people pray individually to avoid mischief, since it would be established with a large gathering. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifah that every imam of a mosque may pray in congregation, but the correct is the apparent transmission because the performance of this (prayer) is for attaining complete sunnah. Indeed, the apparent meaning of what al-Isbijabi said indicates that if one prays it at the time of (the sun's) zenith, it is valid, so ponder it. His statement: (So it indicates it is supererogatory) Al-Bada'i' mentions a response to it: that Muhammad's calling it nafl does not negate obligation, because nafl means an increase, and every obligatory act is an increase upon the prescribed obligatory duties. End. I say: I have a consideration regarding this: if the meaning of nafl is what is additional to the obligatory duties, then it would necessitate the exclusion of 'Eid prayer, even though it is not performed without a congregation. And in al-'Inayah: Some of our companions held that it is obligatory, and it was chosen by the author of al-Asrar, but the majority held that it is sunnah because it is not among the distinctive rituals of Islam, as it occurs due to an accident, but the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, prayed it, so it became a sunnah, and the command is for recommendation.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, provides a detailed analysis of the solar eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf). The passage type is a ruling with proof, as it states the legal ruling and supports it with hadith evidence.

The chapter opens by explaining the suitability of placing this chapter after the chapter on 'Eid prayer: both are performed in congregation during the day without adhan or iqamah, but 'Eid prayer is given precedence because it is obligatory according to the correct view.

The author then clarifies the linguistic aspect of the term 'kusuf', quoting a poetic verse and noting that some scholars differentiate between 'kusuf' (for sun and moon) and 'khusuf' (for moon only).

The primary proof for the eclipse prayer is the hadith from al-Bukhari: 'The sun and moon are not eclipsed for the death of anyone... but they are two signs of Allah; so when you see them, pray.' Another narration adds 'and supplicate.'

The matn states: 'He prays two rak'ahs like nafl, the imam of jumu'ah, without loud recitation and without sermon, then he makes supplication until the sun clears.' The commentary expands each element.

Regarding the amount: the minimum is two rak'ahs, but more may be added: two, four, or more, each two rak'ahs with one taslim (as per the Hanafi method) or each four.

The manner of performance is like nafl (supererogatory prayer): each rak'ah has one ruku' and two sajdahs. There is no adhan or iqamah; instead, the call 'al-salatu jami'ah' is proclaimed to gather the people. It is not performed in disliked times. Lengthening the qiyam, ruku', sujud, and supplications is not disliked, which is a characteristic of nafl.

The author notes that the phrase 'like nafl' excludes the view of Abu Yusuf, who held it should be performed like the 'Eid prayer (with two rak'ahs and additional takbirs). The Hanafi school follows the nafl model.

The qualification 'imam of jumu'ah' indicates that it is recommended (mustahabb) for the prayer to be led by the imam who leads the Friday prayer, i.e., the sultan, judge, or whoever has authority to establish Friday and 'Eid prayers. Three things are recommended: the imam, the time (when voluntary prayers are permissible), and the place (the 'Eid prayer ground or the large mosque). If they pray elsewhere it suffices. Praying individually at home is permissible but disliked if it causes gatherings in every locality.

The commentary refutes a point from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that the mention of imam implies all conditions of jumu'ah (like 40 men, etc.). The correct view is that only the imam condition applies, except for the sermon (khutbah). The commentator also objects to considering the time as merely recommended, because eclipse prayer cannot be performed in the disliked times (e.g., sunrise, zenith, sunset); it is not valid then.

The author then discusses whether the eclipse prayer is wajib (obligatory) or sunnah. He notes that the author of Kanz did not specify. In al-Bada'i', two opinions are mentioned. Muhammad al-Shaybani's statement in al-Asl appears to indicate non-obligation: he said that no nafl is prayed in congregation except qiyam Ramadan and eclipse prayer. Since what is excluded is from the same category, it suggests eclipse prayer is nafl (supererogatory). However, the absolute command in the hadith 'pray' indicates obligation unless there is a diverting factor. Some might argue that since the Prophet mentioned 'pray' alongside 'supplicate', and supplication is not obligatory, prayer is also not obligatory. But this argument is invalid because parallelism in wording does not require parallelism in ruling.

The commentary then addresses the issue of loud recitation. The matn says 'without loud recitation,' consistent with nafl, which in daytime is silent. This refutes the view of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and al-Shafi'i, who held that it should be loud based on the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas where the Prophet recited a long qira'ah. The Hanafi response is that if it were loud, there would be no need to estimate the length; the hadith does not explicitly state loudness. The recitation length is recommended but not fixed; one may lengthen recitation and shorten supplication or vice versa.

Regarding the sermon, the matn says 'without sermon.' The Prophet commanded the prayer but did not prescribe a sermon. The incident where he delivered a sermon after an eclipse during the death of his son Ibrahim was to refute the claim that the eclipse was for his death, not to establish a sunnah for the prayer. If it were sunnah, he would have done it before the prayer.

Supplication: after the prayer, the imam and people supplicate until the sun clears, based on the hadith. The supplicant may sit facing the qiblah or stand facing the people. The word 'then' indicates the sunnah is to delay supplication until after the prayer. The imam does not ascend the pulpit nor go out for the supplication.

If the imam of jumu'ah is not present, the people pray individually to avoid mischief of gathering in large crowds. There is a narration from Abu Hanifa that any imam of a mosque may lead the congregation, but the relied-upon view (zahir al-riwayah) is that it should be led by the imam of jumu'ah for the completion of sunnah. The commentator notes that al-Isbijabi's statement implies one may pray at the time of zenith (against the general rule of disliked times), and this should be considered.

Finally, the commentary returns to the obligation issue. In al-Bada'i', a response is given to Muhammad's argument: calling it nafl does not negate obligation because nafl etymologically means 'increase,' and every obligatory act is an increase upon the prescribed obligatory acts. However, the commentator objects that if nafl means what is additional to the fara'id, then 'Eid prayer would be excluded from this definition since it is obligatory but not nafl. In al-'Inayah, the view of obligation is attributed to some Hanafi scholars (e.g., the author of al-Asrar), but the majority hold it is sunnah because it is not a constant ritual of Islam—it arises due to an accident. The Prophet's performing it makes it a sunnah, and the command is interpreted as recommendation (nadb) rather than obligation. The authority weight of the majority view is stronger in the later tradition.

Key Terms
كسوف (kusūf): Eclipse of the sun (and sometimes the moon). Some scholars differentiate between kusuf (sun) and khusuf (moon).
نافلة (nāfilah): Supererogatory prayer; a voluntary act of worship. In this context, the eclipse prayer is described 'like nafl' in form (manner, time) but its legal status may be different.
إمام الجمعة (imām al-jumuʿah): The imam who leads Friday prayer; the person with authority to lead the eclipse prayer, preferably the sultan, judge, or one appointed for jumu'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) ruling regarding the status of the eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf)?
A) It is wajib (obligatory) based on the absolute command in the hadith.
B) It is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah) because it is not a constant ritual.
C) It is nafl (supererogatory) and may be performed at any time.
D) It is fard kifayah (community obligation) like Friday prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that eclipse prayer is sunnah mu'akkadah, performed silently like nafl, without sermon, led by the jumu'ah imam if possible, followed by supplication until the eclipse ends.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Ruling of Eclipse Prayer: Obligatory or Sunnah?
Analyzing whether eclipse prayer is wajib or sunnah with proofs from al-Asl and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on the ruling of eclipse prayer and identify the mufta bihi position with its evidence.

Core Idea
The eclipse prayer is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib, because it is not a constant symbol of Islam and the command is interpreted as recommendation.

The eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf) is a prayer performed during a solar or lunar eclipse. While the command to pray is clear, the Hanafi school debated whether it is obligatory (wajib) or recommended (sunnah). This lesson unpacks the key arguments from the text, focusing on the classification of the prayer as nafila and the interpretation of the Prophet's command. By working through this intra-Hanafi dispute, you will understand how different proofs are weighed to arrive at the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the exact legal question: Is eclipse prayer wajib or sunnah? Note that both positions exist within the Hanafi school.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not a cross-madhhab dispute.
2
Identify the majority position and its proof
The majority (al-ammah) hold it sunnah. Their main proof: Imam Muhammad classified it as nafila in al-Asl, and the Prophet's action established it as sunnah, not a constant symbol.
Look for the phrase 'العامة ذهبت إلى كونها سنة'.
3
Identify the minority position and its proof
Some early Hanafis (e.g., author of al-Asrar) held it wajib. Their proof: the absolute command 'fajilu' (pray) in the hadith indicates obligation unless diverted.
The command is paired with 'ud'u' (supplicate), but conjunction in wording does not necessitate conjunction in ruling.
4
Analyze the key arguments
Examine the nafila argument: if eclipse prayer is excepted from nafila, it is of the same genus. But 'nafila' can mean any increase, including wajib. Consider the counter-argument about Eid prayer.
The author critiques the 'nafila as increase' argument because it would also exclude Eid prayer, which is not without congregation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is sunnah mu'akkadah, as stated in al-Inayah and supported by the generality of Hanafis. The minority wajib view is not practiced.
The practical consequence: no sin for leaving it, but it is highly recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنه لا بد من شرائط الجمعة وهو كذلك إلا الخطبة اهـ . لكن جعله الوقت من المستحبات لا يصح لأنه لا تجوز الصلاة في الأوقات المكروهة ولم يبين المصنف رحمه الله صفتها من الوجوب والسنية. وقد ذكر في البدائع قولين وذكر محمد في الأصل ما يدل على عدم الوجوب فإنه قال : ولا تصلى نافلة في جماعة إلا قيام رمضان وصلاة الكسوف استثناها من النافلة، والمستثنى من جنس المستثنى منه فدل على كونها نافلة، لكن مطلق الأمر في قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «فصلوا» يدل على الوجوب إلا لصارف وما قد يتوهم من أنه ذكره مع قوله «وادعوا» فإن الدعاء ليس بواجب إجماعاً فكذا الصلاة غير صحيح لأن القرآن في النظم لا يوجب القرآن في الحكم.
قوله : (فدل على كونها نافلة) ذكر في البدائع الجواب عنه وهو أن تسمية محمد إياها نافلة لا ينفي الوجوب لأن النافلة عبارة عن الزيادة وكل واجب زيادة على الفرائض الموظفة اهـ . قلت : لي فيه نظر فإنه إذا كان المراد من النافلة الزائد على الفرائض يلزم عليه خروج العيد مع أنها لا تصلى بدون جماعة. وفي العناية : ذهب إلى وجوبها بعض أصحابنا واختاره صاحب الأسرار والعامة ذهبت إلى كونها سنة لأنها ليست من شعائر الإسلام فإنها توجد بعارض لكن صلاها النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم فكانت سنة والأمر للندب .
That the conditions of Friday prayer are necessary, and it is so except the sermon. But making the time from the recommended acts is not correct because prayer is not permissible in disliked times, and the author did not clarify its nature of obligation or sunnah. In al-Badai' two opinions are mentioned, and Muhammad mentioned in al-Asl what indicates non-obligation, for he said: No supererogatory prayer is performed in congregation except Ramadan vigil and eclipse prayer. He exempted it from supererogatory prayer, and the exempted is of the same genus as the exempted from, so it indicates it is supererogatory. However, the absolute command in his saying (peace be upon him) 'Pray' indicates obligation unless there is a diverting factor. And what may be imagined that he mentioned it with his saying 'And supplicate' and supplication is not obligatory by consensus, so likewise prayer is not correct because conjunction in wording does not necessitate conjunction in ruling. His statement: 'So it indicates it is supererogatory' – mention in al-Badai' the answer to it: that Muhammad's calling it supererogatory does not negate obligation because supererogatory means increase, and every obligatory is an increase over the stipulated obligatory acts. I said: I have a consideration in this, for if supererogatory means the increase over the obligatory, then it would necessitate the exclusion of Eid prayer, though it is not performed without congregation. And in al-Inayah: Some of our companions held it obligatory, and the author of al-Asrar chose it, but the general public went to it being sunnah because it is not among the symbols of Islam, for it occurs due to an accident. But the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed it, so it became sunnah, and the command is for recommendation.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the legal status of the eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf). The author begins by noting that the conditions for Friday prayer apply to eclipse prayer except the sermon. He criticizes the claim that time is mustahabb because prayer is not allowed in disliked times. The author then presents two opinions from al-Badai' and cites Imam Muhammad's statement in al-Asl that eclipse prayer is nafila (supererogatory), using the argument that exception from nafila indicates it is nafila. However, the general command 'pray' in the hadith suggests obligation. The objection that the command is paired with 'supplicate' which is not obligatory is refuted because conjunction in wording does not require conjunction in ruling. In al-Badai', the answer is that calling it nafila does not negate obligation since nafila can mean any increase, and every wajib is an increase over the fara'id. The author finds this problematic because it would exclude Eid prayer which is also not without congregation. Finally, al-Inayah reports that some Hanafis held it wajib, but the majority consider it sunnah because it is not a constant symbol and occurred due to an accident, so the Prophet's action made it sunnah and the command is for recommendation.

Key Terms
نافلة (nafilah): In this text, nafilah is used by Imam Muhammad to mean supererogatory prayer, but the author argues it can also mean an increase (ziyadah) that includes wajib. The context is that Muhammad said 'no nafila in congregation except...' implying eclipse prayer is nafila.
الوجوب والسنية (al-wujub wa al-sunniyyah): The two possible legal statuses: obligation (fard or wajib) and sunnah (recommended). The text discusses whether eclipse prayer is wajib (obligatory) or sunnah (recommended).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafis as stated in this passage, what is the ruling of eclipse prayer?
A) It is wajib (obligatory).
B) It is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah).
C) It is haram (forbidden).
D) It is makruh (disliked).

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that eclipse prayer is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib, due to its accidental nature and not being a constant symbol of Islam.

Recitation in Eclipse Prayer: Silent Mode and Length
Inter-madhhab dispute on recitation mode with additional ruling on length.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rules that eclipse prayer is recited silently and state the recommended length of recitation.

Core Idea
Eclipse prayer is like daytime nafila: recited silently, and its recitation length is estimated from the Prophet's practice.

The eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf) is a confirmed sunnah, but its mode of recitation has been a point of scholarly debate. In this passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq, the author clarifies the Hanafi position that it is recited silently, like any daytime supererogatory prayer. He also provides the recommended length of recitation based on the Prophet's practice. Understanding the evidence and the response to opposing views will sharpen your ability to weigh proofs in fiqh disputes.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on recitation mode
Identify the explicit ruling: eclipse prayer is recited without loud recitation (bila jahr). The author says this is implied by the matn's wording 'like nafila' because daytime nafila is always silent.
The matn is a concise legal text; the sharh expands it.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that eclipse prayer is recited aloud. Their proof is the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas where the Prophet stood a long time, and they estimated the recitation to be like Surah al-Baqarah.
This hadith is the main textual evidence for loud recitation.
3
Analyse the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response is that the estimation (hazr) itself proves silent recitation: if it were loud, the companions would have known the exact surah, not estimated. Therefore, the hadith actually supports silence.
This is a clever use of the same hadith to refute the opposing view.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to Hanafis, reciting aloud in eclipse prayer makes the prayer valid but disliked (makruh). For Shafi'is, jahr is sunnah. This difference affects the merit of the prayer.
The dispute does not affect validity, only desirability.
5
Identify the recommended length of recitation
The passage from al-Mujtaba states that the Prophet stood in the first rak'ah for the length of Surah al-Baqarah and in the second for Surah Al 'Imran. If recitation is long, supplication is shortened, and vice versa.
This is a recommended amount, not obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بلا جهر تصريح بما علم من قوله كالنفل لأن النفل النهاري لا يكون جهراً لدفع قولهما من الجهر لحديث ابن عباس : صلى بنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الكسوف فقام بنا قياماً طويلاً نحواً من سورة البقرة ولوجهر لما احتيج إلى الحزر، وقد تركنا الدلائل الكثيرة في هذا الباب والكلام مع الشافعي والصاحبين روماً للاختصار قال في المجتبى: وأما قدر القراءة فيها فروي أنه عليه السلام قام في الركعة الأولى بقدر سورة البقرة، وفي الثانية بقدر سورة آل عمران، فإن طول القراءة خفف الدعاء أو على العكس .اهـ.
His statement: (without loud recitation) is a clarification of what is known from his statement 'like nafila' because daytime nafila is not recited loudly, to refute the statement of the two (companions) regarding loud recitation due to the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) led us in eclipse prayer and stood with us for a long standing, about the length of Surah al-Baqarah. And if he had recited loudly, there would be no need for estimation. And we have left many evidences in this chapter and the discussion with al-Shafi'i and the two companions for the sake of brevity. He said in al-Mujtaba: As for the amount of recitation in it, it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) stood in the first rak'ah for the amount of Surah al-Baqarah, and in the second for the amount of Surah Al 'Imran. So if the recitation is long, he shortened the supplication, or vice versa.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues: the mode of recitation (silent vs loud) and the length of recitation in eclipse prayer. The author explains that the matn's phrase 'without loud recitation' makes explicit what was implied by likening it to nafila (supererogatory prayer) because daytime nafila is always recited silently. This is to refute the view of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Imam al-Shafi'i, who held that eclipse prayer should be recited aloud based on the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas. The Hanafi response is that the hadith mentions a long standing, which required estimation of the recitation; if it were loud, there would be no need for estimation. The author mentions that many evidences are omitted for brevity. Then, quoting al-Mujtaba, he states that the Prophet stood in the first rak'ah for the length of Surah al-Baqarah and in the second for Surah Al 'Imran. The recitation and supplication are inversely related: longer recitation means shorter supplication.

Key Terms
جهر (jahr): Loud recitation audible to others. In eclipse prayer, the Hanafi school holds that it is not recited loudly.
حزر (hazr): Estimation or approximation. In the hadith, the companions estimated the length of the Prophet's recitation, indicating they could not determine the exact surah because it was recited silently.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis argue that eclipse prayer should be recited silently (sirr) rather than aloud (jahr)?
A) Because the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas states that the Prophet recited aloud.
B) Because daytime nafila is always recited silently and eclipse prayer is like nafila.
C) Because loud recitation is forbidden in all prayers.
D) Because the companions could not estimate the recitation if it were silent.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that eclipse prayer is recited silently, with the recitation length approximating one long surah per rak'ah, and any loud recitation renders the prayer valid but disliked.

No Sermon in Eclipse Prayer
Explaining that there is no sermon in eclipse prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sermon in eclipse prayer and identify the proof from the Prophet's action.

Core Idea
Eclipse prayer has no sermon — the Prophet prescribed the prayer but not the sermon.

In this passage, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a common misconception: that the Prophet's sermon during an eclipse established a sermon for eclipse prayer. He clarifies that the sermon was a response to a false belief, not a ritual component. Understanding this distinction is key to applying the Hanafi ruling correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act under discussion is delivering a sermon during the eclipse prayer. The ruling is that it is not part of the prayer.
The passage states the prayer is 'bila khutbah' (without a sermon).
2
Examine the primary proof
The Prophet commanded the eclipse prayer but did not explain or mention a sermon. This silence indicates it is not prescribed.
The text: 'li-annahu amara biha wa lam yubayyin al-khutbah'.
3
Analyze the secondary proof
The Prophet gave a sermon on the day of the eclipse when his son Ibrahim died, but he delivered it after the eclipse cleared, not before. This timing proves it was not part of the prayer ritual.
If it were sunnah, it would have preceded the prayer like the prayer and supplication.
4
Conclude the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that there is no sermon in eclipse prayer. Adding a sermon would be an innovation.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وخطبة) أي بلا خطبة لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أمر بها ولم يبين الخطبة، وما ورد من خطبته يوم مات إبراهيم وكسفت الشمس فإنما كان للرد على من قال إنها كسفت لموته لا لأنها مشروعة له، ولذا خطب بعد الانجلاء ولو كانت سنة له الخطب قبله كالصلاة والدعاء
His statement: (and a sermon) i.e., without a sermon, because he (peace be upon him) commanded the prayer but did not explain the sermon. And what is reported of his sermon on the day Ibrahim died and the sun eclipsed was only to refute those who said the eclipse occurred due to his death, not because a sermon is prescribed for eclipse prayer. Hence, he delivered the sermon after the eclipse cleared. If it had been a sunnah for the eclipse prayer, he would have delivered it before it, like the prayer and supplication.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage explains that eclipse prayer is performed without a sermon (khutbah). The author argues that the Prophet commanded the prayer but did not mention a sermon, indicating none. The incident where the Prophet gave a sermon when his son Ibrahim died and the sun eclipsed was an exception: he spoke to correct the misconception that the eclipse was due to Ibrahim's death. He gave the sermon after the eclipse, not before, proving it was not part of the eclipse prayer ritual. If a sermon were sunnah, it would precede the prayer, just as the prayer and supplication are performed before the eclipse clears.

Key Terms
خطبة (khutbah): Sermon delivered by the imam. In eclipse prayer, it is not prescribed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the Prophet forbade sermons during eclipses.
B) Because the Prophet commanded the prayer but not the sermon.
C) Because the sermon is only for Friday and Eid.
D) Because the sermon would invalidate the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Eclipse prayer is performed without a sermon because the Prophet prescribed the prayer but did not include a sermon.

Supplication After Eclipse Prayer: Rulings and Postures
Describing the ruling of supplication after eclipse prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of supplication after eclipse prayer and identify the permissible postures for the imam.

Core Idea
Supplication after eclipse prayer is sunnah; the imam may sit or stand, but should not ascend the minbar.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author explains the supplication after eclipse prayer. He clarifies that it is a sunnah act to be performed after the prayer, with flexibility in posture. The imam may choose to sit facing the qiblah or stand facing the congregation. Notably, the imam should not ascend the minbar for this supplication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? What is the hukm (sunnah muakkadah)?
The act is du'a after eclipse prayer, and it is sunnah, not wajib.
2
Determine the sequence
The word 'thumma' (then) indicates that the supplication comes after the prayer. What does this tell us about the timing?
The supplication is delayed until after the prayer, following the general sunnah.
3
Analyze the optional postures
What are the permissible postures for the imam? List the options mentioned in the text.
Sitting facing qiblah or standing facing the people; leaning on a stick or bow is also good.
4
Note the prohibition
What is the imam prohibited from doing?
He should not ascend the minbar nor go out (of the mosque) for the supplication.
5
Summarize the evidence
What is the basis for these rulings? The passage refers to a 'previously mentioned hadith' and general practice.
The hadith is not quoted but the ruling is derived from it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم يدعو حتى تنجليي الشمس) أي يدعو الإمام والناس معه حتى تنجلي الشمس للحديث المتقدم. أطلقه فأفاد أن الداعي مخير إن شاء دعا جالساً مستقبل القبلة وإن شاء دعا قائماً يستقبل الناس بوجهه. قال الحلواني وهذا أحسن ولو قام ودعا معتمداً على عصا أو قوس كان أيضاً حسناً . وأفاد بكلمة «ثم» أن السنة تأخير الدعاء الصلاة لأنه عن هو السنة في الأدعية. وفي المحيط : ولا يصعد الإمام على المنبر للدعاء ولا يخرج
His statement: (then he supplicates until the sun clears) i.e., the imam and the people with him supplicate until the sun clears, based on the previously mentioned hadith. He made it absolute, so it indicates that the supplicant has a choice: if he wishes, he can supplicate while sitting facing the qiblah, and if he wishes, he can supplicate while standing facing the people. Al-Halwani said: This is better. And if he stood and supplicated leaning on a stick or a bow, it would also be good. And he indicated with the word 'then' that the sunnah is to delay the supplication after the prayer, because that is the sunnah in supplications. And in al-Muhit: The imam should not ascend the minbar for supplication, nor should he go out.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage explains the supplication (du'a) after the eclipse prayer. The imam and the congregation make supplication until the sun clears. The author notes that the phrase 'then' indicates that the supplication comes after the prayer, not before. There is flexibility: the imam may supplicate sitting facing the qiblah or standing facing the people. Al-Halwani prefers standing. Leaning on a stick or bow is also permissible. The general rule is that the supplication is delayed until after the prayer. Additionally, the imam should not ascend the minbar for this supplication, nor should he leave the mosque (to supplicate elsewhere).

Key Terms
دعاء (du'a): Supplication to Allah. In the context of eclipse prayer, it is a recommended act after the prayer.
ثم (thumma): The word 'then' indicating sequence: the supplication comes after the prayer, not concurrent or before.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) After the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Supplication after eclipse prayer is a sunnah act performed after the prayer, with permissible postures of sitting or standing, and the imam should not ascend the minbar.

Eclipse Prayer Without the Friday Imam
Ruling on praying eclipse prayer individually if the Friday imam does not lead

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eclipse prayer when the Friday imam is absent and distinguish between the zahir al-riwayah position and the alternative narration from Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
If the Friday imam is absent for eclipse prayer, praying individually is the relied-upon ruling to avoid fitna.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with a specific scenario: the eclipse prayer and who should lead it. The text clarifies that when the Friday imam is absent, individuals should pray separately. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute, as Abu Hanifa had a view allowing any mosque imam to lead, but the preferred position is the one transmitted in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and context
The act is the eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf). The context is the absence of the Friday imam, who is the designated leader for such congregational prayers.
The Friday imam (imam al-jumu'ah) holds authority over special prayers like Eid and eclipse in Hanafi fiqh.
2
State the primary ruling
The matn says: 'and if not (he is absent), they pray individually' – meaning the people should pray separately, not in congregation.
3
Understand the reason for individual prayer
The reason given is 'to avoid fitna' – because congregational prayer would attract a large crowd and potentially cause discord.
Fitna here refers to social disturbance or chaos.
4
Note the alternative narration from Abu Hanifa
There is a narration from Abu Hanifa that any mosque imam can lead the congregation in eclipse prayer. This is a variant within the Hanafi school.
This shows that Abu Hanifa saw validity in congregational leadership beyond the Friday imam.
5
Determine the preferred (mufta bihi) view
The author states 'and the correct is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya)', meaning individual prayer is the relied-upon position. This is because the zahir al-riwaya is the well-known transmission from the early masters.
The tarjih is based on the authority of the six core books.
6
Consider the additional nuance from al-Asbijabi
Al-Asbijabi's comment suggests that if one prays at the proper time (zenith of the eclipse), the prayer is valid, even if done individually. This reinforces the validity of individual prayer.
This may be a note on the timing, not the congregation issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإلا صلوها فرادى) أي إن لم يحضر إمام الجمعة صلى الناس فرادى تحرزاً عن الفتنة إذ هي تقام بجمع عظيم. وروي عن أبي حنيفة أن لكل إمام مسجد أن يصلي بجماعة والصحيح ظاهر الرواية لأن أداء هذه في تحصيل كمال السنة ، نعم ظاهر ما قاله الأسبيجابي يفيد أنه لو صلاها عند الاستواء صحت فتدبره
His statement: (otherwise they pray individually) i.e., if the Friday imam is not present, the people pray individually, to avoid fitna because it (the congregational prayer) is held with a large gathering. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that every mosque imam may lead the congregation in prayer, but the sahih (correct) is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) because performing this (prayer) in congregation achieves the perfection of the sunnah. Yes, the apparent meaning of what al-Asbijabi said indicates that if one prays it at the time of the sun's zenith, it is valid, so ponder upon it.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage discusses the situation when the Friday imam (i.e., the imam appointed for Friday prayers) does not lead the eclipse prayer. In that case, the people should pray individually to avoid fitna (discord), since congregational prayer would attract a large crowd and potentially cause chaos. However, there is a narration (riwaya) from Abu Hanifa that any mosque imam can lead the congregation in eclipse prayer. The correct view is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) which prefers individual prayer. The reason given is that performing it in congregation achieves the perfection of the sunnah. The author then notes al-Asbijabi's suggestion that if one prays it at the time of the sun's zenith (i.e., at the time of eclipse), it is valid. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf about whether the Friday imam's leadership is necessary.

Key Terms
إمام الجمعة (imam al-jumu'ah): The imam appointed for Friday congregational prayer. In the context of eclipse prayer, he is the one who should lead if he is present.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent or well-known transmitted ruling, as opposed to a lesser-known narration (riwaya). In this case, it is the ruling that people pray individually.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the sahih (apparent riwaya) in this passage, what should people do if the Friday imam does not lead the eclipse prayer?
A) They should not pray at all.
B) They should pray in congregation with any imam.
C) They should pray individually.
D) They should wait for the imam to come.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, if the Friday imam does not lead the eclipse prayer, the preferred ruling is to pray individually, based on the zahir al-riwaya, to avoid fitna.
