Prayer During Lunar Eclipse and Calamities: Individual Prayer as Sunnah
Ruling on individual prayer for lunar eclipse and similar calamities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that for lunar eclipse and similar calamities, prayer is performed individually, not in congregation, and cite the Prophetic practice as the primary proof.

Core Idea
Lunar eclipse, storms, earthquakes: pray alone, not assembled — the Prophet never gathered for these.

The text expands the ruling of lunar eclipse prayer to other frightening natural events. Unlike solar eclipse, which has a sunnah congregational prayer led by the Friday imam, lunar eclipse and similar calamities are to be prayed individually at home. The proof is the Prophet's practice: the moon eclipsed many times in his lifetime, yet he never gathered people for a special prayer. This omission is a clear indication for the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing salah during a lunar eclipse or similar calamity. The ruling is that it is sunnah to pray individually (farada), not in congregation.
This applies also to darkness, strong wind, earthquake, thunder, etc.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the Prophetic practice: the moon eclipsed many times during his life, and he did not gather people for a congregational prayer. This is a 'dalil al-fi'l' (proof from action/inaction).
Additional evidence: gathering would be difficult (ta'addhur) for such events.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's repeated omission (tark) in a situation where he could have gathered people shows that congregation is not established as a sunnah. In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's deliberate omission when he had the ability to act indicates that acting differently is not part of the sunnah.
This is a form of bayan al-tark, indicating the ruling is not congregational.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars (as quoted from al-Mujtaba) hold that congregation is permissible (ja'iz) but not sunnah. However, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that individual prayer is the sunnah.
This is a difference within the school, not a full disagreement.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The author presents the individual prayer as the primary ruling, supported by the stronger evidence (zahir al-riwayah). The permissibility of congregation is a secondary opinion. The fatwa is on individual prayer.
This ruling is consistent across similar calamities due to the common illah (difficulty of gathering).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كالخسوف والظلمة والريح والفزع أي حيث يصلي الناس فرادى لأنه قد خسف القمر في عهده عليه السلام مراراً ولم ينقل أنه جمع الناس له، ولأن الجمع فيه متعسر كالزلازل والصواعق وانتشار الكواكب والضوء الهائل بالليل والثلج والأمطار الدائمة وعموم الأمراض والخوف الغالب من العدو ونحو ذلك من الأفزاع والأهوال، لأن ذلك كله من الآيات المخوفة والله تعالى يخوف عباده ليتركوا المعاصي ويرجعوا إلى الطاعة التي فيها فوزهم وخلاصهم، وأقرب أحوال العبد في الرجوع إلى ربه الصلاة وذكر في البدائع أنهم يصلون: في منازلهم. وفي المجتبى وقيل الجماعة جائزة عندنا لكنها ليست بسنة والله أعلم

And the closest state of the servant in returning to his Lord is prayer. Al-Badai' mentioned that they pray in their homes. In al-Mujtaba: It is said that congregation is permissible in our school but it is not sunnah. And Allah knows best.

Commentary
This passage extends the ruling of individual prayer to other natural phenomena: lunar eclipse (khusuf), darkness, strong wind, and general terror (faza'). For each, people pray individually in their homes. The proof is that the moon eclipsed many times during the Prophet's lifetime, and he never gathered people for a congregational prayer. Moreover, gathering would be difficult for events like earthquakes, lightning, meteors, strange lights, continuous rain/snow, widespread diseases, and fear of the enemy. These are all frightening signs by which Allah warns people. The best response is to pray individually. Al-Badai' states they pray in their homes. In al-Mujtaba, there is an opinion that congregation is permissible but not sunnah. The author concludes 'Allahu a'lam'.

Key Terms
خسوف (khusuf): Lunar eclipse. The text states that for lunar eclipse, people pray individually, not in congregation, unlike solar eclipse (kusuf) which has a congregational prayer if led by the Friday imam.
فزع (faza'): Terror or fear from an overwhelming event. In this context, it includes any fearful natural phenomenon.
فرادى (furada): Individually, alone. The text says 'يصلي الناس فرادى', i.e., they pray individually, not in congregation.

For lunar eclipse and similar calamities, the sunnah is to pray individually at home, based on the Prophet's practice and the difficulty of gathering.

Istisqa' (Rain Prayer): Definition and Hanafi Ruling
Definition and ruling of istisqa' with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of istisqa', identify its evidence from Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma, and explain the Hanafi ruling that it is performed individually without congregation.

Core Idea
Istisqa' prayer is legislated but individually, not congregationally, per Abu Hanifa.

When drought strikes, Muslims turn to Allah in prayer and supplication, known as istisqa'. This lesson unpacks its definition, its firm basis in the primary sources, and the distinctive Hanafi position that it is performed alone, not in congregation. Understanding this ruling clarifies why you may not see a large assembly for rain prayer in Hanafi communities.

Guided Path
1
Define istisqa'
Identify the core meaning: asking Allah for rain through praise, turning to Him, and seeking forgiveness. This is the legal definition.
The term itself indicates the action, not just a prayer.
2
Identify the evidence
Locate the three proofs: Quranic verse (Nuh 10-11), multiple Prophetic practices (Sunnah), and unanimous consensus (Ijma).
This is a dalil naqli passage.
3
Extract the ruling on congregation
The key phrase 'la bi-jama'ah' indicates that according to Abu Hanifa, istisqa' prayer has no congregational form.
Compare with other prayers that are congregational (Eid, Friday).
4
Distinguish from solar eclipse prayer
Note the text's mention of kusuf (solar eclipse) to highlight that rulings differ: solar eclipse prayer is sunnah or wajib, istisqa' is sunnah but individual.
This clarifies the relative emphasis.
5
Apply the ruling to modern contexts
In the Hanafi school, when drought occurs, individuals pray two rak'ahs alone at home or in the mosque without a leader or sermon.
Shafi'is and others may gather, but the Hanafi mufta bihi is individual prayer.

Chapter on Rain-Prayer (Istisqa'): It is asking for rain from Allah Almighty by praising Him, turning to Him, and seeking forgiveness. It is established by the Book, Sunnah, and consensus. As for the Book, Allah says recounting from Nuh (peace be upon him) when drought and barrenness afflicted his people: 'Ask forgiveness of your Lord; indeed, He is ever a Perpetual Forgiver. Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on Istisqa' (Rain Prayer). It defines istisqa' as seeking water (rain) from Allah through praise, turning to Him, and seeking forgiveness. Its legitimacy is proven by the Quran (the story of Prophet Nuh), the Sunnah (the Prophet's multiple practices), and unanimous consensus (ijma') of the ummah. The key ruling is that, according to Abu Hanifa, istisqa' has a prayer but it is performed individually, not in congregation (la bi-jama'ah). Then it addresses widespread diseases, stating that people pray individually and supplicate. It references al-Nahr and discusses the plague, distinguishing between the disease and the reward of martyrdom. The author notes he has expanded on this in his work al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir. The passage ends with the beginning of a commentary on the phrase 'congregation is not legislated' but is cut off.

Key Terms

بجماعة (bi-jama'ah): In congregation. The text states that according to Abu Hanifa, istisqa' has no congregation.

Individual Prayer During Eclipses and Natural Phenomena
Explaining the ruling of individual prayer during eclipses and fearful events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for prayer during lunar eclipses and other terrifying phenomena, and explain why congregation is not a sunnah.

Core Idea
For lunar eclipses, earthquakes, and the like, pray individually — congregation is neither established nor required.

When the moon eclipses or the earth shakes, how should we pray? The Hanafi school holds that such events call for individual prayer, not congregation. The Prophet ﷺ never gathered people for a lunar eclipse, so congregation is not a sunnah. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? It is the prayer during a lunar eclipse (khusuf) and similar fearful events (faza'). The ruling is that people pray individually, not in congregation.
The matn says: 'صلوا فرادى' (they pray individually).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? The absence of a report that the Prophet gathered people for a lunar eclipse. The text says: 'لم ينقل أنه جمع الناس له' (it is not transmitted that he gathered people for it).
This is a dalil naqli from the Sunnah (absence of practice).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the absence prove the ruling? The lack of transmission indicates that congregation is not part of the sunnah. If it were a sunnah, the Prophet would have done it publicly given the repeated eclipses.
This is a negative proof: what is not established is not required.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there disagreement? Within the Hanafi school, some scholars (in al-Mujtaba) consider congregation permissible but not sunnah. The text says: 'وقيل الجماعة جائزة عندنا لكنها ليست بسنة'.
This is an intra-madhhab difference; the majority view remains individual prayer.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Which position is relied upon for fatwa? The individual prayer is the mufta bihi. Congregation is not a sunnah; the safer practice is to pray alone or in homes.
The text concludes with 'والله أعلم' after stating the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإلا صلوا فرادى كالخسوف والظلمة والريح والفزع . باب الاستسقاء الصلوات بالجماعة عرف بإقامة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فإنما يقيمها الآن من هو قائم مقامه، فإن لم يقمها الإمام صلى الناس فرادى إن شاؤوا ركعتين وإن شاؤوا أربعاً والأربع أفضل، ثم إن شاؤوا طولوا القراءة وإن شاؤوا قصروا واشتغلوا بالدعاء حتى تنجلي الشمس . كذا في البدائع قوله : (كالخسوف والظلمة والريح والفزع أي حيث يصلي الناس فرادى لأنه قد خسف القمر في عهده عليه السلام مراراً ولم ينقل أنه جمع الناس له، ولأن الجمع فيه متعسر كالزلازل والصواعق وانتشار الكواكب والضوء الهائل بالليل والثلج والأمطار الدائمة وعموم الأمراض والخوف الغالب من العدو ونحو ذلك من الأفزاع والأهوال، لأن ذلك كله من الآيات المخوفة والله تعالى يخوف عباده ليتركوا المعاصي ويرجعوا إلى الطاعة التي فيها فوزهم وخلاصهم، وأقرب أحوال العبد في الرجوع إلى ربه الصلاة وذكر في البدائع أنهم يصلون : في منازلهم. وفي المجتبى وقيل الجماعة جائزة عندنا لكنها ليست بسنة والله أعلم
And otherwise they pray individually like during lunar eclipse, darkness, wind, and terror. The congregational prayers are known by the establishment of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). So now only the one standing in his place initiates them. If the imam does not establish them, the people pray individually if they wish two rak'ahs or if they wish four—and four is better—then if they wish they lengthen the recitation or shorten it, and occupy themselves with supplication until the sun clears. Thus in al-Bada'i'. His statement: '(like lunar eclipse, darkness, wind, and terror)' meaning that then people pray individually because the moon was eclipsed in his time (peace be upon him) many times and it is not reported that he gathered people for it, and because gathering for it is difficult like earthquakes, thunderbolts, the scattering of stars, the awesome light at night, continuous snow and rain, general diseases, overwhelming fear from the enemy, and similar terrors and horrors. All of these are frightening signs; Allah frightens His servants so they abandon sins and return to obedience which is their success and salvation. And the closest state of the servant in returning to his Lord is prayer. It is mentioned in al-Bada'i' that they pray in their homes. And in al-Mujtaba: it is said that congregation is permissible among us but it is not sunnah. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the matn ruling concerning prayer during natural phenomena. The matn states that if the imam does not lead a congregational prayer for such events, individuals pray alone. The commentary explains that the Prophet (peace be upon him) never gathered people for a lunar eclipse prayer, so congregation is not established as a sunnah. Moreover, gathering is impractical due to the widespread and alarming nature of these events—earthquakes, lightning, comets, epidemics, etc. The purpose is to drive people to repentance, and prayer is the best way to turn to Allah. Individuals may pray two or four rak'ahs, and are encouraged to lengthen supplication until the phenomenon ends. There is also a mention that some Hanafi scholars consider congregation permissible but not a sunnah. The commentary then references al-‘Ayni’s distinction between solar eclipse (kusuf) as sunnah or wajib and lunar eclipse (khusuf) as hasanah, and extends the same principle to general plagues, citing Ibn Hajar’s opinion that gathering for supplication during plague is a good innovation, though the author’s discussion is expanded in al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir.

Key Terms
خسوف (khusuf): Lunar eclipse
فزع (faza'): Fear or terror from natural phenomena or enemy
صلاة الخسوف (salat al-khusuf): Prayer during a lunar eclipse

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) There is no prayer at all.

Key Takeaway
For eclipses and terrifying phenomena, the Hanafi school prescribes individual prayer, not congregation, due to lack of prophetic precedent and practical difficulty.

Istisqa: Between Supplication and Prayer — The Hanafi Position and Key Disputes
Defining istisqa and detailing its prescribed practices and legal disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school does not prescribe a congregational prayer for istisqa and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on qalb al-rida'.

Core Idea
Istisqa is primarily supplication; congregation and cloak-turning are not sunnah in the Hanafi school.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq opens the chapter on Istisqa by defining it as a request for rain through praise, supplication, and seeking forgiveness. It then delves into the disputed elements: whether there is a congregational prayer, whether the imam turns his cloak, and who may attend. Understanding these debates clarifies the Hanafi emphasis on sincere supplication over ritual elaboration.

Guided Path
1
Define istisqa and its evidence
Identify the definition of istisqa (request for rain through praise, flight to Allah, and seeking forgiveness) and its scriptural basis: Quranic verse from Surah Nuh and numerous hadith of the Prophet and caliphs.
The consensus is that istisqa is established.
2
Analyze the prayer dispute
Distinguish Abu Hanifa's view (individual prayer, no congregation) from the Sahibayn (imam leads two rak'ahs). Note the Hanafi proof: the Prophet did it once and abandoned it, so it is not sunnah.
The later view of Muhammad in al-Kafi holds no prayer at all, only supplication.
3
Examine the cloak-turning dispute
Understand Abu Hanifa's rejection (istisqa is supplication, and turning is not done in other supplications) vs the Sahibayn and Quduri (imam turns based on narrated action). Evaluate the argument that the Prophet's act was an omen specific to him.
The common people do not turn their cloaks according to most Hanafis.
4
Apply the practical rules
List the prescribed conduct: go out three consecutive days, wear humble attire, give charity, renew repentance, no pulpit (though allowed), no dhimmis attend.
The imam leads but if he refuses, the people may go without him.
5
Assess the later fatwa
Note the view from Fatawa Qadikhan that there is no prayer in istisqa, only supplication, and that congregation is disliked. This becomes the relied-upon position.
The text states 'the apparent is what is in the book: that it is permissible and not sunnah.'

صفتها وقد اختلف فيها، والظاهر ما في الكتاب من أنها جائزة وليست بسنة. وقالا : يصلي الإمام ركعتين لما روي أن النبي صلى فيه ركعتين كصلاة العيد قلنا: فعله مرة وتركه أخرى فلم يكن سنة كذا في الهداية قوله : ( ودعاء واستغفار) أي للاستسقاء دعاء واستغفار لما تلونا قوله : (لا قلب رداء أي ليس فيه قلب رداء لأنه دعاء فيعتبر بسائر الأدعية، ولا فرق بين الإمام والقوم. وقالا : يقلب الإمام رداءه واختاره القدوري وهو أن يجعل الأيمن على الأيسر والأيسر على الأيمن ليقلب الله تعالى الحال من الجدب إلى الخصب، ومن العسر إلى اليسر. وقيل: أن يجعل أعلاه أسفل. وفي المدور يعتبر اليمين واليسار قوله: (وإنما يخرجون ثلاثة أيام) يعني متتابعات ويخرجون مشاة في ثياب خلق غسيلة أو مرقعة متذلليين متواضعين خاشعين الله تعالى ناكسي رؤوسهم، ويقدمون الصدقة في كل يوم قبل خروجهم ويجددون التوبة ويستغفرون للمسلمين ويتواضعون بينهم ويستسقون بالضعفة والشيوخ. وفي المجتبي : والأولى أن يخرج الإمام بالناس وإن امتنع وقال اخرجوا جاز، وإن خرجوا بغير إذنه جاز. ولا يخرج في الاستسقاء منبر بل يقوم الإمام والقوم قعود فإن أخرجو المنبر جاز لحديث رضي الله عنها أنه أخرج المنبر لاستسقائه ، وقيد بالخروج ثلاثة أيام لأنه لم ينقل أكثر منها قوله : (ولا يحضر أهل الذمة الاستسقاء) لنهي عمر رضي الله عنه ولأن المقصود هو الدعاء قال تعالى وما دعاء الكافرين إلا في ضلال [الرعد: ١٤] وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : محمد كما في الكافي لا صلاة في الاستسقاء وإنما فيها دعاء بلغنا عن رسول الله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم أنه خرج ودعا، وبلغنا عن عمر أنه صعد على المنبر ودعا واستسقى ولم يبلغنا عن النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم في ذلك صلاة إلا حديث واحد شاذ اهـ. وهذا يفيد أن الجماعة فيها مكروهة ويدل على ذلك ما مر عن الأصل قوله : ( وقالا لا يقلب الإمام رداءه) قال في النهر : لأنه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم فعل ذلك ولأبي حنيفة أنه دعاء فيعتبر بسائر الأدعية، وما روي من فعله كان تفاؤلاً واعترض بأنه لم لا يتفاءل من ابتلي به تأسياً به عليه الصلاة والسلام؟ وأجيب بأنه علم أن الحال ينقلب متى قلب الرداء وهذا مما لا يتأتى في غيره فلا فائدة بالتأسي ظاهراً. كذا العناية وغيرها وفيه بحث إذا الأصل في أفعاله عليه الصلاة والسلام كونها شرعاً عاماً حتى يثبت دليل الخصوص. وقوله في البدائع يحتمل أنه تغير عليه فأصلحه فظن الراوي أنه قلبه أبعد من هنا جزم القدوري بقول محمد، وأما القوم فلا يقلبون أرديتهم بالتشديد أي في يقلبون كما في السراج عند كافة العلماء خلافاً لمالك قول المصنف : ولا يحضر أهل الذمة) كان بنسخة المتن التي وقعت للمؤلف هكذا أو تابع الزيلعي وإلا فالذي في المتن مجرداً وعليه شرح في النهر لا قلب
Chapter of Istisqa: It is the request for rain from Allah by praising Him, fleeing to Him, and seeking forgiveness. This is established by the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus. As for the Book, His statement recounting from Noah (peace be upon him) when his people were driven by drought and barrenness: 'I said: Seek forgiveness of your Lord; indeed, He is ever a Pardoner, He will send rain upon you in abundance.' (Nuh 71:10-11) As for the Sunnah, it is established in many reports that the Prophet prayed for rain many times, as did the caliphs after him, and the community agreed upon it from predecessor to successor without rejection. His statement: 'He has a prayer without congregation' according to Abu Hanifa is an explanation that it is legislated for the individual, and congregation is not legislated for it. He did not explain the author's statement: 'like lunar eclipse, etc.' al-Ayni said: The shaykh made an absolute ruling in both, and the detail is that solar eclipse prayer is sunnah or obligatory, and lunar eclipse prayer is good, and the rest similarly. His statement: 'and general diseases' – al-Nahr said: Know that their words agree that they pray individually and supplicate during general diseases, which includes plague, because epidemic is a name for every general disease; every plague is an epidemic but not vice versa. Supplication lifts it, as people perceive in the mountain, and it is legislated; it is not a supplication for removing martyrdom because that is its effect not its essence. Based on this, what Ibn Hajar said – that gathering for supplication to lift it is a bid’ah – means a good bid’ah. So if they gather, each one prays two rak'ahs intending its removal. This issue is among the incidents of fatwa. End quote. The author expanded on this issue in al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir. Chapter of Istisqa. His statement: 'And congregation is not legislated' – al-Nahr said: As for the lack of legislation of congregation in it, it is because of the statement: 'He has a prayer without congregation and supplication and seeking forgiveness, without turning a cloak, and presence of a dhimmi, and they go out for three days.' Its description: it differed concerning it, and the apparent is what is in the book: that it is permissible and not sunnah. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: The imam prays two rak'ahs because it is narrated that the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs like the Eid prayer. We say: He did it once and left it another time, so it was not a sunnah. Thus in al-Hidaya. His statement: 'and supplication and seeking forgiveness' – meaning for istisqa there is supplication and seeking forgiveness as we recited. His statement: 'without turning a cloak' – meaning there is no turning of the cloak in it, because it is supplication, so it is considered like other supplications, and there is no difference between the imam and the people. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: The imam turns his cloak. Al-Quduri chose it, and it is to place the right on the left and the left on the right so that Allah changes the situation from drought to fertility, from hardship to ease. It is also said: He makes its top bottom. In al-Mudawwar, left and right are considered. His statement: 'and they go out for three days' – meaning consecutive days. They go out walking in worn washed or patched garments, humbling themselves, submissive, fearful of Allah, hanging their heads. They give charity each day before going out, renew repentance, seek forgiveness for the Muslims, humble themselves among each other, and seek rain by means of the weak and the elderly. In al-Mujtaba: It is better that the imam goes out with the people; if he declines and says 'go out', it is permissible; if they go out without his permission, it is permissible. No pulpit is taken out for istisqa; rather the imam stands and the people sit. If they do take out the pulpit, it is permissible due to the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that he took out the pulpit for his rain prayer. The going out was limited to three days because no more than that is transmitted. His statement: 'And dhimmis do not attend the istisqa' – due to the prohibition of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), and because the objective is supplication, Allah says: 'And the supplication of the disbelievers is not but in error' (Ghafir 13:14). In Fatawa Qadikhan: Muhammad as in al-Kafi: There is no prayer in istisqa; rather there is only supplication. It reached us that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) went out and supplicated, and it reached us that Umar ascended the pulpit, supplicated, and prayed for rain. Nothing has reached us from the Prophet (peace be upon him) concerning a prayer for it except a single anomalous hadith. End quote. This indicates that congregation in it is disliked, and that is indicated by what passed from the original. His statement: 'And they both said: The imam does not turn his cloak.' Al-Nahr said: Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did that, and for Abu Hanifa, it is supplication so it is considered like other supplications. What is narrated of his action was an omen. It is objected: Why should not one who is afflicted take it as an omen in emulation of him (peace be upon him)? The answer is that he knew that the situation changes when he turns his cloak, and this is not attainable by others, so there is no benefit in emulation apparently. Thus al-‘Inaya and others. There is discussion: the principle concerning his actions (peace be upon him) is that they are general legislation until evidence of specificity is established. His statement in al-Bada'i': It is possible that his garment became crooked and he straightened it, so the narrator thought he turned it—this is far-fetched. Al-Quduri was decisive about Muhammad's view. As for the people, they do not turn their cloaks (with emphasis) i.e. they do not turn them, as in al-Siraj according to all scholars, contrary to Malik. The author's statement: 'And dhimmis do not attend' – in the version of the matn that came to the author it is thus, or he followed al-Zayla'i; otherwise, what is in the matn without that, and upon it is the commentary in al-Nahr: no turning.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the chapter on istisqa (rain prayer). It begins by defining istisqa as requesting rain from Allah through praise, turning to Him, and seeking forgiveness, and establishes it via Quran (the story of Noah), numerous hadith, and consensus. The core of the chapter is the matn stating that for istisqa, there is a prayer without congregation, supplication, seeking forgiveness, no turning of the cloak, no attendance of dhimmis, and going out for three days. The commentary then expands each point. The first major dispute is whether the istisqa prayer is congregational. Abu Hanifa holds that there is no congregation; the prayer is for individuals. The Two (Sahibayn) argue that the imam should lead two rak'ahs as the Prophet once did. The Hanafi response is that the Prophet did it once and left it, so it is not a sunnah; congregation is not established. The relied-upon view is that congregation is not sunnah; some say it is permissible but not sunnah, and some later scholars like Muhammad in al-Kafi hold there is no prayer at all, only supplication. The second dispute concerns turning the garment (qalb al-rida'). Abu Hanifa says it is not part of istisqa because it is a supplication, and turning is not done in other supplications. The Sahibayn, supported by al-Quduri, say the imam should turn his cloak, based on the Prophet's action. The commentary explains that the Prophet's act was an omen and not general legislation, as the effect of turning is specific to him. The common people do not turn their cloaks according to most scholars, contrary to Malik. Third, the ruling on going out for three consecutive days: the people go out in humble attire, barefoot, with lowered heads, giving charity, and seeking rain through the weak and elderly. The imam should lead; if he refuses, the people may go without him. No pulpit is taken out, but if done, it is permissible. Fourth, dhimmis are not permitted to attend because the purpose is supplication, and their supplication is not accepted. Umar prohibited it. The passage concludes with the point that there is no specific prayer for istisqa; it is primarily supplication.

Key Terms
استسقاء (istisqa): Request for rain from Allah through supplication, praise, and seeking forgiveness, performed collectively with specific rituals.
قلب رداء (qalb al-rida'): Turning one's cloak or garment, specifically changing the right side to left and top to bottom, as a symbolic act during istisqa.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under Islamic rule with a pact of protection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi ruling on turning the cloak (qalb al-rida') during istisqa?
A) The imam must turn his cloak.
B) The imam does not turn his cloak; only the people do.
C) The imam does not turn his cloak, as it is supplication and not a prescribed act.
D) The imam turns his cloak only on the third day.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school emphasizes that istisqa is primarily supplication; the congregational prayer and cloak-turning are not part of the sunnah, and dhimmis should not attend.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Salat al-Istisqa: Dispute on Sunnah Status and Cloak Turning
Expansion of matn with intra-Hanafi dispute and proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Salat al-Istisqa and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding its sunnah status and the turning of the cloak.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: Istisqa is permissible, not sunnah; Sahibayn: imam prays two rak'ahs and turns cloak.

The prayer for rain (Salat al-Istisqa) is a topic of significant intra-Hanafi disagreement. While the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the view of Abu Hanifa that it is permissible but not a confirmed sunnah, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it a sunnah with specific rites. This lesson unpacks the arguments of each position and the practical implications for the congregation and the imam's actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
Determine the ruling according to Abu Hanifa as stated in the matn: is it a sunnah, wajib, or merely permissible? What is the evidence cited?
The matn says 'ja'iz wa laysat bi-sunnah' – permissible, not sunnah.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's objection
What do Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold regarding the prayer and the cloak turning? What is their evidence from the Sunnah?
They cite the hadith that the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs like 'Eid.
3
Analyse Abu Hanifa's response
How does Abu Hanifa rebut the hadith? Why does he conclude that it does not establish a sunnah?
He argues the Prophet did it once and left it, so it does not become a confirmed practice.
4
Resolve the conflicting views on the cloak turning
How does the commentary weigh the positions on qalb al-rida'? Which view is adopted as mufta bihi?
Al-Quduri adopts Muhammad's view on the turning method, but Abu Hanifa's general position is preferred.
5
Note additional issues
What are the rules regarding congregation, duration (three days), and attendance of dhimmis? How do the scholars differ on these?
The passage also covers the manner of going out and the permissibility of dhimmi attendance based on the verse about their supplication.

كتاب الصلاة باب الاستسقاء له صلاة لا بجماعة ودعاء واستغفار لا قلب رداء وحضور ذمي وإنما يخرجون ثلاثة أيام . صفتها وقد اختلف فيها، والظاهر ما في الكتاب من أنها جائزة وليست بسنة. وقالا : يصلي الإمام ومن العسر إلى اليسر. وقيل: أن يجعل أعلاه أسفل. وفي المدور يعتبر اليمين واليسار قوله: (وإنما يخرجون ثلاثة أيام) يعني متتابعات ويخرجون مشاة في ثياب خلق غسيلة أو مرقعة متذلليين متواضعين خاشعين الله تعالى ناكسي رؤوسهم، ويقدمون الصدقة في كل يوم قبل خروجهم ويجددون التوبة ويستغفرون للمسلمين ويتواضعون بينهم ويستسقون بالضعفة والشيوخ. وفي المجتبي : والأولى أن يخرج الإمام بالناس وإن امتنع وقال اخرجوا جاز، وإن خرجوا بغير إذنه جاز. ولا يخرج في الاستسقاء منبر بل يقوم الإمام والقوم قعود فإن أخرجو المنبر جاز لحديث رضي الله عنها أنه أخرج المنبر لاستسقائه ، وقيد بالخروج ثلاثة أيام لأنه لم ينقل أكثر منها قوله : (ولا يحضر أهل الذمة الاستسقاء) لنهي عمر رضي الله عنه ولأن المقصود هو الدعاء قال تعالى وما دعاء الكافرين إلا في ضلال [الرعد: ١٤] وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : عائشة محمد كما في الكافي لا صلاة في الاستسقاء وإنما فيها دعاء بلغنا عن رسول الله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم أنه خرج ودعا، وبلغنا عن عمر أنه صعد على المنبر ودعا واستسقى ولم يبلغنا عن النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم في ذلك صلاة إلا حديث واحد شاذ اهـ. وهذا يفيد أن الجماعة فيها مكروهة ويدل على ذلك ما مر عن الأصل قوله : ( وقالا لا يقلب الإمام رداءه) قال في النهر : لأنه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم فعل ذلك ولأبي حنيفة أنه دعاء فيعتبر بسائر الأدعية، وما روي من فعله كان تفاؤلاً واعترض بأنه لم لا يتفاءل من ابتلي به تأسياً به عليه الصلاة والسلام؟ وأجيب بأنه علم أن الحال ينقلب متى قلب الرداء وهذا مما لا يتأتى في غيره فلا فائدة بالتأسي ظاهراً. كذا العناية وغيرها وفيه بحث إذا الأصل في أفعاله عليه الصلاة والسلام كونها شرعاً عاماً حتى يثبت دليل الخصوص. وقوله في البدائع يحتمل أنه تغير عليه فأصلحه فظن الراوي أنه قلبه أبعد من هنا جزم القدوري بقول محمد، وأما القوم فلا يقلبون أرديتهم بالتشديد أي في يقلبون كما في السراج عند كافة العلماء خلافاً لمالك قول المصنف : ولا يحضر أهل الذمة) كان بنسخة المتن التي وقعت للمؤلف هكذا أو تابع الزيلعي وإلا فالذي في المتن مجرداً وعليه شرح في النهر لا قلب [؟] بالوحي البعيد ومن [؟] رداء وحضور ذمي وإنما يخرجون ثلاثة أيام قوله : اختلفوا في أنه هل يجوز) قال في النهر : أي يجوز عقلاً وإن لم يقع ا ا هـ. وهو بعيد جداً ومما يبعده نسبة الجواز إلى القول لا إلى الاستجابة ولا معنى للاختلاف في جواز القول بها عقلاً، فالظاهر أن المراد الجواز شرعاً يدل عليه قوله في غرر الأذكار : ورأى مالك حضوره لأن دعاءه قد يستجاب في الشدة لقوله تعالى فإذا ركبوا في الفلك دعوا الله مخلصين له الدين [العنكبوت : ٦٥] الآية | هـ . قلت : ولقوله تعالى قال رب انظرني إلى يوم يبعثون قال إنك من المنظرين [ الحجر : ٣٦] ولعل هذا وجه ما عليه الفتوى .
Chapter on Prayer for Rain. It has a prayer without congregation, supplication and seeking forgiveness, no turning of the cloak, and attendance of a dhimmi, and they go out for three days. Its description: there is disagreement about it. The apparent is what is in the book: that it is permissible and not a sunnah. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: The imam prays two rak'ahs because it was narrated that the Prophet ﷺ prayed two rak'ahs like the 'Eid prayer. We said: He did it once and left it another time, so it did not become a sunnah. Thus in al-Hidayah. His statement: 'and supplication and seeking forgiveness' means for the rain prayer there is supplication and seeking forgiveness as we recited. His statement: 'no turning of the cloak' means there is no turning of the cloak because it is a supplication, so it is considered like other supplications. There is no difference between the imam and the people. The two said: The imam turns his cloak. Al-Quduri chose it, and it is to put the right side on the left and the left on the right so that Allah may change the situation from drought to plenty and from hardship to ease. Some said: to make its top bottom. For a round cloak, right and left are considered. His statement: 'they go out for three days' means consecutive days. They go out walking in old washed or patched clothes, humbling themselves, submissive, fearing Allah, with heads lowered. They give charity every day before going out, renew repentance, seek forgiveness for Muslims, humble themselves among them, and seek rain through the weak and elderly. In al-Mujtaba: It is preferred that the imam go out with the people; if he refuses and says go out, it is permissible; if they go out without his permission, it is permissible. No pulpit is taken out for the rain prayer; rather the imam stands and the people sit. If they bring out a pulpit, it is permissible due to the hadith of Lady 'A'ishah that she brought out a pulpit for his rain prayer. The restriction to three days is because no more than that is transmitted. His statement: 'The people of dhimmah do not attend the rain prayer' due to the prohibition of 'Umar, and because the purpose is supplication. Allah said: 'And the supplication of the disbelievers is but in vain' [13:14]. In Fatawa Qadikhan: 'A'ishah and Muhammad as in al-Kafi: No prayer in the rain prayer; rather it includes supplication. It reached us that the Messenger of Allah went out and supplicated, and it reached us that 'Umar ascended the minbar and supplicated and sought rain. Only one odd hadith reached us about prayer from the Prophet in this regard. This indicates that congregation in it is disliked. This is supported by what preceded from the original. His statement: 'The two said: The imam does not turn his cloak.' He said in al-Nahr: Because the Prophet did that. For Abu Hanifah: It is a supplication, so it is considered like other supplications. What is narrated of his action was a good omen. It was objected: Why should one not take a good omen from being afflicted following him? The answer was: He knew that the situation changes when the cloak is turned, and this is not achieved in other cases, so there is no benefit in following outwardly. Thus in al-'Inayah and others. There is discussion: the principle in the Prophet's actions is that they are general legislation until evidence of specificity is established. His statement in al-Bada'i' may be that it changed on him so he fixed it, and the narrator thought he turned it. This is far-fetched. Al-Quduri definitively adopted Muhammad's view. As for the people, they do not turn their cloaks (with emphasis) i.e., they do not turn them, as in al-Siraj, according to all scholars, contrary to Malik. The author's statement: 'And the people of dhimmah do not attend' was in the copy of the text that occurred to the author like this or he followed al-Zayla'i, otherwise the text is isolated and upon it is the commentary in al-Nahr: 'no turning' [؟] by distant revelation and among [؟] cloak and attendance of dhimmi and indeed they go out three days. His statement: The author differed on whether it is permissible... He said in al-Nahr: That is, permissible rationally even if it did not occur. That is very far-fetched. What makes it far-fetched is attributing permissibility to the statement not to the answer, and there is no meaning to disagreement on the permissibility of saying it rationally. So apparently what is meant is permissibility legally. This is indicated by his statement in Ghurar al-Adhkar: And Malik saw his attendance because his supplication may be answered in hardship due to Allah's statement: 'When they board the ship, they call upon Allah sincerely' [29:65]. I say: And due to His statement: 'He said: My Lord, give me respite until the Day they are raised. He said: You are among the respited' [15:36-37]. Perhaps this is the basis of the fatwa.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with the prayer for rain (Salat al-Istisqa). The passage type is an intra-Hanafi dispute, presented as expansion of the matn. The author begins by stating the ruling: the prayer for rain is permissible (ja'iz) but not a sunnah according to Abu Hanifa. This is the relied-upon position in the matn. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, holding that it is a sunnah and the imam should pray two rak'ahs, based on a hadith that the Prophet ﷺ performed it like the 'Eid prayer. Abu Hanifa's response is that the Prophet ﷺ did it once and left it another time, so it did not become an established sunnah. This is an application of the principle that an action done occasionally does not constitute a confirmed sunnah. The commentary then addresses the issue of turning the cloak (qalb al-rida'). According to Abu Hanifa, there is no turning of the cloak because it is a supplication, and supplications are not confined to specific postures. The Sahibayn hold that the imam should turn his cloak, following the practice of the Prophet. The commentary prefers the view of Muhammad (as adopted by al-Quduri) regarding the method of turning. The passage also discusses the duration of going out (three consecutive days), the manner of going out (humble, in old clothes), and the attendance of dhimmis. The basis for excluding dhimmis is the verse that the supplication of disbelievers is futile, although there is a view that it is permissible and their supplication may be answered in times of distress. The fatwa according to al-Walwaji is that it is permissible to say that a dhimmi's supplication is answered. The commentary clarifies that the imam does not lead the prayer as a congregation; rather it is a gathering for supplication. The overall emphasis is on the differences within the Hanafi school and the reasoning behind each position.

Key Terms
الاستسقاء (al-istisqa'): The prayer or supplication for rain during drought.
قلب رداء (qalb ar-rida'): The act of turning the cloak so that the right side becomes left and vice versa, done as a gesture of asking Allah to change the situation.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under Muslim protection with a covenant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (operative ruling) in the Hanafi school, who turns the cloak during Salat al-Istisqa?
A) Only the imam turns his cloak.
B) Both the imam and the congregation turn their cloaks.
C) No one turns the cloak; it is not prescribed.
D) The congregation turns their cloaks but the imam does not.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that Salat al-Istisqa is permissible but not a sunnah; the imam may turn his cloak as a symbolic act, but the congregation does not.

Salat al-Khawf: Procedure and Condition of Intensified Fear
Commentary describing the procedure and condition of the prayer of fear

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for the prayer of fear and explain why proximity of the enemy suffices as a condition.

Core Idea
The prayer of fear is a concession; mere proximity of the enemy triggers it, not subjective fear.

Performing prayer during battle presents practical challenges. The Prophet ﷺ demonstrated a special form called Salat al-Khawf, which this passage describes. Beyond the procedure, a key point of debate is whether 'intensified fear' is a condition. The Hanafi school clarifies that the cause is the presence of the enemy, not the emotional state.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage describes the prayer of fear (Salat al-Khawf) as a permissible concession (ja'iz) when danger is present.
The ruling is permissibility, not obligation.
2
Extract the procedure
List the steps: imam stations a group facing the enemy, leads one rak'ah (or two if resident), then that group goes to the enemy; second group comes, imam leads remaining rak'ahs and says taslim; first group completes without recitation, second group completes with recitation.
This is one of several permissible forms.
3
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Ibn 'Umar is cited: 'Thus the Messenger of Allah performed it.' This is a sunnah ahad proof.
The proof is based on the Prophet's action.
4
Analyse the condition of fear
Note that the text initially says 'when fear intensifies', but the commentary clarifies that intensification is not a condition per the majority of Hanafi scholars. Proximity of the enemy is the cause.
Al-'Inayah and al-Tuhfah support this view.
5
Understand the ikhtilaf
Some scholars interpret 'fear' as actual presence of the enemy, not subjective fear. All forms of the prayer are permissible; the difference is only in the first method.
The commentary dismisses an objection that the ruling is obvious.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب الخوف باب الخوف إذا اشتد الخوف من عدو أو سبع وقف الإمام طائفة بإزاء العدوّ وصلى ركعة وركعتين لو مقيماً ومضت هذه إلى العدو وجاءت تلك فصلى بهم ما بقى وسلم وذهبوا إليهم وجاءت الأولى وأتموا بلا قراءة وسلموا ثم الأخرى وأتموا بقراءة هكذا صلاها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من حديث ابن عمر، وهناك كيفيات أخرى معلومة في الخلافيات. وذكر في المجتبي أن الكل جائز وإنما الخلاف في الأولى. وفي العناية : ليس الاشتداد شرطاً عند عامة مشايخنا. قال في التحفة : سبب جواز صلاة الخوف نفس قرب العدو من غير ذكر الخوف والاشتداد. وقال فخر الإسلام في مبسوطة : المراد بالخوف عند البعض حضرة العدو لا حقيقة الخوف لأن باب الخوف قوله : (إلا أن يقال إنه معلوم مما قدمه الخ) هذا بعيد جداً.
Chapter on Fear [Prayer]. Chapter on Fear. When fear intensifies from an enemy or a beast, the imam stations a group facing the enemy, prays one rak'ah [or two if a resident] with a group, then this group goes to the enemy and another group comes. He leads them in the remaining [rak'ahs], says taslim, they go to the enemy, and the first group returns, completes without recitation and says taslim. Then the other [group] completes with recitation. Thus the Messenger of Allah performed it according to the hadith of Ibn 'Umar. There are other forms known in the books of differences. Al-Mujtaba mentions that all are permissible, the difference is in the first. In al-'Inayah: Intensification is not a condition according to the generality of our masters. In al-Tuhfah: The cause for allowing the prayer of fear is merely the proximity of the enemy, without mentioning fear or intensification. Fakhr al-Islam said in his Mabsut: Some take the meaning of fear to be the presence of the enemy, not actual fear, because... Chapter on Fear. His statement: 'Except that it may be said that it is known from what he preceded...' This is very far-fetched.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq introduces the prayer of fear (Salat al-Khawf). The passage type is a ruling with proof, as it describes the procedure and cites the prophetic practice. The commentary first describes the basic method: when fear intensifies from an enemy or a beast, the imam stations one group facing the enemy, leads one rak'ah (or two if he is a resident), then that group goes to the enemy, another group comes, he leads them in the remaining rak'ahs, then says taslim. The first group completes without recitation, and the second completes with recitation. This is based on the hadith of Ibn 'Umar. The text notes that there are other permissible forms, and the difference lies only in the first. A key point is that according to the majority of Hanafi scholars, intensification of fear is not a condition; rather, mere proximity of the enemy suffices. Fakhr al-Islam explains that some interpret 'fear' as the presence of the enemy, not the subjective feeling. The final line is a commentary on an objection that the ruling is obvious from what preceded; the commentator dismisses this as far-fetched. The overall teaching is that the prayer of fear is a concession to facilitate prayer during battle, with flexibility in its performance.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (salat al-khawf): The special form of prayer performed during battle or when in fear of an enemy or predator.
اشتداد الخوف (ishtidad al-khawf): Intensification of fear; the condition under which the prayer of fear is performed according to some.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The fear must be intense (ishtidad).
B) The enemy must be present and close.
C) The imam must be a resident.
D) The prayer must be performed in congregation.

Key Takeaway
The prayer of fear is a permissible form whose validity depends on the proximity of danger, not the intensity of fear.

The Fear Prayer: Method and the Condition of Fear
Describes the fear prayer method and refutes intensity of fear as a condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi method of the fear prayer and explain why the intensification of fear is not a condition for its validity.

Core Idea
The fear prayer is permissible due to the enemy's presence, not the intensity of fear.

The fear prayer (ṣalāt al-khawf) is a special form of prayer legislated when Muslims face an enemy or danger. This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq explains the method performed by the Prophet ﷺ and clarifies a key Hanafi principle: the permissibility of this prayer depends on the mere proximity of the enemy, not on the subjective intensity of fear. Understanding this distinction saves the prayer from being conditional on an unmeasurable state.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being described? It is the fear prayer. What is its ruling? According to the passage, it is permissible (jā'iz) and the described method is valid.
The passage confirms that the Prophet ﷺ performed it, so it is sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the actual practice (fi‘l) of the Prophet ﷺ as narrated by Ibn Umar. In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action indicates permissibility (dalīl al-jawāz).
The ḥadīth is ahad, so its thubūt is ẓannī, but the ruling is still established.
3
Trace the condition discussed
The passage addresses whether intensification of fear (ishtidād) is a condition. It clearly states from al-ʿInāyah that it is not a condition according to the generality of our Mashāyikh. The cause (sabab) is the mere presence (qurb) of the enemy.
This refutes a common misunderstanding that extreme fear is required.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There are multiple methods of fear prayer known in the books of differences. The passage mentions that all are permissible; the difference is only in which is preferable (al-awla). The described method is considered the best.
This shows that Hanafis allow flexibility within the school.
5
Understand the application of lāḥiq and masbūq
The first group is considered lāḥiq (latecomer) because they prayed the first rak'ah(s) and then left; they complete without recitation. The second group is masbūq (one who missed part) and recites when completing. This shows how the fear prayer integrates with normal prayer rules.
This distinction affects what each group recites.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الخوف أي صلاته. ووجه المناسبة أن شرعية كل منهما لعارض خوف. وقدم الاستسقاء لأن العارض هناك انقطاع المطر وهو سماوي وهنا اختياري وهو الجهاد الذي سببه كفر الكافر قوله : (إن اشتد من عدو سبع وقف الإمام طائفة بإزاء العدوّ وصلى بطائفة ركعة وركعتين لو مقيماً ومضت هذه إلى العدو وجاءت تلك فصلى بهم ما بقي وسلم وذهبوا إليهم وجاءت الأولى وأتموا بلا قراءة وسلموا ثم الأخرى وأتموا بقراءة هكذا صلاها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من حديث ابن عمر، وهناك كيفيات أخرى معلومة في الخلافيات. وذكر في المجتبي أن الكل جائز وإنما الخلاف في الأولى. وفي العناية : ليس الاشتداد شرطاً عند عامة مشايخنا. قال في التحفة : سبب جواز صلاة الخوف نفس قرب العدو من غير ذكر الخوف والاشتداد. وقال فخر الإسلام في مبسوطة : المراد بالخوف عند البعض حضرة العدو لا حقيقة الخوف لأن [رداء وحضور ذمي] [؟] وإنما يخرجون ثلاثة أيام
Chapter of Fear: i.e., its prayer. And the reason for appropriateness is that the legislation of each of them is due to an incidental fear. And he gave precedence to the prayer for rain because the incidental cause there is the lack of rain, which is celestial, while here it is voluntary, which is jihad, whose cause is the disbelief of the disbeliever. His saying: (If fear intensifies from an enemy or a beast, the Imam stands a group facing the enemy and prays with a group one rak'ah, and two rak'ahs if he is a resident, then this group goes to the enemy and that group comes, and he prays with them the remainder and says the salām, and they go to them, and the first group comes and completes without recitation and says the salām, then the other group completes with recitation.) Thus the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم prayed it according to the hadith of Ibn Umar. And there are other known methods in the books of differences. And it is mentioned in al-Mujtabā that all are permissible, and the difference is only in the best. And in al-ʿInāyah: Intensification is not a condition according to the generality of our Mashāyikh. He said in al-Tuḥfah: The cause for the permissibility of the fear prayer is the mere proximity of the enemy, without mention of fear or intensification. And Fakhr al-Islām said in his Mabsūtah: What is meant by fear according to some is the presence of the enemy, not the reality of fear, because [?] and they only go out for three days.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is from the beginning of the Chapter of Fear Prayer in al-Bahr al-Rā’iq. The commentator first explains the connection between this chapter and the previous one on rain prayer: both are due to incidental fear. He then quotes the matn of Kanz al-Daqā’iq: when fear intensifies from an enemy or a beast, the imam divides the congregation into two groups. He prays one rak‘ah (or two if he is a resident) with one group, then they go to face the enemy while the other group comes. He prays the remainder with them and says salām. Then the first group returns and completes their prayer without recitation (since they are lāḥiqūn, followers who missed part), while the second group completes with recitation (since they are masbūqūn, those who joined late). The commentator confirms this was the practice of the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم as narrated by Ibn Umar. He notes that other ways are known but the issue is which is preferable. Importantly, he clarifies from al-‘Ināyah that the intensification of fear is not a condition; rather, the mere presence of the enemy justifies the fear prayer, as stated by Fakhr al-Islām. This is a key Hanafi principle: the ruling is attached to the cause (presence of enemy) not to the subjective feeling.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (ṣalāt al-khawf): A specific form of prayer performed in the presence of an enemy or danger, where the congregation is divided into two groups.
الاشتداد (al-ishtidād): Intensification of fear; the text clarifies it is not a condition for the permissibility of the fear prayer.
لاحق (lāḥiq): One who joins the prayer late but after the imam has completed some rak‘ahs; here, the first group is lāḥiq because they prayed the first part and then leave to face the enemy.
مسبوق (masbūq): One who joins the prayer after the imam has started; here the second group is masbūq and recites when completing their prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the permissibility of the fear prayer?
A) The express command in the Quran
B) The practice of the Prophet ﷺ as narrated by Ibn Umar
C) The consensus of the Companions
D) Analogy to the rain prayer

Key Takeaway
The fear prayer is valid due to the mere presence of the enemy, not the intensity of fear, and the Hanafi method is based on the Prophet's practice.

The Format of Maghrib Fear Prayer
Explains the specific format for Maghrib fear prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the Maghrib fear prayer and explain why the first group prays two rak'ahs.

Core Idea
In Maghrib fear prayer, the first group prays two rak'ahs, the second one rak'ah.

This lesson presents the specific format for Maghrib prayer during the fear prayer (salat al-khawf). The Hanafi school outlines that the imam prays two rak'ahs with the first group and one rak'ah with the second. The reasoning is based on the indivisibility of the single rak'ah and the priority of the first group. Understanding this ruling ensures correct performance in stressful conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? Maghrib fear prayer. What is the ruling? The imam prays two rak'ahs with the first group and one with the second.
This is a specific format, not the general ruling for fear prayer.
2
Understand the reasoning
Why two rak'ahs for the first group? Because two rak'ahs constitute half (shahr) of Maghrib (which is three rak'ahs), and the qa'dah is prescribed after two. Also, the single rak'ah cannot be split, so it goes to the second group.
The logic involves the concept of shatr (half) and indivisibility.
3
Note the priority
The first group is entitled to the two rak'ahs due to their precedence (sabq).
4
Consider the imam's error
The author mentions he omitted the branches about the imam's error deliberately, implying they are less important.
Focus on the main ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المغرب بالأولى ركعتين وبالثانية ركعة ومن قاتل بطلت صلاته لأن الركعتين شطر في المغرب ولهذا شرع القعود عقبيهما ولأن الواحد لا يتجزى فكانت الطائفة الأولى أولى بها للسبق، فإذا ترجحت عند التعارض لزم اعتباره ومسائل خطأ الإمام وتفاريعهم تركناها عمداً للاستغناء عنها قوله : ( ومن قاتل بطلت صلاتة ؛ لأنه عمل كثير مفسد للصلاة وهو مراده بالمقاتلة وإلا فلو قاتل بعمل قليل كالرمية لا تفسد كما علم في مفسدات الصلاة. واستدل في المجتبى بحديث المغيرة أن النبي شغل عن أربع صلوات يوم الخندق فصلاهن من بعد ما مضى من الليل ولو جاز مع القتال لما أخرهن عن وقتهن ا.هـ. وأشار المصنف إلى أن السابح في البحر إذا لم يمكنه أن يرسل أعضاءه ساعة فإنه لا يصلي فإن صلى لا تصح، وإن أمكنه ذلك فإنه يصلي بالإيماء كذا في المجتبى
And he prayed in Maghrib with the first group two rak‘ahs and with the second group one rak‘ah. And whoever fights, his prayer is nullified. Because the two rak‘ahs are half of Maghrib, and for this reason the sitting is prescribed after them, and because the one rak‘ah is indivisible, so the first group is more entitled to it due to priority. So when it is preferred in case of conflict, it must be considered. And the issues of the imam’s error and their branches we have omitted deliberately due to lack of need. His saying: 'And whoever fights, his prayer is nullified' because it is a lot of action that invalidates the prayer, and it is what he means by fighting; otherwise, if he fights with a little action like throwing, it does not invalidate, as is known in the invalidators of prayer. And in al-Mujtabā, they adduced the hadith of al-Mughīrah that the Prophet was occupied from four prayers on the day of al-Khandaq and prayed them after the night had passed, and if fighting had been permissible, he would not have delayed them from their times. And the author pointed out that the swimmer in the sea if he cannot move his limbs for a moment, then he does not pray, and if he prays it is not valid; but if it is possible, he prays with gestures, as in al-Mujtabā.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage gives two specific rulings. First, for the Maghrib prayer in the fear prayer: the imam prays two rak‘ahs with the first group and one rak‘ah with the second group. The reasoning is that two rak‘ahs constitute half of Maghrib (which is three), and the qa‘dah (sitting) is prescribed after the first two. The single rak‘ah cannot be split, so the first group gets two due to their precedence. Second, the ruling that active fighting during prayer nullifies it because it is a lot of action (kathīr al-‘amal). However, minor fighting like a single throw does not invalidate. The hadith of al-Mughīrah shows that the Prophet delayed missed prayers from the battle of al-Khandaq, implying that praying during fighting was not allowed. The commentator also notes the case of a swimmer: if he cannot even move his limbs, he does not pray; but if he can, he prays with gestures.

Key Terms
شطر (shiṭr): Half; in Maghrib, two rak‘ahs are half of the three rak‘ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how is Maghrib fear prayer performed?
A) The first group prays three rak'ahs, the second group prays none.
B) The first group prays two rak'ahs, the second group prays one.
C) Both groups pray two rak'ahs.
D) The imam prays all three alone.

Key Takeaway
In Maghrib fear prayer, the first group performs two rak'ahs and the second group one rak'ah.

Ruling on Fighting During Prayer: Major vs Minor Action
Explains the ruling that active fighting invalidates prayer, with proof from hadith and analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between major and minor action during prayer and apply the Hanafi ruling that active fighting invalidates the prayer, citing the evidence from the hadith of al-Mughirah.

Core Idea
Active fighting (major action) invalidates prayer; minor action like a single throw does not.

This lesson addresses the crucial distinction between major and minor actions during prayer, specifically in the context of combat. The Hanafi school rules that engaging in active fighting (muqatala) that involves a lot of action nullifies the prayer, whereas a single throw does not. The proof is drawn from the Prophet's practice during the Battle of the Trench. Additionally, the swimmer analogy reinforces the principle that significant movement breaks prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is fighting during prayer. The ruling: it invalidates the prayer if it involves a lot of action (kathir al-amal).
The text uses 'muqatala' to refer to major fighting.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites the hadith of al-Mughirah that the Prophet delayed the four prayers on the day of al-Khandaq and prayed them after the night had passed.
The hadith is a type of sunnah ahad.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
If fighting were permissible during prayer, the Prophet would not have delayed the prayers. Thus, fighting is incompatible with the integrity of the prayer.
This is an inference from the Prophet's action (ta'khir).
4
Apply the distinction between major and minor action
Minor action (e.g., a single throw) does not invalidate because it is not considered 'kathir al-amal'. The Hanafi school has clear criteria for what constitutes a lot of action.
The ruling is based on the principle that 'kathir al-amal' invalidates, while 'qalil' does not.
5
Consider the swimmer analogy
The swimmer who cannot move his limbs for a moment should not pray; if he can move, he prays with gestures. This illustrates that significant physical inability or action affects prayer validity.
The swimmer case is an extension of the same principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المغرب بالأولى ركعتين وبالثانية ركعة ومن قاتل بطلت صلاته لأن الركعتين شطر في المغرب ولهذا شرع القعود عقبيهما ولأن الواحد لا يتجزى فكانت الطائفة الأولى أولى بها للسبق، فإذا ترجحت عند التعارض لزم اعتباره ومسائل خطأ الإمام وتفاريعهم تركناها عمداً للاستغناء عنها قوله : ( ومن قاتل بطلت صلاتة ؛ لأنه عمل كثير مفسد للصلاة وهو مراده بالمقاتلة وإلا فلو قاتل بعمل قليل كالرمية لا تفسد كما علم في مفسدات الصلاة. واستدل في المجتبى بحديث المغيرة أن النبي شغل عن أربع صلوات يوم الخندق فصلاهن من بعد ما مضى من الليل ولو جاز مع القتال لما أخرهن عن وقتهن ا.هـ. وأشار المصنف إلى أن السابح في البحر إذا لم يمكنه أن يرسل أعضاءه ساعة فإنه لا يصلي فإن صلى لا تصح، وإن أمكنه ذلك فإنه يصلي بالإيماء كذا في المجتبى
And he prayed in Maghrib with the first group two rak‘ahs and with the second group one rak‘ah. And whoever fights, his prayer is nullified. Because the two rak‘ahs are half of Maghrib, and for this reason the sitting is prescribed after them, and because the one rak‘ah is indivisible, so the first group is more entitled to it due to priority. His saying: 'And whoever fights, his prayer is nullified' because it is a lot of action that invalidates the prayer, and it is what he means by fighting; otherwise, if he fights with a little action like throwing, it does not invalidate, as is known in the invalidators of prayer. And in al-Mujtabā, they adduced the hadith of al-Mughīrah that the Prophet was occupied from four prayers on the day of al-Khandaq and prayed them after the night had passed, and if fighting had been permissible, he would not have delayed them from their times. And the author pointed out that the swimmer in the sea if he cannot move his limbs for a moment, then he does not pray, and if he prays it is not valid; but if it is possible, he prays with gestures, as in al-Mujtabā.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage gives two specific rulings. First, for the Maghrib prayer in the fear prayer: the imam prays two rak‘ahs with the first group and one rak‘ah with the second group. The reasoning is that two rak‘ahs constitute half of Maghrib (which is three), and the qa‘dah (sitting) is prescribed after the first two. The single rak‘ah cannot be split, so the first group gets two due to their precedence. Second, the ruling that active fighting during prayer nullifies it because it is a lot of action (kathīr al-‘amal). However, minor fighting like a single throw does not invalidate. The hadith of al-Mughīrah shows that the Prophet delayed missed prayers from the battle of al-Khandaq, implying that praying during fighting was not allowed. The commentator also notes the case of a swimmer: if he cannot even move his limbs, he does not pray; but if he can, he prays with gestures.

Key Terms
المقاتلة (al-muqātalah): Active fighting; it invalidates prayer if it involves a lot of action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following invalidates prayer?
A) Throwing a spear once.
B) Engaging in prolonged hand-to-hand combat.
C) Winking at a fellow soldier.
D) Reciting Qur'an incorrectly.

Key Takeaway
Active fighting (major action) invalidates prayer; a single throw does not, based on the Prophet's practice and the principle of kathir al-amal.

Intense Fear: Praying on Horseback by Gestures
Ruling on the most intense fear prayer with proof and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for prayer during intense fear and identify its conditions and Quranic proof.

Core Idea
When fear prevents dismounting, the prayer is valid on horseback with head gestures, individually, facing any direction.

This lesson explores the most extreme form of the concession (rukhsah) for prayer under fear. Based on the Quranic verse (2:239) and Hanafi fiqh, we will learn how one may pray while riding, using gestures, without the usual postures or congregation, and only outside the town.

Guided Path
1
State the act and ruling
Identify the act as obligatory prayer performed under intense fear. The ruling: valid (sahih) when performed as described in the text.
This is the extreme end of the fear prayer license.
2
Locate the proof
Find the Quranic evidence: verse 2:239 'If you fear, then pray on foot or riding.' This is a general permission.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalala, requiring interpretation.
3
Trace the derivation
The Prophet's practice and Hanafi commentary specify that when fear prevents normal prayer, one may pray on a riding animal with head gestures (īmā') and in any direction. 'Intense fear' means inability to dismount.
The specific conditions are derived from this general verse and established sunnah.
4
Identify the key conditions
List the conditions: must be outside the town, on a riding animal, individually (not in congregation), with gestures, and facing any direction due to necessity.
Each condition is explicitly mentioned or implied in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإذا اشتد الخوف صلوا ركباناً فرادى بالإيماء إلى أي جهة قدروا لقوله تعالى فإن خفتم فرجالا أو ركباناً) [البقرة: ٢٣٩] والتوجه إلى القبلة للضرورة أراد بالاشتداد أن لا يتهيأ لهم النزول عن الدابة كما في غاية البيان. قيد بقوله «فرادى» لأنه لا يجوز بجماعة لعدم الاتحاد في المكان إلا إذا كان راكباً مع الإمام على دابة واحدة فإنه يجوز اقتداء المتأخر منهما بالمتقدم اتفاقاً. ويرد على المصنف ما إذا صلى راكباً في المصر فإنه لا يجوز إلا أن يقال : إنه معلوم مما قدمه من أن التطوع لا يجوز في المصر راكباً فكذا الفرض للضرورة. وقيد بالركوب لأنه لا يجوز ماشياً فيغير المصر لأن المشي
His saying: (If fear intensifies, they pray as riders, individually, by gestures in any direction they are able) due to His statement: 'If you fear, then [pray] on foot or riding.' [2:239] And facing the qiblah is for necessity. By intensity he means that they are not able to dismount from the animal, as in Ghāyat al-Bayān. He restricted with 'individually' because it is not permissible in congregation due to the lack of unity in place, except if one is riding with the imam on the same animal, then it is permissible for the one behind to follow the one ahead, by agreement. And an objection is made against the author regarding praying on a riding animal in the town: it is not permissible, unless it is said: it is known from what he previously mentioned that voluntary prayer on a riding animal in the town is not permissible, so likewise the obligatory prayer for necessity. And he restricted with riding because it is not permissible to walk outside the town, because walking...
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This ruling covers the most intense form of fear where even the format with groups is not possible. The prayer is performed on horseback (or any riding animal), individually, by head gestures, and facing any direction. The proof is from the Quran (2:239). The commentator specifies that 'intensity' means they cannot dismount. The phrase 'individually' indicates that congregation is not allowed because they are not in one place, except if they are on the same animal. There is also a restriction that this is only for outside the town; inside the town, riding prayer is not permissible even for the obligatory prayer, because it would be similar to voluntary prayer which is not allowed while riding in town. The restriction to riding (as opposed to walking) is important because walking prayer is not permissible outside the town either, due to inability to perform the postures.

Key Terms
الإيماء (al-īmā’): Gestures with the head as a substitute for bowing and prostrating, used when one cannot perform the actual movements.
ركباناً (rukbānan): Riding on animals; specifically, praying while seated on a riding animal.
فرادى (furādā): Individually; here it means not in congregation because they cannot unite in place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the enemy is present but not yet attacking.
B) When one cannot dismount from the animal due to intense fear.
C) When one is in the town.
D) When the imam leads from a separate animal.

Key Takeaway
The extreme fear prayer (salat al-khawf) on a riding animal with gestures is valid only outside the town, when dismounting is impossible, and must be performed individually.

Status of First and Second Groups in Fear Prayer: Lahiq and Masbuq
Commentary on the ruling for Maghrib fear prayer, explaining division of rak'ahs and status of groups.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a lahiq and a masbuq in fear prayer and state the recitation rule for each.

Core Idea
In fear prayer, the first group follows without recitation, the second group recites because they are latecomers.

The fear prayer (salat al-khawf) has unique rulings to accommodate the congregation under threat. One key distinction is the status of the two groups relative to the imam. Understanding whether a person is a lahiq (follower from the beginning) or a masbuq (latecomer) determines whether they recite Quran in the remaining rak'ahs and how the prayer is affected by external factors like a woman passing in front. This lesson unpacks that distinction as presented in the Hanafi commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The fear prayer is valid (sahih) with specific conditions. Identify that the first group completes without recitation and the second with recitation.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Understand the lahiq and masbuq distinction
The first group are lahiquin (those who caught the beginning and are following), so they do not recite in the remaining rak'ahs. The second group are masbuqin (latecomers), so they recite.
A lahiq has already recited with the imam in the first rak'ahs; a masbuq has not.
3
Apply the distinction to a woman passing in front
If a woman passes in front of a lahiq, their prayer is invalid (because they are in a state of following the imam with specific etiquettes). For a masbuq, it does not invalidate because they are considered separate from the imam's direct sequence.
This highlights the practical consequence of the status.
4
Note the analogy with the resident behind a traveler
The same rule applies to a resident praying behind a traveler: if the resident is from the first group (i.e., caught the first rak'ahs), he performs three rak'ahs without recitation; if from the second, with recitation.
This shows the principle applies beyond fear prayer.
5
Recognize the scope of the ruling
The ruling covers all congregational prayers, including the five daily prayers, Friday prayer, and Eid prayer, as fear prayer can be performed for any congregation.
The author expands the application from the specific case of Maghrib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما تتم الطائفة الأولى بلا قراءة لأنهم لاحقون ولذا لو حاذتهم امرأة فسدت صلاتهم، والثانية بقراءة لأنهم مسبوقون ولذا لو حاذتهم امرأة لا تفسد صلاتهم، ويدخل تحته المقيم خلف المسافر حتى يقضي ثلاث ركعات بلا قراءة إن كان الطائفة الأولى، وبقراءة من إن كان من الثانية والمسبوق إن أدرك ركعة من الشفع الأول فهو من الطائفة الأولى وإلا فهو من الثانية. وأطلق في الصلاة فشمل كل صلاة تؤدي بجماعة كالصلوات الخمس ومنها الجمعة وكذا العيد، وفي المجتبى ويسجد للسهو في صلاة الخوف لعموم الحديث ويتابعه ويسجد اللاحق في آخر صلاته .
قوله : (وصلى في المغرب بالأولى ركعتين وبالثانية ركعة لأن الركعتين شطر في المغرب ولهذا شرع القعود عقبيهما ولأن الواحد لا يتجزى فكانت الطائفة الأولى أولى بها للسبق، فإذا ترجحت عند التعارض لزم اعتباره ومسائل خطأ الإمام وتفاريعهم تركناها عمداً للاستغناء عنها
And the first group completes without recitation because they are followers (lahiqun), and if a woman passes in front of them, their prayer is invalid; the second group completes with recitation because they are latecomers (masbuqun), and if a woman passes in front of them, their prayer is not invalid. Included under it is the resident praying behind a traveler, such that he performs three rak'ahs without recitation if he is from the first group, and with recitation if from the second; and the latecomer (masbuq) if he catches one rak'ah of the first two rak'ahs is from the first group, otherwise from the second. And it is general regarding prayer, so it includes every prayer performed in congregation, such as the five prayers, including Friday and Eid. And in al-Mujtaba: one performs prostrations of forgetfulness in the fear prayer due to the general meaning of the hadith, and he follows him [the imam], and the follower (lahiq) performs prostration at the end of his prayer. He said: (And he prays in Maghrib with the first group two rak'ahs and with the second one rak'ah) because two rak'ahs constitute half of Maghrib, hence sitting was prescribed after them, and because the one [rak'ah] cannot be divided, so the first group is more entitled to it due to precedence; when there is conflict, preference is given. And issues of the imam's mistake and their branches we have intentionally left out as unnecessary.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling for Maghrib prayer in the fear prayer context. The author explains that the first group (who pray the first two rak'ahs with the imam) are considered 'lahiqun' (those who caught the beginning and are following the imam), so they complete without recitation. The second group (who join after two rak'ahs) are 'masbuqun' (latecomers), so they pray with recitation. The author draws an analogy to the resident praying behind a traveler. He also notes that fear prayer applies to any congregational prayer, including Friday and Eid. The commentary then addresses the specific division of rak'ahs in Maghrib: the imam prays two rak'ahs with the first group (since half of Maghrib is two) and one rak'ah with the second group. The reasoning is that two rak'ahs constitute half of Maghrib, so the sitting after them is prescribed, and the single rak'ah cannot be split further.

Key Terms
لاحق (lahiq): One who joined the imam from the beginning and is following him, but misses part due to the imam's action; completes without recitation.
مسبوق (masbuq): One who joined the prayer late (after the imam has begun) and catches less than a full rak'ah; recites in the remaining rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In fear prayer, the first group (lahiq) completes without recitation, while the second group (masbuq) recites.

Division of Rak'ahs in Maghrib Fear Prayer: Two and One
Commentary on the ruling for Maghrib fear prayer, explaining division of rak'ahs and status of groups.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the imam prays two rak'ahs with the first group and one with the second in Maghrib fear prayer.

Core Idea
In Maghrib fear prayer, two rak'ahs are given to the first group because that is half, and the single rak'ah cannot be split further.

The Hanafi commentary provides a specific ruling for Maghrib in the fear prayer: the imam prays two rak'ahs with the first group and one rak'ah with the second. This division is not arbitrary but is based on the nature of Maghrib prayer, which has three rak'ahs. The reasoning involves the concept of 'shar' (half) and indivisibility. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and shows how it determines the allocation of rak'ahs between the two groups.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific ruling for Maghrib
The author states: 'He prays in Maghrib with the first group two rak'ahs and with the second one rak'ah.' This is the practical application of the general principle to Maghrib.
2
Understand the reasoning based on 'shar' (half)
Two rak'ahs constitute half of Maghrib (which has three rak'ahs). Because half is a defined portion, the shar' has prescribed sitting after two rak'ahs (tashahhud). This makes two rak'ahs a natural unit.
The word 'shar' is used here to mean half; it is not the technical term from usul.
3
Recognize the indivisibility of the single rak'ah
One rak'ah cannot be divided further. Since the first group has precedence (sabaq), they are entitled to the two rak'ahs, because the single rak'ah would be insufficient for them (they need more time) and cannot be split.
The conflict is between the entitlement of the first group and the indivisibility of the third rak'ah.
4
Apply the principle of preference when conflicting
When there is a conflict between giving the first group two rak'ahs and giving the second group two rak'ahs, the first group is preferred due to their precedence (sabaq). So they get two, and the second gets one.
This is a rule of tarjih (preference).
5
Note the scope of the ruling
The author comments that they have intentionally left out the issues of the imam's mistake and related branches, indicating that the focus is on this core ruling.
This is a pedagogical choice.
